Biography of 'Abd al-Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maydani
Biographical note introducing the commentator

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the full name, lifespan, and significance of 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani as the commentator of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri.

Core Idea
Al-Maydani's al-Lubab is a key Hanafi commentary bridging Quduri's matn to later fatwa practice.

This lesson introduces you to the scholar behind one of the most widely used Hanafi commentaries. Knowing the author and his context helps you appreciate the authority and reliability of the text you are studying.

Guided Path
1
Identify the full name and nisbah
Read the passage carefully and extract the complete name, including 'Abd al-Ghani, his father's name (Talib), and the nisbahs al-Ghanimi, al-Maydani, al-Dimashqi.
These nisbahs indicate his lineage and origin.
2
Note the birth and death years
The passage gives his lifespan as 1222–1298 AH. Remember that AH dates are lunar; this corresponds to the 13th century AH.
1222 AH is approximately 1807 CE; 1298 AH is approximately 1881 CE.
3
Understand his significance
Al-Maydani's commentary 'al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri' is a standard Hanafi text used in madrasas and for fatwa reference. It explains al-Quduri's matn, a foundational Hanafi fiqh primer.
The phrase 'rahmahu Allah ta'ala' is a traditional supplication for deceased scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول
ترجمة
العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني بن طالب الغنيمي الميداني الدمشقي
۱۲۲۲ هـ ـ ۱۲۹۸هـ
رحمه الله تعالى
The First Chapter: Biography of the distinguished scholar, Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani ibn Talib al-Ghanimi al-Maydani al-Dimashqi (1222 H - 1298 H), may Allah Almighty have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This is a biographical passage (tarjama) identifying the author of the commentary we are studying. 'Abd al-Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maydani al-Dimashqi was a Hanafi jurist and scholar from Damascus. He was born in 1222 AH and died in 1298 AH. His commentary 'al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri' is one of the most widely used explanations of al-Quduri's matn in the Hanafi madhhab. The phrase 'rahmahu Allah ta'ala' is a supplication for mercy, commonly written after the names of deceased scholars.

Key Terms
ترجمة (tarjama): Biographical notice or account of a person's life
العلامة (al-'allamah): Title meaning 'the highly learned scholar', used for outstanding scholars

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the death year of 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani?
A) 1222 AH
B) 1298 AH
C) 1300 AH
D) 1220 AH

Key Takeaway
The author of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri is 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani (1222-1298 AH), a key Hanafi commentator.

Biography of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani
Biographical excerpt introducing the author's name, lineage, and a variant nickname

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the full name and lineage of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani and identify the alternative nickname mentioned in the footnote.

Core Idea
Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani: a Hanafi scholar from Damascus, also known as Ibn Khalil Basha.

Knowing the author's full name and any alternative names is essential for verifying manuscripts and chains of transmission. This lesson introduces the author of al-Lubab, a key Hanafi fiqh text, and clarifies a lesser-known nickname.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's full name
From the first paragraph, extract the complete name: Abdul Ghani bin Talib bin Hamada bin Ibrahim bin Sulayman al-Ghanimi.
The name is given in hierarchical format (son of…).
2
Identify the nisba (attribution) and its meaning
The nisba 'al-Maidani' links him to the al-Maidan neighborhood in Damascus.
This geographical nisba is the most famous identifier for this author.
3
Find the alternative nickname in the footnote
Read the footnote (1) which quotes al-Kattani and al-Fasi; both mention that al-Maidani was also known as 'Ibn Khalil Basha'.
This nickname appears only in these two sources according to the editor.
4
Understand the significance of the variant
Knowing the alternative name helps avoid confusion in manuscript attribution and reinforces the need for multiple sources in biography.

Chapter One: Biography of the scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani
First Section
The scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maidani
25
First Requirement: His name and lineage:
Abdul Ghani bin Talib bin Hamada bin Ibrahim bin Sulayman al-Ghanimi, famously known as al-Maidani (1), attributed to the well-known neighborhood – still existing – in southern Damascus, the al-Maidan neighborhood where his noble family resides.
(1) The scholar Sayyid Ja'far bin Idris al-Kattani (1246 AH – 1323 AH) mentioned in his Fihrist Mashayikhih (p. 216, Dar Ibn Hazm, Beirut, 1425 AH), when mentioning his chain to Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani via his teacher Sheikh Ali bin Zahir al-Witri al-Madani: 'al-Shifa' by al-Qadi 'Iyad twice in Medina from Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani, when he was there in the year 1280 AH, he said: '... al-Maidani known as Ibn Khalil Basha.' End quote.
And this was also mentioned by the scholar Sheikh Abdul Hafiz bin Muhammad al-Tahir al-Fasi, who died in 1383 AH, in his Mu'jam Shuyukhih, titled Riyad al-Jannah or al-Mutrib al-Mudhish, p. 227, when he mentioned Sheikh al-Witri and counted al-Maidani among his teachers, and said: 'Known as Ibn Khalil Basha.' End quote.
I say: I have not seen anyone else mention this about al-Maidani, and the honorable teacher Umar Nashuqati al-Dimashqi guided me to this benefit; may Allah reward him well.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction from the commentary (sharh) of al-Lubab on al-Quduri. It provides the full name and lineage of the author, Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. His name is Abdul Ghani bin Talib bin Hamada bin Ibrahim bin Sulayman al-Ghanimi, and he is famously known as al-Maidani, a nisba to the al-Maidan neighborhood in southern Damascus where his family lived. The passage also includes a footnote referencing two later scholars, al-Kattani and al-Fasi, who mention that al-Maidani was also known as 'Ibn Khalil Basha'. The editor notes that he has not found this nickname elsewhere except in these two sources.

Key Terms
الميداني (al-Maidani): A nisba (attribution) to the al-Maidan neighborhood in Damascus; the author's well-known epithet.
الغنيمي (al-Ghanimi): A family name; part of the author's lineage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Ibn Khalil Basha
C) Ibn Talib
D) al-Ghanimi

Key Takeaway
The author of al-Lubab is Abdul Ghani al-Maidani, also known as Ibn Khalil Basha, a Hanafi scholar from Damascus.

The Noble Lineage and Early Life of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani
Introducing the author's life, family, and early education

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key biographical facts of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani's birth, family background, and early education, and explain how his upbringing contributed to his scholarly authority.

Core Idea
A scholar's noble lineage and early discipline in Quran memorization lay the groundwork for a lifetime of learning.

This lesson introduces you to the author of our textbook, Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. Understanding his background—his family, his birth, and his early training—helps you appreciate the scholarly tradition he represents and the authority of his work. While this is not a legal ruling, it reminds us that every fatwa and every commentary comes from a human being shaped by a particular time, place, and education.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his lineage
From the first paragraph, note his full name (Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Ghunaymi al-Maidani) and his family's claimed descent from the Ansar tribe. This establishes his noble heritage.
The Ansar are the helpers of Madinah; claiming such lineage is common among scholars to indicate honour.
2
Extract the birth and death dates
Find the exact Hijri and Gregorian years of his birth (1222 AH / 1807 CE) and death (1298 AH / 1881 CE). Calculate his age: 76 years.
These dates place him in the 13th Islamic century, a period of rich Hanafi scholarship.
3
Describe his early upbringing
Read the second section about his upbringing: his father's special care, religious environment, and early Quran memorization at the hands of a teacher and later in a maktab (school).
This pattern reflects traditional Islamic education: home nurture, then tutor, then formal school.
4
Identify his teachers and scope of study
From the third section, note that he studied under senior scholars of Damascus, later from Hijaz, Egypt, and Palestine. He obtained ijazat (licenses) in various disciplines.
This breadth of teachers reflects the interconnected scholarly networks of the 19th century.
5
Connect to his scholarly authority
Reflect on how his serious pursuit of knowledge, praise from teachers, and extensive reading lend weight to his commentary on al-Quduri.
The passage says his teachers 'loved him' and 'praised him abundantly'—this builds trust in the reliability of his work.

Chapter One: Biography of the eminent scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. It is mentioned that his noble family had great importance in the al-Maidan district, and that they descend from the tribe of Aws al-Ansari, and Allah knows best. Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Ghunaymi al-Maidani was born in Damascus in the year 1222 AH, corresponding to 1807 CE, and he died, may Allah have mercy on him, in the year 1298 AH, corresponding to 1881 CE. He lived seventy-six (76) years filled with beneficial knowledge and righteous deeds, by the success of Allah Almighty. The second section: His upbringing: Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani grew up in the city of Damascus and was raised under the care of his father with a good religious upbringing, in an environment blending knowledge with righteousness. His father had special attention to him from a young age, guiding him to acquire knowledge from the scholars of his time and benefit from them. Thus, his father handed him over from a young age to a teacher-tutor to memorize the Noble Quran under him, as was the custom for young children at that time. Then he sent him to the 'maktab' (school) under the righteous man al-Sayyid Muhammad al-Sharafa. He stayed with him learning and memorizing the Quran, along with the basics of the sciences, until the year 1233 AH, when he reached the age of eleven. Thus, al-Maidani had a lofty status among his teachers and professors from whom he received knowledge at various stages, due to his seriousness and diligence in acquiring knowledge, and due to his religiosity, character, and righteousness. They loved him, took great care of him, granted him permission (ijazah) with their pens and tongues, and praised him abundantly, as you will find shortly when mentioning his teachers. The third section: His pursuit of knowledge, mention of his teachers, and what he studied under them: Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani sought sacred religious knowledge with all seriousness and diligence, and he acquired knowledge from the senior scholars of Damascus in his time. He also later acquired knowledge from scholars of the Hijaz in Makkah al-Mukarramah and Madinah al-Munawwarah during his visits to the Two Holy Sanctuaries for Hajj and Umrah. He also obtained permission (ijazah) from some scholars of Egypt and Palestine. The eminent scholar Sheikh Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Hadrawi al-Makki al-Hashimi (d. 1327 AH) has expanded in mentioning his teachers and what he studied with each of them from the many books of knowledge, which is remarkable, but it is by Allah's grace and help. This was in various disciplines: in theology ('ilm al-tawhid), in hadith...
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This is a biographical passage from 'Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri' by Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. The author is introducing himself, providing a brief biography. He mentions his noble lineage from the Ansar tribe, his birth in Damascus in 1222 AH, and his death in 1298 AH at the age of 76. He describes his upbringing under his father's care, his early Quran memorization, and his studies with scholars. The passage highlights his diligence and the esteem in which his teachers held him, granting him ijazas. It also notes that he studied under scholars from Damascus, the Hijaz, Egypt, and Palestine. The passage is purely biographical, setting the context for the author's scholarly authority.

Key Terms
العلامة (al-Allamah): A title meaning 'the highly learned scholar', used for a scholar of exceptional erudition.
المكتب (al-maktab): A traditional elementary school where children learned Quran and basics of reading and writing.
الإجازة (al-ijazah): A formal license or permission to transmit knowledge or teach a specific text or subject.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani's rigorous early education, respected teachers, and extensive travels for knowledge establish the scholarly foundation behind his commentary on al-Quduri.

Life of the Author

The Role of Scholarly Biography in Hanafi Fiqh Transmission
Biographical account with emphasis on educational lineage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why biographical accounts of scholars are essential for establishing the authority of a fiqh text in the Hanafi tradition and identify key elements of a scholar's tarjamah.

Core Idea
A scholar's biography establishes the reliability of his knowledge: without a verified teacher-student chain, a fiqh text lacks authority.

This passage from the introduction of al-Lubab provides a detailed biography of its author, Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. While it may seem like mere historical background, in the Hanafi tradition, the tarjamah (biography) of a scholar serves as a critical verification of his credentials. It documents his teachers, the texts he studied, and the ijazat he received, thus authenticating the chain of transmission (sanad). This lesson explores why such biographical information is not optional but essential for a fiqh commentary's authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of a tarjamah
In the Hanafi tradition, a scholar's biography establishes his credibility and the trustworthiness of his knowledge. The passage shows al-Maidani's serious pursuit of knowledge and the respect he earned.
2
Locate the teacher-student chain
The passage names Sheikh Omar al-Mujtahid as al-Maidani's first teacher, along with the texts studied, forming an unbroken chain back to earlier authorities.
Chain: al-Maidani → Sheikh Omar al-Mujtahid → ...
3
Analyze the content of study
Note the specific texts: Muqaddimat Abi al-Layth, Nur al-Idah, Imdad al-Fattah, al-Durr. These are core Hanafi works, indicating depth of training.
Muqaddimat Abi al-Layth is an early Hanafi primer.
4
Understand the role of ijazah
The passage mentions that al-Maidani was authorized (ajazuhu) by his teachers, which is a formal permission to transmit and teach the texts.
Ijazah is a key element in scholarly transmission.
5
Connect to fiqh authority
This chain gives weight to al-Maidani's commentary, al-Lubab, on al-Quduri's text. The biography assures readers that the author is qualified.

يقتضيها المقام. قال العلامة الحضراوي رحمه الله في ترجمته للميداني: ١- ثم أرسله والده إلى خدمة العالم الفاضل، الجهبذ الكامل، شيخ الأفاضل ، المرحوم الشيخ عمر المجتهد ابن الشيخ أحمد المجتهد الدمشقي الميداني، المولود سنة ١١٦٩هـ، والمتوفى سنة ١٢٥٤هـ (١) ، رحمه الله تعالى.
(۱)
فقرأ عليه مقدمة أبي الليث ونور الإيضاح»، وشرحه إمداد الفتاح، وكان عنده جماعة يقرؤون عليه «الدر»، فلما ختم «الإمداد»، أحضره مع الجماعة من النصف الثاني إلى الأخير، وبدأه
ثانياً إلى أن أكمله.
(۱) له ترجمة في حلية البشر ١١٣٢/٢.
Chapter One: Biography of the distinguished scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. (1) 27 ... and three hundred and thirty [actually thirty-three? unclear] and one thousand, and he had reached the age of eleven. Thus al-Maidani had a prestigious station with his teachers and professors from whom he received at various stages, due to his seriousness and diligence in acquiring knowledge, and due to his religion, character, and righteousness, so they loved him, gave him extreme care, authorized him with their pens and tongues, and praised him greatly, as you will soon find when mentioning his teachers. Section Three: His seeking of knowledge, mention of his teachers, and what he read with them: Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani sought noble sacred knowledge with all seriousness and diligence (2), and acquired sciences from the great scholars of Damascus in his time, and later from the scholars of Hijaz in Mecca and Medina, during his visits to the Two Holy Sanctuaries for pilgrimage and umrah, and also obtained authorization from some scholars of Egypt and Palestine. The distinguished scholar Sheikh Ahmad bin Muhammad al-Hadrawi (3) al-Makki al-Hashimi (d. 1327 AH) elaborated in mentioning his teachers, and mentioned what he read with each of them from many books of knowledge, which is amazing, but it is Allah's grace and help, in various disciplines: theology, hadith, Shamail and Sirah, Hanafi fiqh and its principles, inheritance law, ethics and self-purification, Arabic and its sciences, and other sciences, as Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani himself informed. They used to meet in Mecca during the seasons and in Damascus when al-Hadrawi traveled there. I will mention below the names of his teachers with whom he read, in the order mentioned by al-Hadrawi, who arranged them according to the years he took knowledge from them in general, and I add to what al-Hadrawi said some benefits and clarifications required by the context. Al-Hadrawi said in his biography of al-Maidani: 1- Then his father sent him to serve the virtuous scholar, the perfect genius, the sheikh of the eminent, the late Sheikh Omar al-Mujtahid bin Sheikh Ahmad al-Mujtahid al-Dimashqi al-Maidani, born 1169 AH, died 1254 AH (1), may Allah have mercy on him. He read with him: Muqaddimat Abi al-Layth and Nur al-Idah, and its commentary Imdad al-Fattah. He had a group reading al-Durr with him. When he finished al-Imdad, he brought him with the group from the second half to the end, and he began it again until he completed it.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account from the introduction of the book, where the author (or compiler) provides a detailed biography of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. The passage describes his virtuous character and high standing among his teachers, who loved him for his diligence, religiousness, and good character. They granted him written and oral authorizations (ijazat) and praised him. It then moves to the third section, detailing his pursuit of knowledge: he studied under major scholars of Damascus and later scholars of the Hijaz, and also received ijazat from scholars of Egypt and Palestine. The author relies on the work of Sheikh Ahmad al-Hadrawi, who extensively listed al-Maidani's teachers and the books he studied with each. The passage begins listing the first teacher: Sheikh Omar al-Mujtahid al-Maidani. With him, al-Maidani studied 'Muqaddimat Abi al-Layth' (a Hanafi fiqh text) and 'Nur al-Idah' (a famous Hanafi text by al-Shurunbulali) along with its commentary 'Imdad al-Fattah'. Additionally, he participated in a group study of 'al-Durr' (likely al-Durr al-Mukhtar, a later Hanafi manual) after completing 'al-Imdad'. This biography establishes the scholarly pedigree of the author, which is important for understanding the authority behind the commentary (al-Lubab) on al-Quduri's text.

Key Terms
الجهبذ (al-jahbadh): A term meaning 'expert', 'genius', or 'thoroughly knowledgeable scholar' used as a title for Sheikh Omar.
المجتهد (al-mujtahid): A scholar qualified to perform ijtihad, independent legal reasoning; used as a title for Sheikh Omar and his father.
الإجازة (al-ijazah): An authorization or license to transmit knowledge or teach a particular book, granted by a teacher to a student.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) To provide historical context only

Key Takeaway
A scholar's tarjamah is the anchor of his authority; without it, his fiqh work is adrift.

The Biography of al-Maidani: Tracing the Hanafi Chain of Transmission
Biographical account of al-Maidani's studies with his first teacher

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key texts studied in the traditional Hanafi curriculum and explain how biographical accounts (tarajim) establish the authority of a scholar.

Core Idea
A scholar's biography (tarjama) is a chain of transmission that validates the fiqh he teaches.

This passage from the commentary on al-Quduri introduces us to the life of the commentator himself, Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. Biographical sections like this are not mere filler; they serve to establish the scholarly lineage (isnad) through which the fiqh knowledge has been passed down. By examining what he studied and with whom, we gain insight into the rigour of Hanafi learning and the importance of personal transmission (talaqqi).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Teacher
Find the full name and lifespan of al-Maidani's first teacher. This anchors the chain in a specific historical and geographical context.
The teacher is Sheikh Umar al-Mujtahid al-Maidani (1169-1254 AH).
2
Map the Curriculum
List the texts al-Maidani studied with his first teacher. Categorize them by subject (fiqh, Arabic, inheritance, hadith, etc.).
Fiqh: Nur al-Idah, Imdad al-Fattah; Arabic: al-Ajurrumiyya, al-Alfiyya; Inheritance: al-Rahbiyya, al-Sirajiyya; Hadith: al-Shama'il.
3
Understand the Ijaza
Explain what an ijaza is and why the teacher's granting of it is significant in the transmission of knowledge.
Ijaza is a permission to transmit and teach the texts, linking the student to the teacher's own chain back to the author.
4
Connect to the Present
Reflect on why a modern student of fiqh should care about these biographical details. How does this chain affect the reliability of the texts we study today?
Knowing the chain strengthens trust and provides a direct link to the early authorities.

Chapter One: Biography of Allama Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. The noble, the Shamail and Sirah, and in Hanafi jurisprudence and its principles, and the obligatory shares, and in ethics and self-purification and Arabic and its sciences, and other sciences, as Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani himself informed. Commentary
This passage is a biographical expansion from the commentary (sharh) on al-Quduri. It provides an account of the life and education of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani, the commentator. The author begins by outlining al-Maidani's breadth of knowledge in various fields including Hanafi fiqh, usul, faraid, ethics, Arabic, and more. He then explains his method of listing teachers in the order provided by al-Hadrawi, who wrote a biography of al-Maidani. The first teacher mentioned is Sheikh Umar al-Mujtahid al-Maidani, a distinguished scholar. Al-Maidani studied a wide range of texts with him, including introductory Hanafi works (Nur al-Idah, Imdad al-Fattah), Arabic grammar (al-Ajurrumiyya, al-Alfiyya), logic (al-Sanusiyya), inheritance jurisprudence (al-Rahbiyya, al-Sirajiyya), hadith (al-Shama'il), and others. Sheikh Umar also granted him a general ijaza (permission to teach and transmit). The passage also notes that al-Maidani compiled a thabat (a list of his teachers and works) for another teacher, al-Kuzbari, which is listed among his works.

Key Terms
نور الإيضاح (Nur al-Idah): A Hanafi fiqh text by Imam al-Shurunbulali, a basic primer for beginners.
إمداد الفتاح (Imdad al-Fattah): A commentary by al-Shurunbulali on his own Nur al-Idah.
إجازة (ijaza): A certificate of permission to transmit or teach certain texts.

Al-Maidani's Study Under Ibn Abidin: A Model of Scholarly Succession
Biographical note on al-Maidani's study with Ibn Abidin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the duration and significance of al-Maidani's study under Ibn Abidin and identify the key works associated with Ibn Abidin.

Core Idea
A scholar's pedigree is forged through sustained study under a master.

This passage introduces us to the second great teacher of Abdul Ghani al-Maidani: the renowned Hanafi jurist Muhammad Amin Ibn Abidin. Ibn Abidin's commentary Radd al-Muhtar is the most authoritative late Hanafi reference. Understanding the teacher-student relationship helps us appreciate how Hanafi knowledge was transmitted and how al-Maidani became a leading Hanafi scholar of his time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the teacher and his work
Read the passage and note the name of the teacher (Ibn Abidin) and his famous work Radd al-Muhtar. Recognize that this work is a commentary on al-Durr al-Mukhtar.
Radd al-Muhtar is a key text for Hanafi fatwa.
2
Determine the duration and nature of the study
The passage says al-Maidani remained in Ibn Abidin's service from 1244 AH until Ibn Abidin's death in 1252 AH, a period of eight years. The phrase 'لازمه ملازمة تامة' indicates constant, full-time companionship.
3
Note the ages at the time
Al-Maidani was 24, Ibn Abidin 46. This is the prime age for serious scholarly training.
4
Recognize al-Maidani's rank among Ibn Abidin's students
The passage states he was 'one of the most distinguished four students' – this shows his high standing and the depth of his learning.

٢- وفي حياته أيضاً حضر عند الشيخ الفاضل سيدي السيد محمد أمين عابدين بن عمر صاحب الحاشية المشهورة: رد المحتار على الدر المختار، المولود سنة ١١٩٨هـ، والمتوفي سنة ١٢٥٢هـ، فبقي في خدمته من سنة أربع وأربعين إلى أن توفي ابن عابدين رحمه الله. وهكذا حضر عند العلامة ابن عابدين ولازمه ملازمة تامة ثماني سنين، وكانت سن الميداني قد بلغت (٢٤) سنة، وابن عابدين قد بلغ من العمر (٤٦) سنة، سن الكمال والنضج العلمي. وكان الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني أحد أخص أربعة تلاميذ لابن عابدين.

He remained in his service from the year forty-four until Ibn Abidin died, may Allah have mercy on him. The age of al-Maidani had reached 24 years, and Ibn Abidin had reached 46 years, the age of perfection and scientific maturity. And Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani was one of the most distinguished four students of Ibn Abidin.

Commentary
This passage continues the biography of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani by introducing his second teacher, the renowned Hanafi jurist Muhammad Amin Ibn Abidin, author of Radd al-Muhtar, the most authoritative commentary on al-Durr al-Mukhtar. Al-Maidani studied under Ibn Abidin from the year 1244 AH until Ibn Abidin's death in 1252 AH, a period of eight years. This was a time when al-Maidani was 24 years old and Ibn Abidin was 46, a prime age for both teaching and learning. Al-Maidani became one of Ibn Abidin's four most special students, highlighting his high standing and the depth of his study under this great mujtahid.

Key Terms
رد المحتار (Radd al-Muhtar): A famous Hanafi fiqh commentary by Ibn Abidin on al-Durr al-Mukhtar.
الدر المختار (al-Durr al-Mukhtar): A Hanafi fiqh text by al-Haskafi, commented upon by Ibn Abidin.
ملازمة تامة (mulazama tamma): Constant, full-time companionship with a teacher for study.

The Scholarly Training of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani
Biography of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani: teachers and studies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key teachers of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani, describe the subjects he studied under each, and explain the significance of ijazah in the transmission of knowledge.

Core Idea
A scholar's training requires multiple teachers: each contributes a distinct discipline to form a complete faqih.

This biographical passage offers a window into the traditional method of acquiring Islamic knowledge. By examining the teachers and subjects of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani, we see how a student systematically masters Arabic, usul, and fiqh under different experts. The passage also highlights the role of ijazah (formal permission) and the close teacher-student relationship that defined pre-modern education.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary teachers
Read the passage and list the two main teachers mentioned: the early teacher (likely al-Kazabari) and the later master Ibn Abidin. Also note the mention of Sheikh Abd al-Rahman al-Kazabari al-Shafi'i.
The first teacher's full name is not given in this excerpt; the passage refers to him as 'his teacher' (shaykhuh).
2
List the subjects studied under each teacher
Under the first teacher, al-Maidani studied Arabic grammar, logic, inheritance law (al-Rahbiyyah, al-Sirajiyyah), and hadith (al-Shama'il). Under Ibn Abidin, he focused on Hanafi fiqh (al-Durr, al-Hidayah), usul al-fiqh, and heard Sahih al-Bukhari.
The subjects reflect a comprehensive curriculum: from language tools to core fiqh texts.
3
Understand ijazah and thabt
Both teachers granted al-Maidani ijazah (permission to teach). He also compiled a thabt (register) for his first teacher, showing the formal recording of chains of transmission.
Ijazah was both oral and written; it certified the student's mastery and authorized him to transmit the texts.
4
Analyze the depth of study under Ibn Abidin
Al-Maidani spent eight years closely studying with Ibn Abidin, from age 24 to 32. He went through major Hanafi works and was considered one of the four closest students.
This long-term immersion is a hallmark of traditional fiqh training.
5
Consider the significance of multiple teachers
Al-Maidani studied under different specialists: a Shafi'i hadith scholar (al-Kazabari al-Shafi'i) and Hanafi jurist (Ibn Abidin). This diversified his knowledge and strengthened his expertise.
Cross-madhhab study was common; it enriched the scholar's understanding.

Chapter One: Biography of the distinguished scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani

During that time he attended a good portion of Arabic studies with him (his teacher al-Kazabari), reading al-Ajrumiyyah and its commentary by Sheikh Khalid al-Azhari, al-Azhariyyah, Qawa'id al-I'rab, Sharh al-Qatr by the author, and he memorized al-Alfiyyah. He also attended with him al-Sanusiyyah and its commentary by al-Lahdudi, Sharh al-Rahbiyyah, Sharh al-Sirajiyyah, al-Sakhawiyyah, and al-Shama'il by al-Tirmidhi, and others.

He (al-Kazabari) gave him ijazah (permission to teach) for everything that was permissible for him, orally and in writing.

Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani prepared a thabt (biographical register) for his teacher al-Kazabari, which will be mentioned in his works.

2- Also during his lifetime, he attended with the virtuous master, al-Sayyid Muhammad Amin Abidin ibn Umar, the author of the famous hashiah 'Radd al-Muhtar ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar', born 1198 AH and died 1252 AH. He remained in his service from the year 1244 until Ibn Abidin died, may Allah have mercy on him.

Thus he attended with the scholar Ibn Abidin and associated with him closely for eight full years. Al-Maidani was then 24 years old, and Ibn Abidin had reached the age of 46, the age of perfection and scholarly maturity.

Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani was one of the four closest students of Ibn Abidin. Ibn Abidin issued ijazah to all four together in a poem that will be mentioned in the praises of scholars upon Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani, Allah willing.

* Al-Maidani would read with Ibn Abidin on al-Durr, along with Radd al-Muhtar, and on al-Hidayah and its commentary al-Inayah, reaching the end of the Book of Sales in eight years.

During that time he read with him a portion in Arabic language and a portion in Usul al-Fiqh, and attended with him his Fatawa, al-Tanqih, and some of his epistles, and heard Sahih al-Bukhari in its entirety from him, and the musalsalat of Ibn 'Aqilah, with their chains of transmission as much as possible.

He (Ibn Abidin) gave him ijazah for everything permissible for him more than once, orally and in writing.

Also among those who attended with him and sought blessing by sitting before him was the Imam, the ocean of knowledge, the hadith scholar of Damascus, the faqih, muhaddith, athari, Sheikh Abd al-Rahman ibn Muhammad al-Kazabari al-Shafi'i, born 1184 AH and died in Makkah in 1262 AH. He read Sahih al-Bukhari with him in the place of the muhaddithin under the Dome of the Eagle in the Umayyad Mosque in Damascus for fifty-two years. May Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani, focusing on his education and scholarly connections. It describes his studies under two major teachers: the first is al-Kazabari (likely referring to his early teacher, possibly from the Kazabari family), and the second is the famous Hanafi jurist Ibn Abidin. Under al-Kazabari, he studied Arabic grammar, logic (al-Sanusiyyah), inheritance law (al-Rahbiyyah, al-Sirajiyyah), hadith (al-Shama'il), and received a general ijazah. He compiled a thabt (scholarly register) for his teacher. Under Ibn Abidin, he studied the major Hanafi texts: al-Durr al-Mukhtar with its supercommentary Radd al-Muhtar, al-Hidayah with al-Inayah, and also studied Arabic, usul al-fiqh, and heard Sahih al-Bukhari. Ibn Abidin gave him ijazah multiple times. Al-Maidani is noted as one of Ibn Abidin's four closest students. The passage also mentions that al-Kazabari (the second, actually a different person, Sheikh Abd al-Rahman al-Kazabari al-Shafi'i) read Sahih al-Bukhari with him for many years. This shows al-Maidani's high standing among the scholars of Damascus and his wide-ranging education.

Key Terms
إجازة (ijāzah): In this text, it refers to a formal permission granted by a teacher to a student, authorizing him to transmit certain texts or teach them. The teacher gave it both orally and in writing.
ثبت (thabt): A biographical register or list of works and chains of transmission of a teacher, often compiled by a student. Here, al-Maidani compiled a thabt for his teacher al-Kazabari.
حضر عنده (haḍara ʿindahu): To attend or study with a teacher. It implies regular attendance and learning from the teacher, not necessarily formal enrollment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which major Hanafi work did al-Maidani study under Ibn Abidin that is explicitly mentioned in the passage?
A) Al-Hidayah
B) Al-Mabsut
C) Al-Quduri
D) Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair

Key Takeaway
Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani's scholarly formation exemplifies the traditional path: a broad foundation under one master followed by deep specialization in Hanafi fiqh under another, supplemented by cross-madhhab hadith study.

The Scholarly Training of Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani: A Model of Hanafi Hadith Mastery
Biographical account of al-Maydani's teachers and studies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key teachers of Shaykh al-Maydani and explain the significance of ijazah in the transmission of Hanafi knowledge.

Core Idea
A scholar's authority rests on authentic chains of transmission—ijazah bridges generations.

This lesson presents the biography of Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, the author of al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri. By examining his teachers and the books he studied, we gain insight into the traditional Hanafi learning curriculum and the importance of scholarly licenses (ijazah). This passage is not a fiqh ruling but a window into how authoritative knowledge is passed down from one generation to the next.

Guided Path
1
Identify the teachers
List the names of al-Maydani's teachers mentioned in the passage: Ibn 'Abidin, al-Kuzbari, and al-Halabi. Note their specialties—fiqh for Ibn 'Abidin, hadith for al-Kuzbari, and both for al-Halabi.
Each teacher contributed a different dimension to al-Maydani's training.
2
Analyze the curriculum
Observe the texts studied: fiqh works like al-Durr al-Mukhtar and al-Hidayah under Ibn 'Abidin; hadith collections like Sahih al-Bukhari and Muwatta Malik under al-Kuzbari. Also note Arabic and usul studies.
This shows the breadth expected of a Hanafi scholar.
3
Understand ijazah
Al-Maydani received multiple ijazahs from his teachers. Understand that ijazah is a certification of competence and permission to transmit the teacher's works, forming a chain back to the original authors.
Ijazah is a hallmark of traditional Islamic education.
4
Appreciate breadth
Notice that al-Maydani studied both fiqh and hadith, as well as auxiliary sciences. This reflects the Hanafi ideal of a scholar being well-rounded, not merely a jurist.
This breadth enhances the reliability of his later commentary.
5
Connect to the present
Reflect on how the ijazah system continues to operate in traditional seminaries today, ensuring that Hanafi knowledge is transmitted with an authenticated chain.
Understanding this helps appreciate the authority of classical texts.

Chapter One: Biography of the eminent scholar Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani
... [full translation of the Arabic text as provided]

Commentary
This is a biographical section from the front matter of the book, detailing the scholarly life of Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, the author of this commentary. It describes his primary teachers: first, Ibn 'Abidin (Muhammad Amin ibn 'Umar), the renowned Hanafi jurist, under whom he studied al-Durr al-Mukhtar with its gloss Radd al-Muhtar, al-Hidayah with al-'Inayah, and other works. He also received an ijazah (scholarly license) from Ibn 'Abidin for all that he was permitted to transmit. Second, he studied under Shaykh 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Muhammad al-Kuzbari al-Shafi'i, a prominent hadith scholar in Damascus, reading with him the six major hadith collections (except most of Sahih Muslim), the Muwatta of Imam Malik, al-Adab al-Mufrad, and many other books. Al-Maydani also attended the lessons of Shaykh Sa'id al-Halabi after Ibn 'Abidin's death. The passage emphasizes al-Maydani's rigorous scholarly training and his connection to authoritative chains of transmission.

Key Terms
الإجازة (al-ijāzah): A scholarly license given by a teacher to a student, permitting the student to transmit the teacher's works or teachings.

Scholarly Chains and Ijazah in the Hanafi Tradition
Biographical account of the author's scholarly training and teachers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the role of isnad (chain of transmission) and ijazah in establishing a Hanafi scholar's authority, using al-Maydani's biography as a case study.

Core Idea
A scholar’s authority is built through chains of transmission (isnad) and ijazah from multiple teachers.

This passage from al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri is not fiqh itself, but a biographical credential (tarjama) that establishes the author's right to teach and comment on the matn. Understanding how scholars like al-Maydani accumulated knowledge through direct study with masters and received formal permission (ijazah) reveals the living chain that preserves Hanafi orthodoxy. Let us walk through the key elements of this scholarly pedigree.

Guided Path
1
Identify the teachers
List the shaykhs mentioned with whom al-Maydani studied directly. Note their full names and any details given.
At least four teachers are named: al-Kuzbari, Ibn 'Abidin, al-Halabi, al-'Attar, and al-'Ajluni.
2
Catalog the texts studied
For each teacher, note which texts or genres al-Maydani studied. This shows the breadth of his training.
Texts range from hadith (Sahih al-Bukhari, Muwatta) to fiqh (al-Quduri), usul (al-Manar), tasawwuf (al-Shifa', 'Awarif), etc.
3
Understand the concept of ijazah
Highlight where al-Maydani received ijazah from each teacher. Ijazah is a formal permission to transmit knowledge.
The phrase 'ajazahu bi-lisani wa qalamihi' (orally and in writing) appears multiple times.
4
Recognize the chain of transmission
Notice how al-Maydani connects to earlier authorities through his teachers. For example, he studied with Ibn 'Abidin, who studied with al-Kuzbari, etc.
The author even notes that al-Maydani 'met' Ibn 'Abidin by sharing a teacher (al-Kuzbari).
5
Assess the significance for the commentary
Reflect on why the author included this biography at the beginning of his commentary. It establishes his credibility to interpret al-Quduri.
In Hanafi tradition, a commentator must trace his knowledge back through reliable chains.

Chapter One: Biography of the Scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani

Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani attended with him [al-Kuzbari] all six books [of Hadith] except Sahih Muslim, of which he missed a small portion.
He also read with him Muwatta' of Imam Malik, al-Adab al-Mufrad of al-Bukhari, al-Jam' bayn al-Sahihayn of al-Saghani, Musalsalat Ibn 'Uqayla in their serial chain, Musalsalat Ibn al-Tayyib, al-Arba'in Hadithan of Sheikh Isma'il al-'Ajluni from the beginnings of forty books, al-Shifa' al-Sharif of Qadi 'Iyad, Risalah of Imam al-Qushayri with its commentary by Shaykh al-Islam in some places, 'Awarif al-Ma'arif of al-Suhrawardi, and other books and treatises.
He granted him ijazah more than once, orally and in writing, may Allah have mercy on him.
Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani met with his teacher Ibn 'Abidin in taking from this al-Kuzbari.
When the late Sheikh Muhammad Amin ibn 'Umar 'Abidin died, he turned to serve the Imam, the scholar, my master Sheikh Sa'id ibn Hasan al-Halabi by origin, born in Damascus, the Hanafi jurist, the teacher of hadith scholars, the pillar of acting scholars, born in Aleppo in 1188 AH, came to Damascus in 1207 AH, settled there, and died there in 1259 AH, may Allah have mercy on him.

Sheikh al-Maydani read with him the book al-Quduri, al-Manar, and al-Tawdih, and heard from him Sahih al-Bukhari and others, and he granted him ijazah orally and in writing.
Thus al-Maydani also met with his teacher Ibn 'Abidin through Sheikh Sa'id al-Halabi, as they both took from him. He also read with the distinguished scholar, the most learned of scholars, the foremost of them, Hamid ibn Ahmad ibn 'Ubayd al-'Attar al-Shafi'i al-Dimashqi, born in 1186 AH and died in 1262 AH, may Allah have mercy on him.
He read with him Musalsalat Ibn 'Uqayla, al-Arba'in al-'Ajluniyya, a large portion of Sharh al-Fusus of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Nabulsi (d. 1143 AH), and other works, and he also granted him ijazah for what he was permitted, orally and in writing. He also read with the distinguished scholar, the proof, the authoritative scholar, the young Shafi'i, Ahmad Baybars al-'Ajluni, son of Sheikh Isma'il al-'Ajluni al-Dimashqi, who died in 1247 AH, may Allah have mercy on him, and he granted him ijazah for what he was permitted.
Among those who also granted him ijazah is the distinguished scholar, the great scholar, Abd Allah ibn Mustafa...
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section (tarjama) detailing the scholarly training of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, the author of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. It describes his studies with several prominent teachers in Damascus, focusing on the chain of transmission (isnad) and the specific texts he read with each. The passage emphasizes the continuity of the Hanafi tradition by showing how al-Maydani studied with multiple shaykhs, including the famous Hanafi jurist Ibn 'Abidin (d. 1252 AH) and al-Kuzbari, and how he received written and oral ijazat (permissions to teach and transmit). Notably, al-Maydani studied al-Quduri (the matn of Hanafi fiqh), al-Manar (a work of usul), and al-Tawdih (a commentary). This biography serves as a credential for the author, establishing his authority as a reliable transmitter of Hanafi knowledge. The mention of his teachers 'Ibn 'Abidin and al-Halabi' shows his direct connection to the major Hanafi scholars of his time. The passage also notes that al-Maydani studied a wide range of texts beyond fiqh, including hadith collections (e.g., the six books, Sahih al-Bukhari, Muwatta'), spiritual works (e.g., al-Shifa', 'Awarif al-Ma'arif), and even Shafi'i sources with a Shafi'i teacher, indicating the breadth of his learning. The biographical information is typical for a scholarly work, establishing the author's credentials (ijazah and chain) to lend weight to his commentary.

Key Terms
إجازة (ijāzah): A formal permission granted by a scholar to a student to transmit specific texts or to teach, orally or in writing.
مسلسلات (musalsalāt): Hadiths or chains of transmission that have a serial link, where each narrator uses a specific phrase or action, emphasizing the continuity of the chain.
القدوري (al-Qudūrī): The Mukhtasar of al-Quduri, a foundational text of Hanafi fiqh that serves as the matn being commented upon in this book.

Key Terms from Source Passage

What is the primary purpose of including a detailed biography (like al-Maydani's) at the beginning of a sharh (commentary)?
A) To make the book longer.

Key Takeaway
The biography of al-Maydani demonstrates that a Hanafi scholar's authority is derived from direct, verified transmission through a chain of qualified teachers, preserved by ijazah.

The Scholarly Network of Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani
Biographical introduction listing teachers and ijazahs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the teachers and ijazah-grantors of Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani and explain the significance of ijazah in establishing scholarly authority in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
A scholar's authority is traced through his teachers and their ijazah — the living chain of transmission.

This lesson introduces the scholarly credentials of the author of 'Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri', Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani. The passage lists his key teachers and those who granted him ijazah, demonstrating his connection to major centers of learning and multiple madhhabs. Understanding this network is essential for appreciating the reliability of his transmissions and the breadth of his training.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary teacher and his role
Locate the first teacher mentioned: Shaykh Sa'id al-Halabi. Note what al-Maidani studied with him and how this links him to Ibn Abidin.
Studying under a teacher who also taught Ibn Abidin strengthens the chain.
2
List the other teachers and their specialties
Scan the passage for each teacher's name, their madhhab (if indicated), and what they taught. Examples include Hamid al-Attar (Shafi'i), Ahmad Baybars al-Ajluni (Shafi'i), and others.
Notice the diversity of madhhabs among teachers.
3
Map the geographic spread of ijazahs
Identify the cities of the ijazah-grantors: Damascus, Madinah, Makkah, Egypt. This shows al-Maidani's recognition across the Islamic world.
Ijazahs from different regions indicate wide acceptance.
4
Explain the function of ijazah in Hanafi pedagogy
Reflect on why ijazah is mentioned. It certifies that the student has heard and is authorized to transmit specific texts, preserving the chain of learning.
Ijazah is both a permission and a certification of mastery.

الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني
وقد قرأ عليه الشيخ الميداني كتاب «القــدوري»، و«المنار»، والتوضيح، وسمع منه صحيح البخاري، وغيره، وأجازه بلسانه وقلمه. وبهذا يكون الميداني قد التقى مع شيخه ابن عابدين أيضاً بالشيخ سعيد الحلبي، حيث أخذا عنه.
وقرأ كذلك على العلامة الشيخ الفاضل، فاضل العلماء، وعالم الفضلاء، حامد بن أحمد بن عبيد العطار الشافعي الدمشقي، المولود سنة ١١٨٦ هـ، والمتوفى سنة ١٢٦٢هـ، رحمه الله تعالى.
قرأ عليه مسلسلات ابن عقيلة، والأربعين العجلونية، وحصةً وافرة من «شرح الفصوص» للشيخ عبد الغني النابلسي (ت ١١٤٣هـ)، وغير ذلك، وأجازه أيضاً بما يجوز له بلسانه وقلمه.
وقرأ أيضاً على الشيخ الفاضل الحجة العالم التحرير، والشافعي الصغير أحمد بيبرس العجلوني ابن الشيخ إسماعيل العجلوني الدمشقي، المتوفى سنة ١٢٤٧هـ، رحمه الله تعالى، وأجازه بما يجوز له.
وممن أجازه أيضاً الشيخ الفاضل العلامة عبد الله بن مصطفى ابن عبد الله الكردي العبد لاني المتوفى سنة ١٢٧٨هـ، رحمه الله تعالى.
وأجازه أيضاً من أهل المدينة المنورة الشيخ محمد بن أحمد العَطُّوشي المالكي.
وأجازه من أهل مكة سيدي السيد عبد الله بن محمد بن عبد الله المحجوب الميرغني الحنفي مفتي مكة المكرمة ورئيسها، المتوفى سنة ١٢٧٣هـ، رحمه الله تعالى.
وأجازه من أهل مصر شيخ الإسلام إبراهيم بن محمد الباجوري، المولود سنة ۱۱۹۸هـ، والمتوفى سنة ١٢٧٦هـ، وقيل ۱۲۷۷ هـ، رحمه الله تعالى.
وأجازه أيضاً من أهل مصر العلامة الشيخ الفاضل مصطفى السلط [؟]
Chapter One: Biography of the scholar Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani. Shaykh al-Maidani studied with him the book 'Al-Quduri', 'Al-Manar', and 'Al-Tawdih', and heard from him Sahih al-Bukhari and others, and he gave him ijazah verbally and in writing. Thus al-Maidani also met his teacher Ibn Abidin through Shaykh Sa'id al-Halabi, as they both studied under him. He also studied with the illustrious scholar, the most excellent of scholars, and the scholar of the excellent, Hamid ibn Ahmad ibn Ubayd al-Attar al-Shafi'i al-Dimashqi, born 1186 AH and died 1262 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. He studied with him the sequences of Ibn Aqila, the 'Forty Hadith of al-Ajluni', and a large portion of 'Sharh al-Fusus' by Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Nabulsi (d. 1143 AH), and other things, and he also gave him ijazah for what he was permitted, verbally and in writing. He also studied with the excellent scholar, the proof, the erudite, the minor Shafi'i, Ahmad Baybars al-Ajluni, son of Shaykh Ismail al-Ajluni al-Dimashqi, died 1247 AH, may Allah have mercy on him, and he gave him ijazah for what he was permitted. Among those who also gave him ijazah was the excellent scholar, the erudite, Abdullah ibn Mustafa ibn Abdullah al-Kurdi al-Abdalani, died 1278 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. He was also given ijazah by, from the people of Madinah, Shaykh Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Attushi al-Maliki. And he was given ijazah by, from the people of Makkah, my master Sayyid Abdullah ibn Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Mahjub al-Mirghani al-Hanafi, Mufti of Makkah and its chief, died 1273 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. And he was given ijazah by, from the people of Egypt, Shaykh al-Islam Ibrahim ibn Muhammad al-Bajuri, born 1198 AH and died 1276 AH, and it is said 1277 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. And he was also given ijazah by, from the people of Egypt, the erudite scholar, the excellent Shaykh Mustafa al-Salt [or al-Mublat?]
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section from the introduction of the book 'Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri' by Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani. It establishes the author's scholarly credentials by listing his prominent teachers and those who granted him ijazah (authorization to transmit) in various Islamic sciences. The focus is on al-Maidani's connection to major scholars from Damascus, Madinah, Makkah, and Egypt, indicating his wide network and recognition. Notably, al-Maidani studied with Shaykh Sa'id al-Halabi, who was also a teacher of Ibn Abidin, linking him to the great Hanafi jurist. Teachers like Hamid al-Attar and Ahmad Baybars al-Ajluni were prominent Shafi'i scholars, showing his exposure to multiple madhhabs. Ijazah from figures like the Maliki scholar al-Attushi, the Hanafi mufti of Makkah al-Mirghani, and the Egyptian scholar al-Bajuri (a Shafi'i but Shaykh al-Islam) further underscore his broad acceptance. The inclusion of such ijazas was a standard way of authenticating a scholar's transmission chain and pedagogical authority.

Key Terms
الإجازة (al-ijazah): Permission granted by a teacher to a student to transmit specific texts or teachings, often in writing and orally, establishing a certified chain of transmission.
شيخ (shaykh): A respected teacher or scholar, often indicating a person with authority to teach and grant ijazah.
المفتي (al-mufti): A jurist qualified to issue fatwas; here used for the mufti of Makkah al-Mirghani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Damascus
B) Madinah
C) Makkah
D) Egypt

Key Takeaway
The chain of teachers and ijazahs is essential for authenticating a scholar's authority and the reliability of their transmitted knowledge.

Understanding Ijazah and Scholarly Lineage in Hanafi Tradition
Biographical listing of ijazah-granting teachers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key teachers of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani and explain the significance of ijazah in establishing scholarly authority in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
A scholar's authority is built on the chain of ijazah from recognized teachers, ensuring authentic transmission of knowledge.

This passage opens a classical Hanafi fiqh commentary with a biography of the author. Why? In Islamic scholarship, the credibility of a text depends on the author's credentials. This biographical section establishes that Sheikh al-Maydani received ijazah from multiple scholars across the Islamic world, demonstrating his wide learning and authentic chain to earlier authorities. Understanding this context is essential before diving into the fiqh rulings themselves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of the biography
Explain why a fiqh text often begins with the author's biography. This establishes the authenticity and reliability of the transmission of the text.
In the Hanafi tradition, the chain of transmission (sanad) is paramount.
2
List the teachers who granted ijazah
Extract the names and locations of the teachers mentioned. There are five: from Medina, Mecca, Egypt (two), Jaffa, and Jerusalem.
Count only those explicitly stated as granting ijazah; studying under a teacher is different.
3
Observe the geographical diversity
Note that the teachers are from different cities: Medina, Mecca, Egypt, Jaffa, Jerusalem. This shows al-Maydani's broad network.
Some teachers held official positions like Mufti of Mecca or Jerusalem.
4
Define the term 'ijazah'
Understand that ijazah is a formal permission to transmit knowledge. It is a key method of certification in Islamic scholarship.
Compare to modern academic degrees; ijazah is personal and chain-based.
5
Recognize the primary teacher
Sheikh Hasan al-Bitar is highlighted as the one he studied under and accompanied for a long time. This indicates a deeper mentorship beyond ijazah.
The passage mentions a poem written for al-Bitar, showing personal connection.

Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the first chapter of the book, which is a biography (tarjamah) of the author, Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. In the Hanafi tradition, establishing the author's scholarly lineage and chain of transmission (sanad) is of great importance. The text lists multiple scholars from different cities (Medina, Mecca, Egypt, Jaffa, Jerusalem) who granted ijazah to al-Maydani, indicating the breadth of his learning and the authenticity of his transmission. The biography also highlights his primary teacher, Sheikh Hasan al-Bitar, whom he accompanied for a long period. This biographical material is not a legal ruling but serves to establish the authority of the work that follows. The footnotes provide references to biographical dictionaries such as 'Hilyat al-Bashar' and 'Nashr al-Nur wa al-Zahr'.

Key Terms
إجازة (ijazah): Permission granted by a scholar to another to transmit or teach specific texts or knowledge.
ترجمة (tarjamah): Biography, especially of a scholar, detailing his life, teachers, and works.
مفتي (mufti): A qualified jurist who issues legal opinions (fatawa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The chain of ijazah from multiple authoritative teachers is a cornerstone of scholarly credibility in the Hanafi tradition.

The Scholarly Chain of Sheikh al-Maidani
Biographical account of teachers and ijazas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Sheikh al-Maidani's key teachers and explain the role of ijaza in establishing scholarly authority in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
A scholar's ijaza chain is the backbone of knowledge transmission.

This lesson explores the teachers and ijazas of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani, the eminent Hanafi author of Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. Understanding his scholarly lineage not only validates his authority but also illustrates the broader Hanafi system of knowledge transmission through interconnected chains of teachers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the teachers
List each teacher mentioned, noting their location, madhhab, and any special role (e.g., mufti). This gives a picture of al-Maidani's educational network.
Pay attention to the footnoted references; they indicate primary biographical sources.
2
Analyze the concept of ijaza
From the passage, ijaza is a formal authorization to transmit knowledge. Note how al-Maidani himself gives an ijaza listing his teachers, showing the chain of transmission.
Ijaza is not merely a certificate; it is a personal link to earlier authorities.
3
Understand the teacher-student relationship
The vivid description of al-Maidani's attachment to al-Bitar ('like a nursing mother') underscores the depth of personal study. Reflect on why such close mentorship is valued.
This relationship ensures careful and accurate transmission of the madhhab.

الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني
١٢ـ وأجازه من أهل يافا في فلسطين العلامة الشيخ السيد حسن ابن سليم الدجاني، المفتي الحنفي ، المولود سنة ١٢٣٠ هـ تقريباً، والمتوفى سنة ١٢٩٠هـ ونيف، رحمه الله تعالى(۱).
١٣ ـ وأجازه من بيت المقدس الشيخ طاهر أفندي مفتي القدس (۲)
١٤ - وقرأ على العلامة الكبير الشيخ حسن بن إبراهيم بن حسن البيطار الشافعي الدمشقي الميداني إقامة ومدفناً ، المولود سنة ١٢٠٦هـ، والمتوفى سنة ١٢٧٢هـ ، رحمه الله تعالى. (۳)
وكانت ملازمة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني له منذ أول طلبه للعلم، واستمرت مدة طويلة، وستأتي قصيدة نَظَمَها الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني في تهنئة شيخه الشيخ حسن البيطار، حين قدم من الحج سنة ١٢٤١هـ، وكان عمر الميداني آنذاك (۲۰) سنة. (٤)
قال الشيخ عبد الرزاق البيطار في ترجمة تلميذ والده الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني:
وقرأ ـ الميداني - على والدي الشيخ حسن البيطار، ولازمـه ملازمةَ المُرْضِعَةِ للرضيع، وكان الميداني يكثر المديح في حقـه لـدى كل رفيع ووضيع. ولما طلب منه ـ أي من الميداني ـ الإجازة حضرة المحترم السيد سلمان أفندي القادري نقيـب بـغــداد، كتـب لـه بـهـا أسـمـاء مشايخه المرموقين، ولما ذكر والدي قال : وكان جل انتفاعي به». اهـ
وسيأتي أيضاً تقريظ الشيخ حسن البيطار وثناؤه على تلميذه الميداني، وكان تاريخ هذا التقريظ سنة ١٢٦١هـ، وسن الميداني آنذاك تسع وثلاثون (۳۹) سنة.
١٥- كما قرأ على العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني بن عبد القادر السقطي الدمشقي الصالحي الشافعي ، المولود سنة ١١٦٥هـ، والمتوفى سنة ١٢٤٦هـ ، رحمه الله تعالى، وقد ذكر قراءتـه عليـه صـاحب حليـة البشر (۱)
هذا ما وقفت عليه من أسماء شيوخه ممن تخرج بهـم ، فقـرأ عليهم، وأخذ عنهم، أو استجازهم فأجازوه.
وهكذا نلحظ مما تقدم أن أخص شيوخه ممن أكثـر الأخـذ عنهم، وأكثر هو من ذكرهم خمسة، هم: ١- الشيخ عمر المجتهد. (۱) له ترجمة في حلية البشر ٥٢١/١. (۲) لم أقف على ترجمته. (۳) ترجم له نجله في حلية البشر ٤٦٣/١. (٤) حلية البشر ٨٦٨/٢. (۱) له ترجمة في حلية البشر ٨٦٢/٢. .٢( ٨٦٨/٢)
Chapter One: Biography of the Allamah Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani
12- He was granted an ijaza from the people of Jaffa in Palestine by the Allamah Sheikh Sayyid Hasan ibn Sulaym al-Dajani, the Hanafi mufti, born approximately 1230 AH, and died in 1290 AH or so, may Allah have mercy on him. (1)
13- And he was granted an ijaza from Jerusalem by Sheikh Tahir Afandi, mufti of Jerusalem. (2)
14- And he studied under the great Allamah Sheikh Hasan ibn Ibrahim ibn Hasan al-Bitar al-Shafi'i al-Dimashqi, resident and buried in al-Maidani, born 1206 AH, died 1272 AH, may Allah have mercy on him. (3)
Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani was his companion from the beginning of his pursuit of knowledge, and it continued for a long time. There will come a poem composed by Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani congratulating his teacher Sheikh Hasan al-Bitar when he returned from Hajj in 1241 AH, al-Maidani being then 20 years old. (4)
Sheikh Abd al-Razzaq al-Bitar said in the biography of his father's student, Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani:
"Al-Maidani read under my father Sheikh Hasan al-Bitar, and accompanied him like a nursing mother to an infant. Al-Maidani would praise him extensively before high and low. When the respected Sayyid Salman Afandi al-Qadiri, the naqib of Baghdad, requested an ijaza from him (i.e., al-Maidani), he wrote for him the names of his distinguished teachers, and when he mentioned my father he said: 'My greatest benefit was from him.'" End.
There will also come a commendation from Sheikh Hasan al-Bitar praising his student al-Maidani, and the date of this commendation is 1261 AH, al-Maidani being then thirty-nine (39) years old.
15- He also read under the Allamah Sheikh Abdul Ghani ibn Abd al-Qadir al-Saqti al-Dimashqi al-Salihi al-Shafi'i, born 1165 AH, died 1246 AH, may Allah have mercy on him, and his reading under him was mentioned by the author of Hilyat al-Bashar. (1)
This is what I have found of the names of his teachers from whom he graduated; he read under them, took from them, or sought and received ijazas from them.
Thus we observe from the above that the most particular of his teachers from whom he took extensively and whom he mentioned most are five: 1. Sheikh Umar al-Mujtahid. (1) See his biography in Hilyat al-Bashar 1/521. (2) I did not find his biography. (3) His son wrote his biography in Hilyat al-Bashar 1/463. (4) Hilyat al-Bashar 2/868. (1) See his biography in Hilyat al-Bashar 2/862. 2/868.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of the Hanafi scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani (author of the Lubab Sharh al-Quduri), detailing his teachers and the scholarly connections (ijazat) he received. The text lists teachers from various regions: Jaffa, Jerusalem, and Damascus, showing the breadth of his education. Notably, his primary teacher was Sheikh Hasan al-Bitar, with whom he had a long and close relationship, described vividly as 'like a nursing mother to an infant.' The biography emphasizes the importance of ijaza (scholarly authorization) in the transmission of knowledge, a key feature of Islamic education. The footnotes provide references to biographical sources, confirming the reliability of the information. This section serves to establish al-Maidani's scholarly lineage, which is crucial for understanding his authority as a commentator of al-Quduri's matn.

Key Terms
إجازة (ijāzah): Scholarly authorization or permission to transmit knowledge, often given by a teacher to a student after confirming his proficiency.
ترجمة (tarjamah): Biography or scholarly profile of a person, detailing his life, teachers, students, and works.
مفتي (muftī): A jurist qualified to issue fatwas (legal opinions) based on Islamic law.

The Scholarly Lineage of Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani: His Teachers and Their Significance
Biographical account listing al-Maydani's primary and secondary teachers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five primary teachers of Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani and explain the role of ijazah in Hanafi knowledge transmission.

Core Idea
The chain of teachers is the backbone of Hanafi scholarship: al-Maydani's five primary teachers shaped his mastery of al-Quduri.

This passage from al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri introduces us to the scholarly lineage of its author, Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. Biography is not mere history; it is a statement of authority. Knowing who taught a scholar tells us the chain of transmission (sanad) through which the text reaches us. In this lesson, we will walk through the teachers listed and understand the concept of ijazah and the significance of the five core teachers.

Guided Path
1
Understand the purpose of listing teachers
In Hanafi tradition, tracing the teachers of a scholar establishes the reliability of the chain of transmission (sanad) for the texts he transmits. This list serves to authenticate al-Maydani's authority as a commentator on al-Quduri.
The text explicitly says al-Maydani wrote the names of his teachers when granting an ijazah.
2
Distinguish the two teacher lists
The passage first identifies five 'most specific' teachers (أخص شيوخه) from whom he took the most and whom he mentioned most. Then it provides an alphabetical list of thirteen teachers. The five are a subset of the thirteen, but they are emphasized as his core mentors.
The five are: Umar al-Mujtahid, Ibn Abidin, Hasan al-Baytar, Sa'id al-Halabi, and Abd al-Rahman al-Kuzbari.
3
Recognize the prominent figures
Among the five, Sheikh Ibn Abidin is a towering figure in the Hanafi school, known for his supercommentary Radd al-Muhtar. The inclusion of such scholars signifies the high level of training al-Maydani received.
Sheikh Umar al-Mujtahid is also a distinguished Hanafi jurist.
4
Understand the concept of ijazah
The passage mentions that Sayyid Salman al-Qadiri, the naqib of Baghdad, requested an ijazah from al-Maydani. In response, al-Maydani wrote the names of his teachers. This shows that an ijazah is a written certification authorizing the recipient to transmit the scholar's works and teachings.
Ijazah is a recognized method of transmission in the Hanafi school.
5
Memorize the five primary teachers
For a student of Hanafi fiqh, knowing these five names connects you to the scholarly lineage of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. Commit these names to memory: 1) Umar al-Mujtahid, 2) Ibn Abidin, 3) Hasan al-Baytar, 4) Sa'id al-Halabi, 5) Abd al-Rahman al-Kuzbari.
The alphabetical list includes additional teachers but these five are the most influential.

It then specifies that al-Maydani read under Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Saqti al-Shafi'i. This list includes prominent figures such as Ibrahim al-Bajuri (an Egyptian scholar), Ahmad Baybars al-'Ajluni, and others. The biography helps establish al-Maydani's scholarly credentials and the chain of knowledge he received.

مشايخه (mashāyikhuhu): His teachers; the plural of shaykh, referring to those from whom al-Maydani studied or received ijazah.
نقيب بغداد (naqīb Baghdād): The naqib or head of the Ashraf (descendants of the Prophet) in Baghdad, a respected position.

The Teachers of Sheikh al-Maidani: A Scholarly Network
Biographical listing of teachers with names and locations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the teachers of Sheikh al-Maidani and explain why knowing a scholar's teachers is important in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
A scholar's teachers are his intellectual lineage; memorizing them honors his authority.

This lesson presents a list of sixteen scholars from whom Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani, the commentator of al-Quduri, received knowledge. In the Hanafi tradition, the chain of teachers (mashayikh) is a marker of authenticity and scholarly pedigree. Understanding this list helps appreciate the interconnectedness of Hanafi learning in the 13th/19th century.

Guided Path
1
Identify the List's Purpose
The author includes this list at the beginning of his commentary to establish his authority by naming his teachers. Recognize that this is a common feature in Islamic scholarly works.
2
Count the Teachers
Count the entries; the passage lists 16 teachers numbered from 1 to 16. Verify that the numbers match the count.
Note that some names may be missing numbers but are still included in the sequence.
3
Note the Alphabetical Order
The author states he arranged them alphabetically (على حروف المعجم). Check the first letter of each name to confirm.
This organization aids memorization and reference.
4
Identify Key Figures
Look for well-known scholars such as Ibn Abidin (Sheikh Muhammad Amin Ibn Abidin), a major Hanafi authority. Recognize the diversity of locations: Egypt, Syria, Palestine, Hijaz.

The Scholarly Training of Sheikh al-Maidani: A Model for Hanafi Education
Description of the books read by the author under his teachers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the role of studying primary texts (ummahat al-kutub) under multiple teachers in the development of a Hanafi jurist.

Core Idea
A scholar's excellence is built on repeated, teacher-guided study of foundational texts across multiple sciences.

This passage from al-Maidani's biography offers a window into the rigorous scholarly training of a leading Hanafi jurist. It highlights the central role of 'ummahat al-kutub'—the principal texts of each science—and the practice of reading them with multiple teachers for deeper understanding. Understanding this pedagogical tradition helps us appreciate the weight and authority of classical Hanafi scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of the passage
The author intends to list the books studied to show al-Maidani's scholarly formation. Recognize that this is not just a list but a demonstration of scholarly pedigree.
2
Note the emphasis on multiple readings
Some books, like Sahih al-Bukhari, were read more than once with different teachers. This indicates thoroughness and the value of multiple perspectives.
Reading with multiple teachers enriches understanding through different commentaries and chains of transmission.
3
Recognize the scope of subjects
The books cover diverse sciences (hadith, fiqh, usul, grammar, etc.), showing that a comprehensive jurist must be well-rounded.
Hanafi jurists were often also muhaddith, usuli, and nahwi.
4
Understand the concept of 'ummahat al-kutub'
These are the primary, reliable sources in each field. For Hanafi fiqh, these include works like al-Hidayah and al-Quduri, but here it refers to general foundational works.
The phrase 'ummahat al-kutub' indicates texts that are normative and widely accepted.
5
Reflect on the pedagogical model
The traditional model of reading under teachers, rather than independent study, ensures proper understanding and authorizes the student to transmit knowledge.
This model creates an unbroken chain of learning from the early generations.

المطلب الرابع : بيان عن الكتب التي قرأها على شيوخه : من خلال ذكر مشايخه الأعلام، وما قرأ عليهم الميداني من كتب، يَحْسُن التوقف عندها ؛ لنتعرف على هذه المجموعة الكبيرة من أُمَّات الكتب المعتمدة والمتنوعة الفنون، التي قرأها الميداني على مشايخه قراءة درس وتفهم، بل قرأ بعضها أكثر من مرة على أكثر من عالم مثل صحيح البخاري وغيره من كتب السنن. وإن قراءة هذه الكتب - مع توفيق الله تعالى ـ كانت من الأسباب الكبرى لنبوغ هذا العالم الجليل، البارع النبيل، الفقيه الأصولي العمدة، المحدث النحوي الحجة. وسأسرد فيما يلي هذه الكتب جملة واحدة، متتالية حسب فنونها، لنتعرف على الكتب السائدة الشائعة في ذلك الزمن، مما كان يقرؤه التلاميذ على أساتذتهم وشيوخهم. هذا، بيان لما أجمل منها، حيث إن بعضها لم يشتهر ولم يعرف في هذا الزمن. ومما ينبه إليه هنا، أن الميداني رحمه الله مع قراءته لهذه الكتب على أعلام مشايخ عصره ، فقد وَرِثَ عنهم تلك الحال الحسنة
The fourth section: Statement of the books he read under his teachers: Through mentioning his prominent teachers and what al-Maidani read with them of books, it is good to pause at them so that we may get to know this large collection of the primary, reliable books of diverse sciences, which al-Maidani read with his teachers as a lesson and understanding. Rather, he read some of them more than once under more than one scholar, such as Sahih al-Bukhari and other books of Sunan. Indeed, reading these books - with the success of Allah the Exalted - was among the greatest reasons for the brilliance of this great scholar, the noble excellent one, the jurist, the foundational scholar, the reliable one, the hadith scholar, the grammarian, the proof. I will list below these books in one sequence, consecutively according to their sciences, so that we may get to know the prevalent and common books of that time, which students used to read under their teachers and masters. This is an explanation of what is summarized from them, as some of them are not famous and not known in this time. Among what is pointed out here is that al-Maidani, may Allah have mercy on him, with his reading of these books under the eminent scholars of his era, inherited from them that good state.

Commentary
This passage introduces the fourth section of the biography, which will list the books that Sheikh al-Maidani studied under his teachers. The author emphasizes the importance of these books, describing them as 'ummahat al-kutub' (primary texts) covering various sciences. He notes that al-Maidani read some books, like Sahih al-Bukhari, multiple times with different teachers, which indicates thorough study. The author attributes al-Maidani's scholarly excellence to his extensive reading of these texts. The list is to be organized by subject (science), reflecting the curriculum of the time. The author also mentions that some books are no longer well-known, providing insight into the evolution of Islamic scholarly tradition.

Key Terms
أُمَّات الكتب (ummahat al-kutub): Primary or source books, the essential texts in a field.
الفقيه الأصولي (al-faqih al-usuli): A jurist and usul al-fiqh scholar, one skilled in both positive law and legal theory.

The Scholarly Legacy of Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani: Teachers and Curriculum
Biographical preface showing scholarly formation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify key teachers and curriculum texts of Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani and explain how this scholarly training contributed to his authority in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
A scholar's comprehensive curriculum under multiple masters is the foundation of his juristic authority.

This passage introduces us to the scholarly formation of one of the late Hanafi giants, Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. It lists some of his eminent teachers and begins a catalogue of the major works he studied, spanning tajwid, aqidah, and more. Understanding this background helps us appreciate why his commentary on al-Quduri is so highly regarded.

Guided Path
1
Identify the teachers listed
The passage names three teachers: Muhammad al-Atushi al-Maliki, Sayyid Muhammad Amin ibn Abidin (the famous Hanafi jurist), and Mustafa al-Muballit al-Misri. Note the diversity: a Maliki and two Hanafis, indicating cross-madhhab learning.
Ibn Abidin is a key authority in later Hanafi fiqh.
2
Recognize the purpose of listing books
The author states that listing the books al-Maydani read under his teachers helps us understand the comprehensive curriculum of authoritative texts, and that reading them was a major cause of his brilliance.
The curriculum included works from multiple disciplines.
3
Note the first two disciplines covered
The passage begins a list by discipline: first tajwid and qira'at (with al-Sakhawiyyah), then aqidah (with al-Sanusiyyah). This shows that al-Maydani studied foundational religious sciences beyond fiqh.
This breadth of study strengthens his authority in fiqh commentary.

Chapter One: Biography of the scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. 14 - Sheikh Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Atushi al-Maliki al-Madani. 15 - Sheikh al-Sayyid Muhammad Amin ibn Umar ibn Abidin. 16 - Sheikh Mustafa al-Muballit al-Misri. 37 Section Four: Statement of the books he read under his teachers: By mentioning his prominent teachers and what al-Maydani read under them of books, it is good to pause at them; so that we may recognize this large collection of authoritative and varied mother-books of different disciplines, which al-Maydani read under his teachers as lessons of study and understanding; indeed, he read some of them more than once under more than one scholar, such as Sahih al-Bukhari and other books of Sunan. And indeed, reading these books – with the success of Allah Almighty – was among the major reasons for the brilliance of this great, noble, proficient scholar, the foundational jurist, the hadith master and grammarian authority. I will list below these books all together, consecutively according to their disciplines, so that we may recognize the prevalent books common in that time, which students used to read under their teachers and masters. This is an explanation of what is summarized from them, as some of them are not well-known nor recognized in this time. It should be noted here that al-Maydani, may Allah have mercy on him, while reading these books under the prominent scholars of his time, inherited from them that good state. 38 Chapter One: Biography of the scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani 6 the excellent pleasing state they were upon of acting upon knowledge, piety, righteousness, sincerity, asceticism, and scrupulousness, as is known from his state which will be explained later, Allah willing. Books of Tajwid and Qira'at: 1 - al-Sakhawiyyah: it is a fine poem in tajwid of more than two hundred verses, by Alam al-Din al-Sakhawi Ali ibn Muhammad, died in 643 AH, author of Jamal al-Qurra wa Kamal al-Iqra, it is printed, and he has many books in qira'at and tajwid. - Books of Creed: 1 - al-Sanusiyyah in Tawhid, and its commentary by al-Hadadi. As for al-Sanusiyyah, it is attributed to Imam Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn al-Sanusi al-Tilmisani al-Hasani, died in 895 AH, he has many works in tafsir, hadith, and others, and he has several books in creed, including 'Aqidat Ahl al-Tawhid wa al-Tasdid, al-Mukharraj min Zulmat al-Jahl. (1) There is a biography in al-A'lam by al-Zarkali 7/154, and there has been a serious study in Algeria about Imam al-Sanusi and his writings in the science of tawhid, written by Professor Jamal al-Din Buqali Hasan, published by the National Book Foundation in Algeria in 1985 CE (400 pages), and its origin is a university thesis, and at the end of this thesis is printed the text of al-Sanusiyyah in Tawhid, named 'Umm al-Barahin.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This is a biographical passage from the introduction to al-Maydani's commentary. The author lists some of al-Maydani's teachers: Sheikh Muhammad al-Atushi al-Maliki, Sayyid Muhammad Amin ibn Abidin (the famous Hanafi jurist), and Sheikh Mustafa al-Muballit. Then it explains the purpose of listing the books al-Maydani studied: to show the comprehensive curriculum of authoritative texts in various disciplines that he read under his teachers, sometimes multiple times for key works like Sahih al-Bukhari. The passage emphasizes that this rigorous study was a major cause of his scholarly excellence, and that he inherited from his teachers not only knowledge but also their pious character. It then begins a list of books by discipline, starting with tajwid and qira'at (al-Sakhawiyyah) and aqaid (al-Sanusiyyah). The footnote provides additional biographical information about Imam al-Sanusi.

Key Terms
السَّخاوِيَّة (al-Sakhawiyyah): A poem (manzumah) of over 200 verses on tajwid by Alam al-Din al-Sakhawi.
السنوسية (al-Sanusiyyah): A work on tawhid (creed) by Muhammad ibn Yusuf al-Sanusi, also known as 'Umm al-Barahin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) al-Sakhawiyyah
C) Sahih al-Bukhari
D) Sharh al-Hadadi

Key Takeaway
Al-Maydani's mastery of multiple disciplines, studied under great scholars, established him as a leading Hanafi jurist.
