Biography of Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani and His Hadith Studies
Biographical introduction and list of hadith works studied by the author

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key hadith works studied by al-Maidani and explain the importance of hadith mastery for a Hanafi jurist.

Core Idea
A Hanafi jurist's authority is built on mastery of the Prophetic Sunnah.

This lesson introduces you to the scholarly background of al-Maidani, the author of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. Understanding his hadith studies reveals the depth of training expected of a Hanafi jurist. The passage lists the major hadith collections he read, showing his engagement with both the six canonical books and other important compilations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his significance
Locate the name 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani' and note that he is the commentator of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri, a key Hanafi fiqh text. Recognize that this passage is from the editor's introduction.
Al-Maidani lived in Damascus and died in 1298 AH.
2
Recognize the genre of the passage
This is a biographical (tarjama) section, not part of the original fiqh text. It provides context for the author's qualifications.
3
List the hadith works mentioned
Go through the numbered list: 1-8 are the well-known Kutub al-Sitta plus Muwatta' and Adab al-Mufrad. Note that items 9-12 are specialized compilations (Mashariq al-Anwar, Musalsalat, etc.).
The list is incomplete; it ends at number 12.
4
Understand the pedagogical purpose
The editor lists these works to establish al-Maidani's hadith credentials, which underpin his fiqh commentary. In Hanafi tradition, a jurist (faqih) is expected to be well-versed in hadith.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction from the modern printed edition of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri by Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani. It begins with the editor's biography of the author, mentioning his study of various creedal works, particularly the Sanusiyya, and then lists the hadith collections that al-Maidani read. This is not part of the original fiqh text but provides scholarly context. The editor notes that al-Maidani studied the six major hadith books (the Kutub al-Sitta), Muwatta' Malik, and specialized works like al-Adab al-Mufrad and selected compilations. The list ends abruptly with number 12, indicating a missing continuation. The passage serves to establish the author's hadith credentials.

Key Terms
السنوسية (al-Sanusiyya): A concise creedal text (al-Aqida al-Sughra) by Muhammad bin Yusuf al-Sanusi, widely studied in the Hanafi and Ash'ari tradition.
الميداني (al-Maidani): The author of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri, a Hanafi jurist and hadith scholar from Damascus (d. 1298 AH).
الصحيحين (al-Sahihayn): A dual reference to Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim, the two most authoritative hadith collections.
الكتب الستة (al-Kutub al-Sitta): The six canonical hadith collections: Sahih al-Bukhari, Sahih Muslim, Sunan Abi Dawud, Sunan al-Tirmidhi, Sunan al-Nasa'i, and Sunan Ibn Majah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Scholarly Foundations: Sources in al-Maydani's Lubab
Bibliographic listing of author's sources

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and categorize the major hadith, Sira, and Hanafi fiqh works cited by al-Maydani in his Lubab commentary.

Core Idea
Al-Maydani's commentary draws on canonical hadith, prophetic biography, and mature Hanafi textual tradition.

In this lesson, we explore the sources that Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani used to write his Lubab commentary. Recognizing these works helps you understand the author's methodology and the intellectual tradition he represents. This is not a fiqh ruling but a bibliographic orientation essential for engaging with the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
The passage groups the sources into three categories: hadith collections, books on Sira and Shama'il, and Hanafi fiqh works. List each category as a mental framework.
This structure shows the author's comprehensive approach.
2
Note the hadith collections
The list includes the six canonical Sunan (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud, Nasa'i, Ibn Majah), Muwatta' of Malik, and specialized works like Adab al-Mufrad and musalsalat collections.
These are primary sources for Prophetic traditions used in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Recognize the Sira and Shama'il works
Two key works: al-Shama'il al-Muhammadiyyah by Tirmidhi and al-Shifa by Qadi 'Iyad. These are essential for understanding the Prophet's life and attributes.
These are not directly fiqh but provide context for rulings.
4
Examine the Hanafi fiqh texts
The list spans early works (Muqaddimat Abi al-Layth) to later authoritative texts (Nur al-Idah, Durr al-Mukhtar, Ibn 'Abidin's works). This shows the depth of the Hanafi tradition.
Each work builds on earlier ones, forming a chain of commentary.
5
Understand the author's aim
By citing these sources, al-Maydani signals that his commentary is rooted in authentic hadith and the established Hanafi corpus.
This bibliography is a tool for the reader to verify rulings and trace arguments.

١- الشمائل المحمدية، للإمام الترمذي صاحب السنن.
٢- الشفا بتعريف حقوق المصطفى صلى الله عليه وسلم، للقاضي عياض بن موسى اليحصبي، المتوفى سنة ٥٤٤هـ.

كتب الفقه الحنفي وأصوله:
١- مقدمة أبي الليث، للإمام نصر بن محمد السمرقندي، المتوفى سنة ٣٩٣هـ.
٢- نور الإيضاح مع شرحه إمداد الفتاح، للشرنبلالي حسن بن عمار، المتوفى سنة ١٠٦٩هـ.
٣- الدر المختار شرح تنوير الأبصار، للحصكفي محمد بن علي، المتوفى سنة ١٠٨٨هـ.

Books on Hanafi Fiqh and Its Principles:

Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is the first chapter of the book, providing a biographical sketch of the author, Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, and listing the primary sources he used in compiling his commentary. It is divided into three sections: hadith collections, works on the Sira and Shama'il of the Prophet (peace be upon him), and Hanafi fiqh literature. The hadith section includes the six canonical books (the Sunan of Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud, Nasa'i, and Ibn Majah) plus Malik's Muwatta', Bukhari's Adab al-Mufrad, and some specialized works like al-Saghani's selection and two musalsal collections. The Sira section includes Tirmidhi's Shama'il and Qadi 'Iyad's al-Shifa. The Hanafi fiqh section lists foundational texts: the introductory work of Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi, the popular primer Nur al-Idah and its commentary, the authoritative Durr al-Mukhtar and its major commentary by Ibn 'Abidin, Babarti's 'Inayah on al-Hidayah, and various fatwa collections. This list demonstrates the author's reliance on standard Hanafi authorities and his aim to produce a comprehensive commentary that draws from both early and later works of the school.

Key Terms
سنن الترمذي (Sunan al-Tirmidhi): One of the six canonical hadith collections, compiled by Imam al-Tirmidhi (d. 279 AH).
نور الإيضاح (Nur al-Idah): A primer on Hanafi fiqh by al-Shurunbulali, often taught to beginners.
الموطأ (Al-Muwatta'): The hadith collection of Imam Malik (d. 179 AH), containing both hadith and early fiqh opinions.
الشفا (Al-Shifa): A comprehensive work on the rights and virtues of the Prophet, by Qadi 'Iyad (d. 544 AH).
الدر المختار (Al-Durr al-Mukhtar): A comprehensive Hanafi fiqh manual by al-Haskafi (d. 1088 AH), with commentary Radd al-Muhtar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-Maydani's Lubab commentary is built on a foundation of canonical hadith, respected Sira works, and authoritative Hanafi fiqh texts, allowing students to trace arguments back to their sources.

The Hanafi Textual Tradition: Authors and Sources
Biographical introduction listing key sources used in the commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key Hanafi fiqh, usul, and fara'id works cited by al-Maydani and classify them by genre (matn, sharh, hashiya).

Core Idea
A Hanafi scholar's commentary rests on a layered chain of matn, sharh, and hashiya.

This passage introduces the renowned Hanafi jurist Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani and lists the works he relied upon in his commentary al-Lubab. Understanding this list gives you a map of the Hanafi textual tradition—from concise matns like Mukhtasar al-Quduri to supercommentaries like Radd al-Muhtar. It is not a lesson in fiqh rulings, but in the literary apparatus that preserves and transmits the school's positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his era
Note the author's full name, death date (1162 AH), and his lineage (al-Ajluni). This places him chronologically in the later Hanafi tradition (11th-12th centuries AH).
Al-Maydani is a commentator, not a founder of the school.
2
Categorize the listed works by subject
The passage groups works into: prophetic biography (al-Shama'il, al-Shifa), Hanafi fiqh (e.g., Mukhtasar al-Quduri, Nur al-Idah, al-Durr al-Mukhtar), usul al-fiqh (al-Manar, al-Tawdih), and fara'id (al-Rahbiyya, al-Sirajiyya). This shows the breadth of sources needed to produce a comprehensive commentary.
Each category serves a different purpose in the scholar's toolkit.
3
Distinguish matn, sharh, and hashiya
Identify which works are original texts (matn: Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Manar), which are commentaries (sharh: Nur al-Idah, al-Inaya, al-Tawdih, Sharh al-Rahbiyya), and which are supercommentaries (hāshiya: Radd al-Muhtar, Rasa'il Ibn Abidin). This hierarchy reflects increasing depth and refinement.
Al-Durr al-Mukhtar is itself a sharh on Tanwir al-Absar; Radd al-Muhtar is a hashiya on that.
4
Note the lineage of authorities
Many works reference each other. For example, al-Haskafi's al-Durr al-Mukhtar is commented on by Ibn Abidin's Radd al-Muhtar. Recognize these chains to understand how rulings developed.
Later scholars (mutakkhirūn) often settle earlier ikhtilāf.
5
Appreciate the inter-madhhab dimension
Al-Maydani includes two fara'id works from non-Hanafi authors: al-Rahbiyya (Shafi'i) and its commentary by Sibt al-Mardini (Hanafi-leaning?). This shows that Hanafi scholars engage with other schools where useful.
Al-Sirajiyya is purely Hanafi; al-Rahbiyya is widely used across madhhabs.

Books of fara'id and inheritance: 1- Sharh al-Rahbiyya. As for al-Rahbiyya, it is by Muhammad ibn Ali ibn Muhammad al-Rahbi al-Shafi'i, died 577 AH. Among the famous and circulated commentaries of al-Rahbiyya is the commentary of Sibt al-Mardini Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Ghazzal al-Dimashqi, died 912 AH. 2- Sharh al-Sirajiyya. As for al-Sirajiyya, it is by al-Sajawandi Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rashid al-Hanafi, died around 600 AH. Among the famous commentaries of al-Sirajiyya is the commentary of al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani Ali ibn Muhammad, died 816 AH.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and bibliographical introduction from 'Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri' by Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. The author first identifies himself and his death date (1162 AH). He then lists the key sources he relies on in his commentary, divided into categories: books on prophetic biography (such as al-Tirmidhi's Shama'il and Qadi Iyad's al-Shifa), core Hanafi fiqh works (like al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, al-Shurunbulali's Nur al-Idah, al-Haskafi's al-Durr al-Mukhtar, and Ibn Abidin's Radd al-Muhtar), usul al-fiqh works (such as al-Nasafi's al-Manar and Sadr al-Shari'a's al-Tawdih), and works on fara'id (such as commentaries on al-Rahbiyya and al-Sirajiyya). This list demonstrates the depth of Hanafi scholarship and the textual tradition that al-Maydani engages with.

Key Terms
ترجمة (tarjama): Biography or biographical notice, often at the beginning of a book to introduce the author.
الفرائض والمواريث (al-fara'id wa al-mawarith): The Islamic laws of inheritance, covering fixed shares (fara'id) and distribution of estate (mawarith).
المتن (al-matn): The core text, usually concise, that forms the basis for commentary. Example: Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
الشرح (al-sharh): A commentary that explains and expands upon a matn. Example: al-Durr al-Mukhtar.
الحاشية (al-hashiya): A supercommentary or gloss that comments on a sharh, often adding later fatwas and tarjih. Example: Radd al-Muhtar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-Maydani's list of sources reveals the layered structure of Hanafi scholarship, from foundational matns to authoritative supercommentaries like Radd al-Muhtar.

The Scholarly Upbringing of Sheikh Ismail al-Maydani
Biographical account of a scholar's son

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key stages of Sheikh Ismail al-Maydani's education and explain how his biography establishes the authority of the Hanafi fiqh text.

Core Idea
The biography of a scholar's son confirms the continuity of Hanafi teaching across generations.

This passage introduces us to Sheikh Ismail al-Maydani, the son of the distinguished Hanafi scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. While it may appear as a simple biographical note, it serves a deeper purpose: it traces the transmission of Hanafi knowledge from father to son, establishing the author's scholarly lineage and the authority of the fiqh text you are about to study. Understanding this lineage helps you appreciate the reliability of the rulings derived from this tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and sources
Read the passage to identify who is being described and which biographical works are cited. The primary source is 'Hilyat al-Bashar', with a corroborating note from 'Muntakhabat al-Tawarikh li-Dimashq'.
The use of multiple sources reinforces the credibility of the biographical details.
2
Extract key biographical milestones
List the major events: birth year, early Quranic education, study of Hanafi fiqh under his father, acquisition of instrumental sciences under Shaykh Muhammad al-Tantawi, attendance at scholarly gatherings, and his death year.
Note the specific Hijri years: birth in 1254 AH and death in 1332 AH.
3
Analyze the educational curriculum
Identify the subjects mentioned: Quran, Hanafi fiqh (al-fiqh al-nu'mani), instrumental sciences (ulum al-alat), and other high sciences like tafsir, hadith, and tawhid.
Instrumental sciences include Arabic grammar, rhetoric, and logic – essential tools for a jurist.
4
Connect the biography to fiqh authority
Consider why this biography is included in a fiqh text. It establishes the author's son as a credible scholar, reinforces the chain of transmission, and shows that the family produced reliable teachers of the Hanafi school.
The passage notes that Ismail 'followed his father in virtue, guiding the public and teaching them their religious affairs.'

Chapter One: Biography of the distinguished scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani
Section Two
The family of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani
45
Indeed, Allah Almighty honored Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani with virtuous and blessed offspring among the people of knowledge and virtue.
1 - This is his son, Sheikh Ismail ibn Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. The author of Hilyat al-Bashar wrote his biography, saying:
Sheikh Ismail ibn Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, an ally of literature and refinement, a companion of gentleness and delight. His merit extended far, his nature absorbed the love of knowledge. He moved forward in the field of progress in width and length, and in the heights of advancement he had the upper hand.
His birth was in the second half of the sacred month of Dhu al-Hijjah in the year 1254 [AH]. He grew up under the care of his father, the elite of the righteous. After reaching the age of discernment, he read the Noble Quran, then he attended the Hanafi jurisprudence lessons of his father until he achieved his greatest hopes.
46
Chapter One: Biography of the distinguished scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani
He acquired a number of instrumental sciences from our teacher, the virtuous scholar, the perfect genius, the rarity of the age, the unique of the era, Sheikh Muhammad Afandi al-Tantawi—may Allah elevate his station in the ranks of nearness and grant him his desire and aspiration in the Garden of Paradise.
He attended the gatherings of many virtuous people whose words and narrations were relied upon. Among them, indeed the highest and most knowledgeable of them was the banner of banners, the reliance of judges, my brother and full brother, the energetic Sheikh Muhammad Afandi Amin Fatwa al-Sham.
Often, a study session on every lofty science—such as tafsir, hadith, tawhid, and other disciplines of meanings and rhetoric—would include both him and me. He would defer to me and rely on me in solving difficulties.
He had beauty and purity, affection and loyalty.
He died in Ramadan of the year 1332 AH. May Allah elevate his rank in the stations of leadership and make Paradise his dwelling and abode. End quote from Hilyat al-Bashar.
Muhammad Taqi al-Husni said about him in Muntakhabat al-Tawarikh li-Dimashq: "Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani was succeeded by Ismail, who followed his father in virtue, guiding the public and teaching them their religious affairs." End quote. Sheikh Ismail ibn Sheikh Abd al-Ghani has a commentary on his father's treatise.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of Sheikh Ismail al-Maydani, son of the renowned Hanafi scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. It comes from the biographical section of the book, which details the author's scholarly lineage. The primary source cited is 'Hilyat al-Bashar' by another author, which describes Sheikh Ismail's virtues, birth date (mid-Dhu al-Hijjah 1254 AH), early education under his father in Hanafi fiqh, and later studies in instrumental sciences under Sheikh Muhammad al-Tantawi. He also attended circles of learned scholars, notably Sheikh Muhammad Afandi Amin Fatwa al-Sham. The passage highlights his scholarly collaboration with the author and his role in guiding the public. It concludes with his death in Ramadan 1332 AH and notes that he authored a commentary on his father's treatise. Muhammad Taqi al-Husni also confirms his succession of his father in teaching and guiding the community. This serves to establish the credentials and intellectual heritage of the author's family, which is relevant for the authority of the fiqh work.

Key Terms
حلية البشر (Hilyat al-Bashar): A biographical work from which the description of Sheikh Ismail is quoted.
الفقه النعماني (al-fiqh al-nu‘mani): Hanafi jurisprudence, named after Imam Abu Hanifa (Nu'man bin Thabit).
علوم الآلات (‘ulum al-ālāt): Instrumental sciences necessary for understanding primary religious sciences, such as Arabic grammar, rhetoric, and logic.

Life of the Author
beginner
5 min
Biography of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani
Biographical introduction of the commentator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author of Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri and describe his scholarly lineage and teachers.

Core Idea
Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani, the author of Al-Lubab, was a Hanafi scholar who studied under al-Tantawi and his brother the Fatwa Mufti.

This lesson introduces the life and teachers of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani, the commentator of Quduri's matn. Understanding the author's background helps appreciate the authority and chain of transmission of the commentary. We will trace his education, his relationship with his brother, and the continuation of his legacy through his sons.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his teachers
State who the biography is about and name his primary teacher and his brother.
2
Recognize the auxiliary sciences
Note that he studied 'ulum al-alat from Shaykh al-Tantawi.
3
Understand the scholarly relationship with his brother
Observe that his brother was a high-ranking mufti and that they studied together.
4
Trace the author's descendants
Identify his sons Isma'il and Muhammad, and his grandson Yusuf.
5
Identify the evidence of a daughter
Note the mention of a grandson through a daughter (the copyist of a manuscript).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني
وأخذ جملة من علوم الآلات عن شيخنا العلامة الفاضل، والفهامة الكامل، نادرة الزمان، وأوحد العصر والأوان، الشيخ محمد أفندي الطنطاوي، أعلى الله في درجات القرب مقامه، وأعطاه في حديقة الرضوان مرغوبه ومرامه.
وحضر مجالس كثير من أهل الفضل، ممن يعتمد في القول والنقل، منهم بل أعلاهم وأعلمهم : عَلَمُ الأعلام، وعمدة الحكام،
أخي وشقيقي الهمام، الشيخ محمد أفندي أمين فتوى الشام.
وكثيراً ما كان يَضمُّني وإياه مجلس المطالعة في كل علم رفيع، من تفسير وحديث وتوحيد وغير ذلك من معان وبديع، وكان ينقاد إلي، ويعتمد في حل المشكلات علي.
وله جمال وصفا، ووداد ووفا.
توفي في رمضان سنة ١٣٣٢هـ، أعلـى الله في مدارج السيادة مرتقاه، وجعل الجنة مثواه ومأواه». اهـ من حلية البشر.
وقال عنه محمد تقي الحصني في منتخبات التواريخ لدمشق: «وقد أعقب الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني : إسماعيل، الذي خلف والده بالفضيلة، وإرشاد العامة، وتعليمهم أمور دينهم». اهـ وللشيخ إسماعيل ابن الشيخ عبد الغني شرح على رسالة والده:
إسعاف المريدين في إقامة فرائض الدين)، ومنه ثلاث نسخ خطية
في المكتبة الظاهرية بدمشق برقم (٤٧٩٣)، (٦٥٦٢)، (٨٢٠٦). ٢- وللشيخ عبد الغني الميداني ولد آخر اسمه: (محمد)، فقد ذكر العلامة الشيخ عبد الفتاح أبو غدة رحمه الله في مقدمة تحقيقـه لكتاب الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني : كشف الالتباس عما أورده البخاري على بعض الناس )، أنه وقف في دمشق، في ٢٠ من المحرم، سنة ١٣٨٧هـ، على مجموع مخطوط فيه عدة رسائل للشيخ عبد الغني الميداني، ثم قال : وهذا المجموع لحفيده الأخ الكريم يوسف بن محمد بن عبد الغني الغنيمي الميداني، المقيم في حي الميدان بدمشق، أحسن الله إليه ، وعنه نَسَحْتُ رسالته: «تحفة النساك»، و«كشف الالتباس. اهـ
ويظهر أن للشيخ عبد الغني رحمه الله بنتاً أو أكثر، حيث جاء في آخر نسخة من النسخ المخطوطة من كتابه: «كشف الالتباس» مـا يلي:
تمت على يد محمد سبط المؤلف سنة إحدى عشر وثلاثمائة بعد الألف». اهـ
Chapter One: Biography of the scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani. He acquired a number of instrumental sciences from our teacher, the virtuous scholar, the complete intellect, the rarity of the age, the unique of the era, Sheikh Muhammad Afandi al-Tantawi — may Allah elevate his station in the degrees of proximity and grant him his desires and aspirations in the garden of pleasure. He attended the gatherings of many people of virtue, among those relied upon in speech and transmission, including, indeed the highest and most learned of them: the banner of banners, the support of judges, my brother and full brother of high ambition, Sheikh Muhammad Afandi Amin Fatwa al-Sham. Often, a study session would bring together me and him in every elevated science: from interpretation, hadith, theology, and other profound and novel meanings. He would defer to me and rely on me in solving difficult issues. He possessed beauty and purity, affection and loyalty. He died in Ramadan of the year 1332 AH — may Allah elevate his station in the ranks of mastery and make Paradise his resting place and abode. End quote from Hilyat al-Bashar. Muhammad Taqi al-Husni said about him in Muntakhabat al-Tawarikh li-Dimashq: 'Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani left behind Isma'il, who succeeded his father in virtue, guiding the common people and teaching them their religious matters.' End quote. Sheikh Isma'il, son of Sheikh Abdul Ghani, has a commentary on his father's treatise: 'Is‘af al-Muridin fi Iqamat Fara'id al-Din', and there are three manuscript copies of it in the Zahiriyya Library in Damascus under numbers (4793, 6562, 8206). 2- Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani had another son named (Muhammad), for the scholar Sheikh Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghuddah (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned in his introduction to his edition of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani's book 'Kashf al-Iltebas 'amma awradahu al-Bukhari 'ala ba'd al-Nas' that he came across in Damascus on 20 Muharram 1387 AH a manuscript collection containing several treatises by Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani. Then he said: This collection belongs to his grandson, the noble brother Yusuf ibn Muhammad ibn Abdul Ghani al-Ghunaimi al-Maydani, resident in the Maydan quarter of Damascus, may Allah bless him, and from him I copied his treatise: 'Tuhfat al-Nusak' and 'Kashf al-Iltebas'. End quote. It appears that Sheikh Abdul Ghani (may Allah have mercy on him) had a daughter or more, as it comes at the end of one of the manuscript copies of his book 'Kashf al-Iltebas' the following: 'Completed by the hand of Muhammad, grandson of the author, in the year 1311 AH (eleven three hundred after one thousand).' End quote.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch (tarjama) of the author of the commentary, Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani. It begins by mentioning his teacher, Sheikh Muhammad Afandi al-Tantawi, from whom he learned various auxiliary sciences (ulum al-alat). He also attended the circles of many virtuous scholars, particularly his brother, Sheikh Muhammad Afandi Amin Fatwa al-Sham, a prominent figure in issuing fatwas. The two brothers studied together extensively, with Sheikh Abdul Ghani often taking the lead in resolving difficulties. His death occurred in Ramadan 1332 AH (corresponding to 1914 CE), as reported in Hilyat al-Bashar. Muhammad Taqi al-Husni notes that his son Isma'il succeeded him in teaching and guiding the public. Isma'il wrote a commentary on his father's work 'Is‘af al-Muridin'. Another son, Muhammad, had a son named Yusuf who preserved his grandfather's works. The passage also indicates that Sheikh Abdul Ghani had at least one daughter, as a grandson (from a daughter's side) copied one of his manuscripts. This biographical section serves to introduce the author's scholarly lineage and authority.

Key Terms
ترجمة (tarjama): Biographical sketch or introduction of a scholar's life, teachers, and works.
علوم الآلات (ʻulum al-ālāt): Auxiliary sciences necessary for studying the religious sciences, such as Arabic grammar, rhetoric, and logic.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who is the author of the commentary 'Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri' as introduced in this biography?
A) Sheikh Muhammad Afandi al-Tantawi
B) Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani
C) Sheikh Isma'il al-Maydani
D) Sheikh Muhammad Taqi al-Husni

Key Takeaway
Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani was a Hanafi scholar whose teachers, family, and students form a chain of transmission that supports the authority of his commentary Al-Lubab.

Life of the Author
beginner
5 min
The Scholarly Lineage of Shaykh al-Maydani
Biographical introduction to a Hanafi commentator

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the significance of the biographical introduction in a Hanafi fiqh commentary and identify key family members of Shaykh al-Maydani mentioned in the text.

Core Idea
A scholar’s progeny continuing in knowledge is a divine blessing and affirms the text's authority.

Biographical introductions in Hanafi fiqh works are not mere formalities—they establish the scholarly chain and convey the author’s trustworthiness. In this passage, the commentator al-Maydani’s editor highlights the term 'sibt' and lists descendants who were ʿulamāʾ, underscoring that knowledge was preserved in the family. Understanding this background helps us appreciate the care with which Hanafi texts are transmitted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of the biographical introduction
The passage begins with 'Chapter One: Biography...' indicating that the author intends to establish the credentials of the commentator. Note how it functions as a chain of transmission (isnād) for the commentary.
2
Clarify the term 'al-sibṭ'
The text explains that 'sibt' usually means daughter's son but can refer to any grandchild. This is relevant because it identifies a descendant mentioned later as a student of knowledge.
This term appears in inheritance laws but here it is purely genealogical.
3
List the descendants mentioned
The passage names: Muḥammad ibn Adīb al-Ghunaymī (scribe), an unnamed nephew named ʿAbd al-Ghanī, Shaykh Musallam al-Ghunaymī (imam for 50 years), and Shaykh Muḥammad al-Ghunaymī (imam of al-Kiswah). These figures demonstrate the continuity of scholarship.
The author couldn't determine the exact relation of Adīb, showing scholarly honesty.
4
Extract the supplication and its meaning
The passage ends with a duʿāʾ for blessings on the family and all Muslims. This is a standard feature in Islamic texts, reflecting the author's piety and hope for readers.
Such supplications remind us that knowledge is a means to draw closer to Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني
والسبط في الغالب يطلق على ولد البنت، مع إطلاقه لغوياً على ولد الولد.
وهذا يدل على أن ولد بنت الشيخ عبد الغني أيضاً من طلاب العلم، وهذا فضل من الله تعالى أن يُديم الهدي والعلم في ذرية العالم، نسأل الله تعالى بفضله من فضله وبرحمته من رحمته أن يكرمنا بذلك على أحسن حال، وأهدأ بال، إنه أكرم مسؤول.
وممن ذكر من أهل العلم من آل الغنيمي : محمد ابن الشيخ أديب الغنيمي الميداني، فقد جاء في آخر النسخة المخطوطة من رسالة: تحفة النساك في فضل السواك، للشيخ عبد الغني الميداني، التي اعتمدها الشيخ عبد الفتاح أبو غدة رحمه الله تعالى في تحقيق هذه الرسالة ما يلي: تمت على يد كاتبها محمد ابن الشيخ أديب الغنيمي الميداني، في ۱۸ رجب الفرد، سنة ١٣٠٨هـ. اهـ
ولم أستطع تحديد قرابة الشيخ أديب الغنيمي هذا من المترجم.
وممن ذكر أيضاً من طلاب العلم من أسرة الشيخ الميداني ابن الأخ الكبير للشيخ عبد الغني الميداني، واسمه عبد الغني كاسم عمه.
٦ ـ ومنهم : الشيخ مُسَلَّم الغنيمي، وكان إماماً لمسجد ساحة السخانة بحي الميدان، لمدة تزيد على خمسين عاماً.
ومنهم الشيخ محمد الغنيمي، الذي تسلم إمامة وخطابة مسجد الكسوة جنوبي دمشق لمدة تزيد على خمسة عشر عاماً.
وغير هؤلاء من هذه الذرية الطيبة في دمشق الشام إلى يومنا هذا، بارك الله فيهم، وفي العلماء العاملين، وفي ذراريهم والمسلمين أجمعين إلى يوم الدين.
(1) أخذت هذه المعلومة وما بعدها عن بقية أسرة آل الغنيمي الميداني من الإنترنت.
Chapter One: Biography of the eminent scholar Shaykh ‘Abd al-Ghanī al-Maydānī. The term ‘sibt’ (grandson) is generally applied to the daughter’s son, though linguistically it is used for any son’s son. This indicates that the daughter’s son of Shaykh ‘Abd al-Ghanī is also among the students of knowledge. This is a grace from Allah the Exalted that He perpetuates guidance and knowledge in the progeny of the scholar. We ask Allah the Exalted by His bounty and mercy to honor us with that in the best state and most peaceful heart. Indeed, He is the most generous who is asked. Among those mentioned as scholars from the Āl al-Ghunaymī family is Muḥammad ibn al-Shaykh Adīb al-Ghunaymī al-Maydānī. It appears at the end of the manuscript copy of the treatise “Tuḥfat al-Nusāk fī Faḍl al-Siwāk” by Shaykh ‘Abd al-Ghanī al-Maydānī, which was relied upon by Shaykh ‘Abd al-Fattāḥ Abū Ghuddah (may Allah have mercy on him) in editing this treatise, the following: “Completed by the hand of its scribe Muḥammad ibn al-Shaykh Adīb al-Ghunaymī al-Maydānī, on 18 Rajab al-Fard, year 1308 AH.” End quote. I was unable to determine the exact relationship of Shaykh Adīb al-Ghunaymī to the subject of this biography. Also mentioned among the students of knowledge from the family of Shaykh al-Maydānī is the elder brother’s son of Shaykh ‘Abd al-Ghanī al-Maydānī, whose name is ‘Abd al-Ghanī like his uncle. 6 – Among them is Shaykh Musallam al-Ghunaymī, who was the imam of the mosque of Sāḥat al-Sakhānah in al-Maydān district for over fifty years. And among them is Shaykh Muḥammad al-Ghunaymī, who served as imam and khatib of the mosque of al-Kiswah south of Damascus for over fifteen years. And others from this blessed progeny in Damascus, Syria, until this day. May Allah bless them, the righteous scholars, and their descendants, and all Muslims, until the Day of Judgment. (1) This information and what follows about the rest of the Āl al-Ghunaymī al-Maydānī family was taken from the internet.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to Shaykh ‘Abd al-Ghanī al-Maydānī, the commentator of al-Qudūrī’s Mukhtaṣar. The author begins by clarifying the term ‘sibt’ (grandson), noting that while it is commonly used for a daughter’s son, it can linguistically apply to any grandchild. He uses this to highlight that even the daughter’s son of Shaykh ‘Abd al-Ghanī is a student of knowledge, emphasizing the divine blessing of preserving knowledge in the scholar’s lineage. The passage then lists several descendants and relatives who were scholars or imams: Muḥammad ibn Adīb al-Ghunaymī, who copied a manuscript of the Shaykh’s work; an unnamed nephew also named ‘Abd al-Ghanī; Shaykh Musallam al-Ghunaymī, imam of a mosque in the al-Maydān district for over fifty years; and Shaykh Muḥammad al-Ghunaymī, imam and khatib of a mosque in al-Kiswah. The author also mentions his inability to determine the exact relationship of Shaykh Adīb al-Ghunaymī to the subject. The passage concludes with a supplication for blessings upon this family and all Muslims. This material serves as front matter, establishing the scholarly credentials and family background of the commentator.

Key Terms
السبط (al-sibṭ): Grandson, specifically the daughter's son, though linguistically used for any grandchild.
ترجمة (tarjamah): A biographical account or life sketch of a person.
الغنيمي (al-Ghunaymī): A family surname or nisba referring to the Ghunaym clan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Biographical introductions in Hanafi texts affirm the continuity of knowledge and the reliability of the author through their scholarly lineage.

Life of the Author

The Role of Scholarly Lineages in Hanafi Fiqh Transmission
Biographical notice of the author's righteous descendants

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how biographical notices of scholarly lineages establish the authority and chain of transmission of Hanafi fiqh texts.

Core Idea
Scholarly lineages ensure the reliable transmission of Hanafi fiqh across generations.

This passage from the introduction of 'Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri' may seem purely biographical, but it serves a crucial function in the Hanafi tradition: it establishes the chain of transmission (isnad) of the author's knowledge. By listing the author's righteous descendants who held religious posts, the text demonstrates that the author's fiqh is not merely theoretical but lived and taught by a blessed lineage. Understanding this helps us appreciate how Hanafi fiqh was preserved and passed down.

Guided Path
1
Identify the passage's purpose
Recognize that this is a biographical notice (tarjamah) at the beginning of a fiqh commentary. Its purpose is to establish the author's credibility and the reliability of his transmission.
Biographical notices are a standard feature in classical Hanafi texts, akin to the isnad in hadith.
2
Analyze the content: what is listed?
The passage mentions specific descendants: 'the khanqah in al-Maydan serving for over fifty years' and 'Sheikh Muhammad al-Ghunaimi who served as imam and khatib for over fifteen years.' These details highlight continuous service in teaching and leading prayer.
The specific locations (khanqah, mosque in Kiswa) show the geographical spread of Hanafi scholarship in Damascus.
3
Connect to fiqh transmission
Reflect on how this lineage ensures that the fiqh in the commentary is not just book knowledge but has been practiced and taught by reliable scholars who are connected to the author. This chain of transmission (isnad) adds authority to the rulings.
In Hanafi usul, the reliability of transmission is critical, especially for ahad hadith and the school's foundational texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني السخانة بحي الميدان، لمدة تزيد على خمسين عاماً. ومنهم الشيخ محمد الغنيمي، الذي تسلم إمامة وخطابة مسجد الكسوة جنوبي دمشق لمدة تزيد على خمسة عشر عاماً. وغير هؤلاء من هذه الذرية الطيبة في دمشق الشام إلى يومنا هذا، بارك الله فيهم، وفي العلماء العاملين، وفي ذراريهم والمسلمين أجمعين إلى يوم الدين.
Chapter One: Biography of the eminent scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. The khanqah in the al-Maydan neighborhood, for a period exceeding fifty years. Among them is Sheikh Muhammad al-Ghunaimi, who assumed the position of imam and khatib of the Masjid al-Kiswa south of Damascus for more than fifteen years. And besides these, from this righteous progeny in Damascus of Syria to this day, may Allah bless them, and the active scholars, and their descendants, and all Muslims until the Day of Judgment.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This is a biographical passage from the introduction of 'Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri' by Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. The author details the noble lineage of scholars from his family, highlighting their long service in religious posts. This establishes the scholarly pedigree and devotion of the author's family to Islamic learning and leadership.

Key Terms
الذرية الطيبة (al-dhurriyyah al-tayyibah): The righteous progeny/descendants of the author's family, who continued the scholarly tradition.
السخانة (al-sakhanah): A khanqah, a Sufi lodge that often also served as a center for teaching fiqh and other Islamic sciences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Biographical notices in Hanafi fiqh texts serve to authenticate the chain of transmission and establish the reliability of the author.

The Role of Scholarly Endorsements (Taqriz) in Hanafi Scholarship
Biographical praise and scholarly endorsement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the significance of taqriz in the Hanafi tradition and explain how it serves as a form of scholarly validation (tazkiyah) that affirms a scholar's reliability.

Core Idea
Taqriz is a formal scholarly endorsement that certifies a scholar's authority and the soundness of their work.

This passage from al-Maydani's biography highlights the widespread praise he received from his teachers, contemporaries, and students. Such endorsements (taqriz) are not mere compliments; they function as a formal attestation of a scholar's knowledge and character, a practice deeply rooted in the Hanafi tradition of preserving the chain of knowledge transmission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories of scholars who praised al-Maydani
List the groups: his teachers, scholars of his era, his peers, his students, and later biographers. Note the range shows his reputation was not limited to one group.
2
Examine the specific endorsement from al-Kuzbari
Note that al-Kuzbari is described as 'the hadith scholar of his age' and that his taqriz was for al-Maydani's Sharh al-Aqida al-Tahawiyya, written at age 34 — early in his career.
This shows that taqriz often highlights precocious achievement.
3
Understand the function of taqriz in the Hanafi scholarly tradition
Taqriz serves as a public validation of a scholar's reliability (tazkiyah), which is essential for establishing the authority of their works, especially in fiqh and usul.
It helps later students assess the weight of a scholar's opinions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث الثالث ثناءات العلماء عليه اجتمعت كلمة المترجمين للعلامة الميداني على الثناء العطر العالي عليه، في علمه وعمله ودينه وخلقه، وحاله عامة وخاصة. وقد جاءت هذه الثناءات المتعددة من كبار مشايخه، وعلماء عصره، بل من أخص أقرانه وأصدقائه ومحبيه، وهكذا من تلامذته والآخذين عنه، وكذلك ممـن جـاء بعـدهـم ممـن ذكـر الميداني أو ترجم له. وأذكر فيما يلي ما وقفت عليه من ذلك : ثناء شيخه الشيخ عبد الرحمن الكزبري : قال أستاذه شيخ عصره في الحديث الشيخ عبد الرحمن الكزبري، المتوفى سنة ١٢٦٢هـ، وذلك في تقريظه لكتاب الميداني : شرح العقيدة الطحاوية، والميداني قد انتهى من شرحه هذا وهو في ريعان شبابه، وله من العمر أربع وثلاثون سنة، وقد تضمن الثناء .1800(1)
Third Section: Praises of scholars upon him. The statements of the biographers of the eminent scholar al-Maydani agree on fragrant and high praise of him, regarding his knowledge, his action, his religion, his character, and his condition in general and in particular. These multiple praises came from his senior teachers, the scholars of his era, even from his closest peers, friends, and lovers, and likewise from his students and those who studied from him, and also from those who came after them who mentioned al-Maydani or wrote his biography. I will mention below what I have come across of that: The praise of his teacher Sheikh Abd al-Rahman al-Kuzbari: His teacher, the hadith scholar of his age, Sheikh Abd al-Rahman al-Kuzbari, died in 1262 AH, said in his endorsement of al-Maydani's book 'Sharh al-Aqida al-Tahawiyya' – and al-Maydani had completed this commentary while in the prime of his youth, at the age of thirty-four – and the praise included... [footnote]
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This is the third section of the biography, focusing on the praises scholars showered upon Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. The author emphasizes the unanimity and range of sources: teachers, contemporaries, students, and later biographers. He then specifically cites the endorsement of his teacher al-Kuzbari, noting that al-Maydani wrote a commentary on al-Tahawiyya at age 34, showing his early scholarly achievement.

Key Terms
تقريظ (taqrīẓ): A written endorsement or commendation of a book, often written by a senior scholar to certify its value and the author's competence.
ثناء (thanā'): Praise; in the context, refers to the scholarly praise and commendation of al-Maydani's knowledge, character, and works.

Key Takeaway
Scholarly endorsements (taqriz) from multiple independent sources are a vital part of the Hanafi tradition, serving to affirm a scholar's authority and the soundness of their works.

The Role of Taqriz in Hanafi Scholarship
Biographical praise establishing scholarly authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how a biographical taqriz establishes the scholarly authority of a Hanafi fiqh commentator and identify the key elements of scholarly praise in classical texts.

Core Idea
A taqriz by a master scholar validates a work's reliability and the author's place in the Hanafi tradition.

This passage is not a fiqh ruling but a biographical commendation (taqriz) from al-Maidani's teacher, al-Kuzbari. In the Hanafi tradition, such endorsements are crucial for establishing the credibility of a scholar and his commentaries. Understanding how to read these praises helps you assess the authority of the fiqh works you study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source and context of the praise
Who is giving the praise? Al-Kuzbari, a leading hadith scholar of his time. What work is being praised? Al-Maidani's commentary on al-'Aqida al-Tahawiyya, completed at age 34.
Note the age – early mastery indicates exceptional talent.
2
Extract the qualities praised
Al-Kuzbari praises both the book (splendid, reliable, based on authoritative sources) and the author (vast knowledge, intelligence, good character, piety). Identify each attribute from the text.
These qualities directly support al-Maidani's suitability as a Hanafi commentator.
3
Understand the function of taqriz
A taqriz serves to certify the work's orthodoxy and the author's competence. It connects the student to the chain of transmission and trust in the text.
In Hanafi fiqh, the reliability of the commentator impacts the weight of his legal opinions.
4
Connect the praise to fiqh authority
Al-Maidani is the author of the Lubab commentary on al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi text. The praise here reinforces his authority as a commentator on both creed and fiqh.
This lesson helps you appreciate why biographical sections matter for fiqh study.

المبحث الثالث
ثناءات العلماء عليه

اجتمعت كلمة المترجمين للعلامة الميداني على الثناء العطر العالي عليه، في علمه وعمله ودينه وخلقه، وحاله عامة وخاصة. وقد جاءت هذه الثناءات المتعددة من كبار مشايخه، وعلماء عصره، بل من أخص أقرانه وأصدقائه ومحبيه، وهكذا من تلامذته والآخذين عنه، وكذلك ممن جاء بعدهم ممن ذكر الميداني أو ترجم له.

وأذكر فيما يلي ما وقفت عليه من ذلك:

ثناء شيخه الشيخ عبد الرحمن الكزبري:

قال أستاذه شيخ عصره في الحديث الشيخ عبد الرحمن الكزبري، المتوفى سنة ١٢٦٢هـ، وذلك في تقريظه لكتاب الميداني: شرح العقيدة الطحاوية، والميداني قد انتهى من شرحه هذا وهو في ريعان شبابه، وله من العمر أربع وثلاثون سنة، وقد تضمن الثناء الكتاب وكاتبه، حيث قال رحمه الله:

..... أما بعد: فقد أحاط بَصَري بهذا الشرح، وسبرت إرقام هذا المدد الإلهي والفتح، الذي ألفه الفاضل النبيه، الذي قرت به عيون الفضل وذويه فارس ميدان العلم، وسابق جواد مُصَلِّي الذكاء والفهم: الشيخ عبد الغني الملقب بالغنيمي الميداني، كَسَاه الله حُلَلَ القبول والتهاني، فرأيتُه شرحاً في بابه بديعاً، وحصناً للعقائد الحقة منيعاً، لا نَقْدَ فيه فيما أظنُّ لأحد، بل كل ما حواه من مذاهب أئمة الدين هو المعتمد. رَصَّعَ فيه مؤلِّفُه جواهر الدرر، وأودعه حقائق غُرَرِ الغُرَر، مع نسبة كل يتيمة لأصلها، وتأدية كل أمانة إلى أهلها، وضم كل فريدة لمثلها، معولاً فيه على النقل عن أئمة هذا الشان، لتلقي قولهم بالقبول والإذعان.

وكلُّ ذلك دال على غزارة علمه، ونباهة ذكائه وفهمه، يقـول رائيه: كم ترك الأول للآخر، وفضله سبحانه وتعالى ليس له نهاية ولا آخر.

ولقد من الله على هذا الشارح فيما عَلِمْنا بكمال أدب، وحُسْنِ خلق، وتورع وتقوى بها إن شاء الله تعالى إلى المنازل العليَّة يرقى، وإنا لنرجو له فوق ذلك مظهراً، مع طول عمر، وحُسن عمل، ونفع للورى، وذلك بتاريخ (2) محرم، افتتاح سنة ١٢٥٧هـ). اهـ
The Third Section: Praises of the Scholars upon him
The statements of those who wrote about al-Allama al-Maidani have agreed upon lofty fragrant praise of him in his knowledge, actions, religion, character, and his state in general and in particular. These numerous praises have come from his senior teachers, scholars of his time, even from his most special peers, friends, and lovers, and likewise from his students and those who studied from him, as well as from those who came after them who mentioned al-Maidani or wrote his biography.

I will mention below what I have come across of that:

The praise of his teacher Sheikh Abd al-Rahman al-Kuzbari:

His teacher, the hadith scholar of his time, Sheikh Abd al-Rahman al-Kuzbari (died 1262 AH) said in his eulogy of al-Maidani's book 'Sharh al-‘Aqida al-Tahawiyya' – and al-Maidani had completed this commentary while in the prime of his youth, being thirty-four years old – and the eulogy included praise of the book and its author, where he said (may Allah have mercy on him):

... After praising Allah: My eyes have encompassed this commentary, and I have probed the inscriptions of this divine assistance and opening, which was authored by the excellent, intelligent one, by whom the eyes of virtue and its people are delighted, the knight of the field of knowledge, and the foremost champion, the performer of prayer of intelligence and understanding: Sheikh Abd al-Ghani, known as al-Ghunaymi al-Maidani – may Allah clothe him with the garments of acceptance and congratulations. I found it to be a commentary that is, in its field, splendid, and an impregnable fortress for the true creeds. There is no criticism in it, as far as I think, from anyone; rather, everything it contains of the doctrines of the imams of the religion is what is relied upon. Its author adorned it with pearls of jewels, and deposited in it the realities of the most brilliant beauties, while attributing each unique gem to its source, rendering every trust to its people, and joining each precious element with its like, relying therein on transmission from the imams of this art, receiving their statements with acceptance and submission.

And all of that indicates the abundance of his knowledge, the distinction of his intelligence and understanding. The beholder says: How much the first has left for the last! And His grace (glorified and exalted be He) has no end nor last.

And Allah has bestowed upon this commentator, as far as we know, complete manners, good character, piety, and God-consciousness by which, Allah willing, he will ascend to the highest stations. And we hope for him, beyond that, a high position, with long life, good deeds, and benefit to mankind. And this was on (2) Muharram, the opening of the year 1257 AH. End.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is a biographical tribute from the book's author (the commentator of al-Quduri) to Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani, originally part of the introduction to his commentary. The text presents a section on the praises of scholars for al-Maidani, focusing first on the eulogy of his own teacher, Sheikh Abd al-Rahman al-Kuzbari. Al-Kuzbari's praise is detailed and effusive, highlighting al-Maidani's early completion of his commentary on the ‘Aqida al-Tahawiyya at age 34, and lauding the commentary as free from error, relying on authoritative sources, and demonstrating the author's vast knowledge, intelligence, and moral excellence. The eulogy concludes with prayers for al-Maidani's continued success and beneficence. This serves to establish the credibility and scholarly standing of the author of this fiqh commentary (al-Maidani) for the reader.

Key Terms
ثناء (thana'): Praise or commendation, specifically the formal eulogy written by a teacher for a student's work.
تقريظ (taqriz): A written eulogy or commendation, often of a book or its author, as seen here from al-Kuzbari for al-Maidani's commentary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Role of Ijazah and Taqriz in Hanafi Scholarship
Biographical introduction with teacher praises

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the functions of taqriz and ijazah in establishing scholarly authority within the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Taqriz and ijazah authenticate a scholar's work and transmission rights in Hanafi tradition.

Classical Hanafi works often begin with biographical notices and commendations from esteemed teachers. This front matter serves not merely as decoration but as a formal validation of the author's learning and the reliability of his transmission. In this lesson, we examine the praise (taqriz) and license (ijazah) given to Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani by his teachers, and understand how these mechanisms function within the Hanafi scholarly tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of the biographical introduction
Recognize that the text opens with a chapter on the author's biography, establishing his scholarly credentials before the main content. This is a common feature of classical works.
2
Analyze the taqriz (commendation) from Sheikh Hasan al-Baytar
Read the praise carefully: it highlights the author's intellect, knowledge, and the quality of his commentary on the Tahawiyyah creed. Consider how such a commendation serves as an endorsement.
3
Examine the ijazah (license) from Ibn Abidin
Ibn Abidin, a towering figure in the late Hanafi school, granted an ijazah to al-Maidani after hearing Sahih al-Bukhari. This ijazah authorizes al-Maidani to transmit the hadith collection and implicitly endorses his scholarship.
4
Connect to the Hanafi tradition of scholarly authentication
Understand that ijazah and taqriz are not merely honorifics; they are formal mechanisms ensuring the continuity and reliability of knowledge transmission, critical in a tradition that values isnad (chain).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني
الكتاب وكاتبه، حيث قال رحمه الله :
.... أما بعد: فقد أحاط بَصَري بهذا الشرح، وسبرت إرقام هـذا المدد الإلهي والفتح، الذي ألفه الفاضل النبيه، الذي قرت بـه عـيـون الفضل وذويه فارس ميدان العلم، وسابق جواد مُصَلِّي الذكاء والفهم: الشيخ عبد الغني الملقب بالغنيمي الميداني، كَسَاه الله حُلَلَ القبول والتهاني، فرأيتُه شرحاً في بابه ،بديعاً، وحصناً للعقائد الحقة منيعاً، لا نَقْدَ فيه فيما أظنُّ لأحد ، بل كل ما حواه من مذاهب أئمـة المعتمد. الدين هو رَصَّعَ فيه مؤلِّفُه جواهر الدرر ، وأودعه حقائق غُرَرِ الغُرَر، مع نسبة كل يتيمة لأصلها، وتأدية كل أمانة إلى أهلها، وضم كل فريدة لمثلها، معولاً فيه على النقل عن أئمة هذا الشان، لتلقي قولهم بالقبول والإذعان.
وكلُّ ذلك دال على غزارة علمه، ونباهة ذكائه وفهمه، يقـول رائيه : كم ترك الأول للآخر، وفضله سبحانه وتعالى ليس له نهاية ولا آخر.
ولقد من الله على هذا الشارح فيما عَلِمْنا بكمال أدب، وحُسْنِ خلق، وتورع وتقوى بها إن شاء الله تعالى إلى المنازل العليَّة يرقى، وإنا لنرجو له فوق ذلك مظهراً، مع طول عمر، وحُسن عمل، ونفع للورى، وذلك بتاريخ (۲) محرم، افتتاح سنة ١٢٥٧هـ). اهـ

ثناء شيخه الشيخ حسن البيطار :
وقال العلامة الفقيه المحدث الشيخ حسن بن إبراهيم البيطار، المتوفى سنة ١٢٧٢هـ، في تقريظه لشرح الميداني على العقيدة الطحاوية :
..... ولم نَرَ أحداً شَرَحَها شرحاً يَحُلُ رموزها، ويستخرج كنوزها، ثم انتدب لذلك العالم الألمعي، والفاضل اللوذعي، ذو الفهم الثاقب، والرأي الصائب، مَجْمَعُ الكمالات واللطائف، ومشكاة أنوار الهداية والمعارف، القائم بحقوق أشياخه بالأدب التام، والحائز بنور رضاهم أعلى درجةٍ ومَقَام الشيخ عبد الغني الغنيمـي الميداني، بلغه الله الأماني، فشَرَحَها شرحاً حاوياً للتعليــل والدليل، خاوياً عن الحشو والتطويل. تحريراً في سنة ١٢٦١ هـ). اهـ

ثناء شيخه الشيخ ابن عابدين :
وقال العلامة الشيخ محمد أمين ابن عابدين، المتوفى سنة ١٢٥٢هـ، في إجازته لتلميذه الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني، ولزملائه الذين كانوا معه في قراءة صحيح الإمام البخاري، حين أجازهم به وبغيره، قال فيها مثنياً عليه في نظم بلغ (٢٦) بيتا :
هذا وإن جامع البخاري في الكتب صار مجمع الأبحار
أسمعته في أشهر قليلة جماعة ذوي حلى جميلـــة
Chapter One: Biography of the Allamah Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. The book and its author, where he (may Allah have mercy on him) said: ... 'To proceed: my sight has encompassed this commentary, and I have plumbed the depths of this divine outpouring and opening, which was authored by the intelligent and noble one, by whom the eyes of virtue and its people have been delighted, the knight of the field of knowledge, and the swift steed, the prayer hall of intelligence and understanding: Sheikh Abdul Ghani, nicknamed al-Ghanimi al-Maidani—may Allah clothe him in the garments of acceptance and congratulations. I saw it as a commentary that is, in its field, innovative, and an impregnable fortress for true beliefs; I do not think anyone can find fault with it. Rather, everything it contains from the doctrines of the relied-upon imams of the religion is such that its author has set therein the jewels of pearls, and lodged the truths of the choicest gems, while attributing every orphaned idea to its origin, fulfilling every trust to its people, and combining every unique gem with its like, relying therein on transmission from the imams of this art, to receive their statements with acceptance and submission. All of this indicates the abundance of his knowledge, the eminence of his intelligence and understanding. The beholder says: How much the first left for the last, and His grace—glorified and exalted is He—has no end nor finality. And Allah has bestowed upon this commentator, as far as we know, perfect courtesy, good character, piety, and righteousness, by which, Allah willing, he shall ascend to the highest stations. We hope for him, above that, a manifestation, with long life, good deeds, and benefit to creation, and that is dated (2) Muharram, the beginning of the year 1257 AH.' End.

Praise of his teacher Sheikh Hasan al-Baytar:
And the Allamah, the Faqih, the Muhaddith, Sheikh Hasan ibn Ibrahim al-Baytar, died 1272 AH, said in his commendation of al-Maidani's commentary on al-‘Aqidah al-Tahawiyyah: '...We have not seen anyone who explained it with an explanation that unties its symbols and extracts its treasures. Then for that task arose the brilliant scholar, the subtle virtuoso, of penetrating understanding and correct opinion, the assembly of perfections and subtleties, the lamp of the lights of guidance and sciences, the one who fulfills the rights of his elders with complete courtesy, and by the light of their pleasure attains the highest rank and station: Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maidani—may Allah grant him his hopes. So he explained it with an explanation containing reasoning and evidence, free from filler and prolixity. Written in the year 1261 AH.' End.

Praise of his teacher Sheikh Ibn Abidin:
And the Allamah Sheikh Muhammad Amin Ibn Abidin, died 1252 AH, said in his license (ijazah) to his student Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani and his colleagues who were with him in reading Sahih al-Imam al-Bukhari, when he licensed them with it and other things, he said therein praising him in a poem of (26) verses: 'This: Indeed the compendium of al-Bukhari among books has become a gathering of seas. I made it heard in a few months to a group of people of beautiful adornment.'
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to the book and its author, Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. It begins with a statement from the author himself (or perhaps from a writer of the introduction) praising the commentary and its author. The language is highly laudatory, describing the commentary as innovative and robust in defending true beliefs. The author is credited with thorough research, attributing each point to its source. The passage then presents praise from two of al-Maidani's teachers: Sheikh Hasan al-Baytar and the eminent Hanafi jurist Ibn Abidin. Al-Baytar commends al-Maidani's commentary on the Tahawiyyah creed for its clarity and use of evidence. Ibn Abidin, in his ijazah, praises al-Maidani and his companions for their study of Sahih al-Bukhari. This section is purely biographical and serves to establish the scholarly credentials of the author, which is typical in the front matter of classical works. The dates provided (1257, 1261, 1272 AH) give historical context. Note that the author's death year is not given here, but he is later known as al-Maidani.

Key Terms
تقريظ (taqrīẓ): A written commendation or praise of a work by a respected scholar.
إجازة (ijāzah): A license or permission granted by a scholar to a student to transmit a specific text or body of knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi tradition, scholarly endorsements like taqriz and ijazah serve to authenticate the author's knowledge and ensure the continuity of reliable transmission.

Praise of Sheikh Hasan al-Baytar
Commendation by teacher al-Baytar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the commendation of Sheikh Hasan al-Baytar and explain how it establishes al-Maydani's scholarly authority.

Core Idea
A scholar's authority is validated by the praise of his teachers.

Biographical entries (tarjama) serve an important function in the Hanafi tradition: they establish the credentials of an author whose works we study. In this passage, we see the commendation of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani by his teacher Sheikh Hasan al-Baytar, who praises his commentary on al-Aqida al-Tahawiyya as comprehensive and clear.

Guided Path
1
Identify the teacher and his qualifications
Note that Sheikh Hasan al-Baytar (d. 1272 AH) is described as a scholar, jurist, and hadith expert. His own credentials add weight to his praise.
2
Extract the specific qualities praised
Al-Baytar says al-Maydani is a 'brilliant scholar' (al-ʿālim al-almaʿī), with 'sharp understanding' and 'correct opinion', and that his commentary 'encompasses reasoning and evidence' and is free of redundancy.
3
Connect the praise to the teacher's authority
Because al-Baytar is a recognized authority, his commendation serves as a type of informal ijaza, confirming that al-Maydani's work is reliable.
4
Reflect on significance for studying al-Maydani's works
This praise assures students that al-Maydani's commentary (and by extension his other works like al-Lubab) are based on sound scholarship and reliable transmission.

الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني
ثناء شيخه الشيخ حسن البيطار :
وقال العلامة الفقيه المحدث الشيخ حسن بن إبراهيم البيطار، المتوفى سنة ١٢٧٢هـ، في تقريظه لشرح الميداني على العقيدة الطحاوية :
..... ولم نَرَ أحداً شَرَحَها شرحاً يَحُلُ رموزها، ويستخرج كنوزها، ثم انتدب لذلك العالم الألمعي، والفاضل اللوذعي، ذو الفهم الثاقب، والرأي الصائب، مَجْمَعُ الكمالات واللطائف، ومشكاة أنوار الهداية والمعارف، القائم بحقوق أشياخه بالأدب التام، والحائز بنور رضاهم أعلى درجةٍ ومَقَام الشيخ عبد الغني الغنيمـي الميداني، بلغه الله الأماني، فشَرَحَها شرحاً حاوياً للتعليــل والدليل، خاوياً عن الحشو والتطويل. تحريراً في سنة ١٢٦١ هـ). اهـ

وقال العلامة الشيخ محمد أمين ابن عابدين، المتوفى سنة ١٢٥٢هـ، في إجازته لتلميذه الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني، ولزملائه الذين كانوا معه في قراءة صحيح الإمام البخاري، حين أجازهم به وبغيره، قال فيها مثنياً عليه في نظم بلغ (٢٦) بيتا :
هذا وإن جامع البخاري في الكتب صار مجمع الأبحار
أسمعته في أشهر قليلة جماعة ذوي حلى جميلـــة
محمد الجابي ذو المفاخر وابنُ الخُلاصي الشهم عبد القادِرِ
عبد الغني فارس الميدان واللوذعي محمد الحلواني) (۱). اهـ فقد لقبه هنا : بـ (فارس) الميدان) ، وابن عابدين أدرى به ، بل كان يُلقبه بهذا دائماً، كما نقل هذا عنه مفتي سوريا السابق العلامة الشيخ أبو اليسر عابدين (١٣٠٧ هـ ـ ١٤٠١هـ) قال : «كان الشيخ محمد أمين عابدين يقول عندما يأتي الغنيمي لحضور درسه: جـاء فـارس الميدان»(۲).
* ثناء شيخه الشيخ حامد العطار :
ومن تلك الثناءات ما كتبه العلامة الفقيه الشيخ العطار، المتوفى سنة ١٢٦٢هـ، وذلك في تقريظه لشرح الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني على العقيدة الطحاوية، حيث قال: .... أما بعد : فإني قد اطلعت على هذا الشرح الذي ألفه الفاضل الأديب، والبارع الذكي اللبيب الشيخ عبد الغني الغنيمي، الشهير بالميداني، بلغه الله ما يرجوه من الأماني.... فرأيته شرحاً لطيفاً، محتوياً على درر الفوائد، جامعاً لزبدة ما اتفق عليـه أهـل العقائد، فاتحاً لمُغلقها، وموضحاً لمشكلها.... تحريراً في غرة شهر ربيع
The First Chapter: The Biography of the Scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani
Praise of his teacher Sheikh Hasan al-Baytar:
The scholar, jurist, and hadith expert Sheikh Hasan ibn Ibrahim al-Baytar, who died in 1272 AH, said in his commendation of al-Maydani's commentary on al-Aqida al-Tahawiyya: "...We have not seen anyone who explained it with an explanation that solves its symbols and extracts its treasures. Then this brilliant scholar, the distinguished virtuoso, possessing sharp understanding and correct opinion, the gathering of perfections and subtleties, the lamp of the lights of guidance and knowledge, fulfilling the rights of his teachers with complete etiquette, attaining the highest rank and station by the light of their pleasure, Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maydani—may Allah fulfill his hopes—undertook it; he explained it with an explanation encompassing reasoning and evidence, free of redundancy and prolixity. Written in the year 1261 AH."
Praise of his teacher Sheikh Ibn Abidin:
The scholar Sheikh Muhammad Amin Ibn Abidin, who died in 1252 AH, said in his authorization (ijaza) to his student Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani and his colleagues who were with him in reading Sahih al-Bukhari, when he authorized them with it and other things, he said in praise of him in a poem of twenty-six verses: "This, and indeed the collection of al-Bukhari among books became a meeting place of seas. I made it heard to a group adorned with beautiful qualities: Muhammad al-Jabi, possessor of virtues; and Ibn al-Khulasi, the noble, Abdul Qadir; Abd al-Ghani, the knight of the field; and the clever, Muhammad al-Halwani." Thus he titled him here: 'the knight of the field'—and Ibn Abidin knew him best; indeed he always called him by this title. As the former Mufti of Syria, the scholar Sheikh Abu al-Yusr Abidin (1307-1401 AH) reported: 'Sheikh Muhammad Amin Abidin used to say when al-Ghanimi came to attend his lesson: The knight of the field has come.'
Praise of his teacher Sheikh Hamid al-Attar:
Among those praises is what the scholar and jurist Sheikh al-Attar, who died in 1262 AH, wrote in his commendation of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani's commentary on al-Aqida al-Tahawiyya, where he said: "To proceed: I have reviewed this commentary authored by the virtuous, literary, clever, intelligent, brilliant scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Ghanimi, known as al-Maydani—may Allah grant him what he hopes of aspirations. I found it a refined commentary, containing unique benefits, comprehensive of the essence of what the people of creeds agree upon, opening what is closed, and clarifying what is problematic... Written at the beginning of the month of Rabi'..."
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section (tarjama) presenting the scholarly credentials of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani through the commendations of three of his teachers. Each teacher praises his commentary on al-Tahawiyya (a classic work of Islamic creed) and highlights his outstanding qualities. The first, Sheikh Hasan al-Baytar, lauds his deep understanding and ability to elucidate difficult points. The second, the famous Hanafi jurist Ibn Abidin, calls him 'knight of the field' (Faris al-Maydan), a nickname that stuck. The third, Sheikh Hamid al-Attar, praises his commentary as comprehensive and clear. This establishes al-Maydani's reliability and expertise, adding weight to his own works, such as the commentary on al-Quduri (al-Lubab) that this book is introducing.

Key Terms
ترجمة (tarjama): A biographical entry providing information about a scholar's life and accomplishments.
إجازة (ijaza): A license or authorization given by a teacher to a student to transmit a text or body of knowledge.
شيخ (shaykh): A teacher or mentor, often a senior scholar qualified to teach and authorize students.
ميداني (Maydani): Al-Maydani is a nisba (surname) indicating origin from a place called al-Maydan in Damascus. It also became a personal nickname associated with the phrase 'Faris al-Maydan' (knight of the field) from Ibn Abidin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which teacher praised al-Maydani's commentary for 'encompassing reasoning and evidence, free of redundancy'?
A) Sheikh Hasan al-Baytar
B) Sheikh Ibn Abidin
C) Sheikh Hamid al-Attar
D) Sheikh Abu al-Yusr Abidin

Key Takeaway
Teacher commendations in a tarjama serve as informal endorsements that validate a scholar's authority.

Praise of Sheikh Ibn Abidin and the Epithet 'Knight of the Field'
Commendation by Ibn Abidin with the epithet

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the praise of Ibn Abidin, state the nickname 'Faris al-Maydan', and explain its significance.

Core Idea
Ibn Abidin, the great Hanafi jurist, called al-Maydani 'knight of the field'—a lasting mark of honor.

The praise of Sheikh Muhammad Amin Ibn Abidin carries special weight because he is one of the most authoritative later Hanafi jurists. In his ijaza poem, he calls al-Maydani 'Faris al-Maydan' (knight of the field), a nickname that stuck and indicates his high standing in the field of fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the teacher and his standing
Ibn Abidin (d. 1252 AH) is a pivotal figure in the later Hanafi school, known for his supercommentary Radd al-Muhtar. His endorsement is highly respected.
2
Extract the specific praise from the poem
In a poem of 26 verses, Ibn Abidin lists the students who studied Sahih al-Bukhari with him, and calls al-Maydani: 'Abd al-Ghani, the knight of the field'.
3
Understand the anecdote reported by Abu al-Yusr Abidin
The passage adds that Ibn Abidin always called al-Maydani 'knight of the field', and would say, 'the knight of the field has come', when al-Maydani arrived for class.
4
Reflect on the significance of the nickname
A nickname from a master jurist indicates that al-Maydani was considered a champion in the field of fiqh, ranking high among his peers.

Praise of his teacher Sheikh Hasan al-Baytar:

Praise of Sheikh Hamid al-Attar
Commendation by teacher al-Attar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the commendation of Sheikh Hamid al-Attar and explain the qualities he highlighted in al-Maydani's commentary.

Core Idea
Sheikh Hamid al-Attar praised al-Maydani's commentary as 'refined, comprehensive, and clarifying' — a mark of its scholarly value.

The third commendation comes from Sheikh Hamid al-Attar (d. 1262 AH), another teacher of al-Maydani. In his taqrīẓ, he praises al-Maydani's commentary on al-Aqida al-Tahawiyya as 'laden with unique benefits' and 'comprehensive of the essence of the agreed-upon creed'. This further solidifies al-Maydani's reputation as a meticulous commentator.

Guided Path
1
Identify the teacher and his field
Sheikh Hamid al-Attar is described as a scholar and jurist. He died in 1262 AH, and his commendation is part of the same tradition of teacher endorsements.
2
Extract the specific merits praised
Al-Attar says the commentary is 'refined' (sharḥ laṭīf), contains 'unique benefits', 'comprehensive of the essence of what the people of creeds agree upon', and 'opens what is closed and clarifies what is problematic'.
3
Connect to the teacher's authority
Al-Attar is a recognized scholar; his endorsement adds to the chorus of approval from multiple teachers, reinforcing al-Maydani's reliability.
4
Reflect on the overall weight of multiple commendations
Having three teachers independently praise al-Maydani's work shows that his scholarship was widely recognized, making his later works (like al-Lubab) highly credible.

D) 'free of redundancy and prolixity'

Key Takeaway
Al-Attar's praise confirms the comprehensive and clarifying nature of al-Maydani's commentary, adding to his scholarly credibility.

The Biography of Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani and Scholarly Endorsements
Biographical introduction with scholarly endorsements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the role of taqriz (scholarly endorsements) in Hanafi scholarship and identify the key figures who praised al-Maydani.

Core Idea
Scholarly endorsements (taqriz) establish a scholar's authority and the reliability of his works.

Before diving into a fiqh text, it is essential to understand the author's credentials. This passage provides a biography of Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, including his nickname and two endorsements from prominent scholars. These endorsements not only praise the author but also serve to authenticate his scholarship, a common practice in Islamic tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his nickname
Read the opening lines to find the author's full name and the epithet 'Faris al-Maydan' (Knight of the Field). Note who used this nickname and why it is significant.
The nickname indicates mastery in his field, akin to a champion.
2
Recognize the role of Ibn Abidin's testimony
Ibn Abidin, a major Hanafi authority, is reported to have used the title routinely. This connection boosts al-Maydani's credibility.
Ibn Abidin's opinion carries weight in the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the first taqriz by Shaykh Hamid al-Attar
Read al-Attar's endorsement and identify what he praises: the commentary's comprehensiveness, clarity, and utility.
This taqriz is from al-Maydani's teacher, adding a layer of credibility.
4
Analyze the second taqriz by Shaykh Abd al-Rahman al-Taybi
Notice that al-Taybi is a Shafi'i scholar, which shows cross-madhhab recognition. He compares al-Maydani to al-Sanusi, emphasizing his youth and excellence.
Cross-madhhab praise enhances the author's reputation beyond his own school.
5
Synthesize the significance of taqriz
Understand that taqriz function as a certification of a work's value and the author's competence, similar to modern peer review.
This practice helps students choose reliable texts.

* ثناء شيخه الشيخ حامد العطار :

ومن تلك الثناءات ما كتبه العلامة الفقيه الشيخ العطار، المتوفى سنة ١٢٦٢هـ، وذلك في تقريظه لشرح الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني على العقيدة الطحاوية، حيث قال: .... أما بعد : فإني قد اطلعت على هذا الشرح الذي ألفه الفاضل الأديب، والبارع الذكي اللبيب الشيخ عبد الغني الغنيمي، الشهير بالميداني، بلغه الله ما يرجوه من الأماني.... فرأيته شرحاً لطيفاً، محتوياً على درر الفوائد، جامعاً لزبدة ما اتفق عليـه أهـل العقائد، فاتحاً لمُغلقها، وموضحاً لمشكلها.... تحريراً في غرة شهر ربيع الأنور، سنة ١٢٥٩هـ). اهـ
ثناء الشيخ عبد الرحمن الطيبي :
وقال العلامة الشيخ عبد الرحمن بن علي الطيبي الشافعي، المتوفى سنة ١٢٦٤هـ، مقرظـاً لشرح الميداني على العقيدة الطحاوية :
.... أما بعد : فإن الله تعالى لما أوجب علينا معرفة بعض صفاته تفصيلاً، قيَّض لتحريرها جَحَاجحة (١) سَراةً، فحرروها بأدلتها الواضحة المنتقاة، ...، وكان ممن انتظم في سلك هذه اللآلي العِظام : سنوسي هذه الأعوام المولى التحرير الهمام، نادرة هذه الأيام، الحاج الشيخ عبد الغني الغنيمي الميداني، الذي ليس له في زماننا من ثاني بلغه الله غاية الأماني، ونفع به القاصي والداني، وأجرى قلمه بما فيه ألطف المعاني، فشرح العقيدة النافعة الطحاوية، وأشاد منها المباني، شرحاً لطيفاً أظهر فيه ما خفي من المعاني. وهو مع صغر سنه (۲) فاق أهل زمانه، وأضحى كأنـه سنوسي أوانه، فلا زال قلمه جارياً بما ينفع العباد ، ويهديهم سبيل الرشاد...». اهـ
Chapter One: Biography of the Scholar Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani
Muhammad al-Jabi, possessor of virtues, and Ibn al-Khulasi, the valiant, Abd al-Qadir, Abd al-Ghani, the knight of the field, and the clever Muhammad al-Halwani. End quote. So he titled him here as 'knight of the field (faris al-maydan)'. Ibn Abidin knew him better; indeed, he always used to address him with this title, as narrated from him by the former Mufti of Syria, the scholar Shaykh Abu al-Yusr Abidin (1307 AH – 1401 AH) who said: 'Shaykh Muhammad Amin Abidin used to say when al-Ghanimi came to attend his lesson: The knight of the field has come.'
* Praise from his teacher Shaykh Hamid al-Attar:
Hamid ibn Ahmad
Among those praises is what was written by the scholar jurist Shaykh al-Attar, died in 1262 AH, in his endorsement of the commentary of Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani on al-Aqida al-Tahawiyya, where he said: '... To proceed: I have examined this commentary authored by the virtuous, literary, brilliant, intelligent, sagacious Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Ghanimi, known as al-Maydani. May Allah grant him his aspirations... I found it a refined commentary, containing pearls of benefits, encompassing the essence of what the people of doctrines agreed upon, opening what was closed, and clarifying what was problematic... Written at the beginning of the month of Rabi al-Anwar, in the year 1259 AH.' End quote.
Praise from Shaykh Abd al-Rahman al-Taybi:
The scholar Shaykh Abd al-Rahman ibn Ali al-Taybi al-Shafi'i, died in 1264 AH, said in endorsement of al-Maydani's commentary on al-Aqida al-Tahawiyya:
'... To proceed: When Allah Almighty obligated upon us the detailed knowledge of some of His attributes, He appointed for their formulation senior leaders, so they formulated them with their clear, selected proofs... Among those who joined the string of these great pearls was the Sanusi of these times, the distinguished author, the rare one of these days, al-Hajj Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maydani, who has no second in our time. May Allah grant him the utmost aspirations, benefit by him the near and far, and make his pen flow with the most subtle meanings. He commented on the beneficial Aqida al-Tahawiyya and raised its structures, a refined commentary in which he manifested hidden meanings. Despite his young age (2), he surpassed the people of his time, and became as if the Sanusi of his era. May his pen always flow with what benefits the servants and guides them to the path of rectification...' End quote.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section from the beginning of the book, providing an account of the author Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. It opens with a quote that includes several names and epithets, among them 'faris al-maydan' (knight of the field), which appears to be a nickname given by his teacher or contemporaries. The text then reports that Ibn Abidin (a famous Hanafi jurist) used to refer to al-Maydani with this title, confirming its usage. Next, the passage records two scholarly praises (taqriz) for al-Maydani's commentary on al-Aqida al-Tahawiyya. The first is from his teacher Shaykh Hamid al-Attar, who praises the commentary as refined, comprehensive, and clarifying difficult points. The second praise is from Shaykh Abd al-Rahman al-Taybi, a Shafi'i scholar, who likens al-Maydani to the renowned scholar al-Sanusi, emphasizing that despite his youth (34 years old at the time), al-Maydani surpassed his contemporaries. These endorsements establish the author's scholarly standing and the value of his works. The tone is reverential, characteristic of biographical entries in traditional Islamic texts. This passage serves as front matter, introducing the author's credentials to the reader.

Key Terms
فارس الميدان (faris al-maydan): A title meaning 'knight of the field', used as a nickname for the author, implying mastery in his field.
الغنيمي (al-Ghanimi): A surname or nisba referring to the author, possibly indicating his lineage or origin.
تقريظ (taqriz): A commendatory endorsement or preface written by a scholar praising a book or its author.

Biographical Introduction of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani: Contemporary Praises and Scholarly Standing
Biographical introduction with contemporary scholarly praises

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key elements of a Hanafi scholar's biography through contemporary scholarly praises and evaluate its significance for the madhhab.

Core Idea
A scholar's standing is affirmed by the recognition of peers from other madhhabs, as seen in the praises of al-Maidani.

Biographical introductions are essential in the Hanafi tradition for establishing scholarly authority. This passage presents praises from three scholars—one Shafi'i, one Naqshbandi, and one Hanafi—all commending Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani's commentary on the 'Aqida al-Tahawiyya. By analyzing these encomiums, you will understand how the Hanafi school values external validation and how such recognition solidifies a scholar's place in the tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the biographee and his work
The text focuses on Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani and his commentary on the 'Aqida al-Tahawiyya. Note the title of his work and its significance as a core theological text in the Hanafi tradition.
The 'Aqida al-Tahawiyya is a foundational creed text accepted by multiple Sunni schools.
2
Identify each praising scholar and his madhhab
Three scholars are quoted: al-Tayyibi (Shafi'i), al-Khani (Naqshbandi), and al-Khalasi (Hanafi, student of Ibn Abidin). Note their backgrounds and why their praise carries weight.
Al-Tayyibi being Shafi'i indicates recognition beyond the Hanafi madhhab.
3
Analyze the content of the praise
Look for key phrases: al-Tayyibi calls him 'nadirah hadhihi al-ayyam' (rare one of this age); al-Khani describes him as 'al-ālim al-āmil' (the knowledgeable and practicing scholar); al-Khalasi mentions his service to Ibn Abidin during Hajj. These highlight his intellect, piety, and connection to the Hanafi chain.
Such praises establish both his knowledge and his spiritual lineage.
4
Reflect on the significance for the Hanafi tradition
The praise from a Shafi'i shows broad acceptance; the Naqshbandi connection indicates integration with Sufi traditions; the Hanafi praise from a student of Ibn Abidin places him in the direct line of Hanafi authority.
This multi-dimensional recognition strengthens his reliability as a transmitter of Hanafi fiqh.
