The Ijazah System: Ibn Abidin's Poetic License for Four Students
Biographical preface with poetic ijazah excerpt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the function of ijazah in Hanafi hadith transmission and identify the key elements of Ibn Abidin's poetic ijazah as a model of scholarly authorization.

Core Idea
Ibn Abidin's 26-verse ijazah immortalizes four students, proving that scholarly transmission depends on a living chain (isnad).

This biographical passage from al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri introduces the author Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani by recounting how his teacher Ibn Abidin granted a remarkable ijazah – a poem – to four select students. The passage illustrates the high value placed on personal transmission (samā') and written authorization (ijāzah) in the Hanafi tradition, where the chain of teachers matters as much as the content. Understanding this context helps appreciate the authority of classical Hanafi texts and the importance of isnad in preserving knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of the poem
Read the first few lines of the poem to determine what Ibn Abidin is doing. He is granting permission (ijazah) to transmit Sahih al-Bukhari and his other narrations to four specific students.
The poem functions as a formal authorization, not just a praise.
2
List the four students and their epithets
Extract the names and descriptive phrases: Muhammad al-Jabi (possessor of virtues), Abd al-Qadir ibn al-Khulasī (the brave), Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani (knight of the field), Muhammad al-Halwani (the clever).
Each title hints at the student's character or scholarly rank.
3
Examine Ibn Abidin's humility and conditions
Note that Ibn Abidin states 'I am not worthy to grant ijazah' and mentions his own teachers (Ibn al-Kuzbari, Ahmad al-Attar, Shakir al-Aqqad). This shows that the authority comes from the chain, not the individual, and humility is a scholarly virtue.
He emphasizes that his ijazah is based on his own received permissions.
4
Understand the thabat and musalsalat
Ibn Abidin refers to a thabat he compiled containing his teachers' chains and musalsalat. The thabat is a formal record that serves as the basis for further transmission.
A thabat is a crucial biographical tool for verifying a scholar's credentials.
5
Reflect on the wisdom of selection
After Ibn Abidin's death, it became clear that only these four students attained prominence. This demonstrates that the selection was divinely guided and underscores the importance of direct mentorship in the Hanafi tradition.
The passage implies that ijazah is not just ceremonial but reflects genuine scholarly caliber.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني

وكان ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى وقدس سره، فَعَلَ شيئاً في حال حياته، وهو أنه اختار من تلامذته أربعة أشخاص، وأسمعهم صحيح البخاري في مدة قليلة وأجازهم فيه، وفي سائر مروياته وأنشأ إجازة نظماً ، وذَكَرَ فيها أسماء الأربع، وقد أوْجَزَ وبالغ وأبدع، وهي في ستة وعشرين بيتاً، قال فيها:

باسم الإله الواحد المجيد ذي الفضل والإنعام والتمجيد
ثم الصلاة والسلام السرمدي على النبي المصطفى محمد
وآله وصحبه الأطهار و مسند الآثار والخيار
وبعد فالحديث أشـرف الـذي يقصده كل امرىء ويحتذي
لكن مَن يَطلبه بلا سَنَد كحاطب ليل فليس يُعتمد
هذا وإن جامع البخاري في الكتب صار مجمع الأبحارِ
قد فاقها في الضبط والتصحيح في مذهب المعتمد الرجيح
أسمعته في أشهر قليلــــة جماعة ذوي حلى جميلة
محمد الجابي ذو المفاخر وابنُ الخُلاصي الشهم عبد القادر
عبد الغني فارس الميدان واللوذعـي محمـــد الحـلـــوانـي
ثم أرادوا أن أُجيـــــزهــم بمـــــا قد سمعوا وغيره معمماً
مع أنني لست بأهل أن أُجاز ولا من الطريق في ذاك المجاز
فقلت قد أجزتُهم بكل ما رويته عن الشيوخ الكرما
کشیخنا المحدث المعمر محمد الشهير بابن الكزبري
وحافظ الوقت الشهاب الساري شيخ الشيوخ أحمد العطار
وشاكر العقاد من ربَّاني وبحلِي دُرِّه حَلاني
وكنت قد جمعت في حياته ثبتــا حـــوى جميـع مروياتــه
شعبتُ فيه سند الشيوخ إلى شيوخهم ذوي الرسوخ
وفيه ذكر معظم الأثبات وجملة من المسلسلات
وكتب السنة والعلــــوم عن غيره يكفي ذوي الفهوم
وقد أجزتُهم بما فيه وما بــه علــي الله قــــد تكرمــــا
من الشروح الغُـر والرسائل ومن حواشــي الــدر والمسائل
وما به الإله بعده يَمُن علي في مستقبل من الزمن
بشرطه المعروف عند أهله والضبط في إملائــه ونقله
مع الدعاء لي بحسن الخاتمة والعفو والغفران في يوم الكاظمة
فإنني محمد بن عابدين أرجو من الله القبول كـل حـين

ثم قال الخلاصي عقبها :
وقد ظهرت حكمة تخصيصه لهؤلاء الأربعة بعد وفاته، وهي أنـه لم تَظْهَر مزيةٌ لتلامذته إلا لمن ذكره في النظم.
أما أحد الأربعة، وهو محمد أفندي ابن السيد عثمان الجابي... وأما ثالث الأربعة، الذي لقبه شيخنا رحمه الله تعالى بـ (فارس الميدان)، بل فارس البلدان المتصدي للقاء الأقران في مقام العرفان، الذي حاز قصبات السبق، ولم يسبقه إليها أحد في دمشق،
Chapter One: Biography of the scholar Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani

Ibn Abidin (may Allah have mercy on him and sanctify his spirit) did something during his life: he selected four of his students, had them listen to Sahih al-Bukhari in a short period, granted them ijazah in it and in all his other narrations, and composed an ijazah in verse, mentioning the names of the four. He was concise, eloquent, and innovative; it consists of 26 verses, in which he said:

In the name of the One Majestic God, possessor of bounty, grace, and glorification. Then eternal prayers and peace upon the chosen Prophet Muhammad, his family, his pure Companions, the chain of transmissions, and the best. After that, hadith is the most honorable thing that every person seeks and follows. But whoever seeks it without a chain is like a wood-gatherer at night, not reliable. This work, and indeed the collection of al-Bukhari among books, has become an ocean of seas; it surpassed them in precision and authentication according to the preferred authoritative school. I made it heard in a few months to a group of beautiful qualities: Muhammad al-Jabi, possessor of virtues; Ibn al-Khulasī, the brave Abd al-Qadir; Abd al-Ghani, the knight of the field; and the clever Muhammad al-Halwani. Then they wanted me to grant them ijazah for what they heard and more, comprehensively, even though I am not worthy to grant ijazah nor am I upon the path in that authorization. So I said: I have granted them ijazah for everything I narrated from the generous shaykhs, like our shaykh, the muḥaddith, the aged Muhammad known as Ibn al-Kuzbari, and the guardian of time, the shining star, shaykh of shaykhs Ahmad al-Attar, and Shakir al-Aqqad, a rabbani, and with my tears of pearls he adorned me. I had compiled during his life a thabat containing all his narrations; in it I branched the chain of shaykhs to their firmly rooted shaykhs. It contains mention of most thabats and a number of musalsalat, and books of Sunnah and sciences enough for people of understanding. I have granted them ijazah for what is in it and what Allah may grace me with later from the radiant commentaries, treatises, and glosses of al-Durr and legal issues, and what Allah may bestow upon me in the future, under its condition known to its people, and precision in its dictation and transcription, along with prayer for me for a good end and pardon and forgiveness on the Day of Calamity. For I am Muhammad ibn Abidin, hoping for acceptance from Allah all the time.

Then al-Khulasī said after it: The wisdom of his specifying these four became evident after his death, namely that no distinction appeared among his students except for those he mentioned in the poem. As for one of the four, Muhammad Afandi ibn al-Sayyid Uthman al-Jabi... and as for the third of the four, whom our shaykh (may Allah have mercy on him) called 'the knight of the field,' rather the knight of the lands, the one who encounters peers in the station of gnosis, who attained the foremost marks and none preceded him in Damascus...
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a biographical excerpt from al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. It introduces the author, Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, and recounts a notable event from his teacher Ibn Abidin's life. Ibn Abidin selected four outstanding students and orally transmitted Sahih al-Bukhari to them along with his other narrations, then composed a 26-verse poem granting them formal ijazah. The verses include the names of the four: Muhammad al-Jabi, Abd al-Qadir ibn al-Khulasī, Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani (the author himself), and Muhammad al-Halwani. Ibn Abidin humbly expresses his unworthiness but invokes his teachers' chains. After Ibn Abidin's death, it became clear that this selection was divinely guided, as only those mentioned in the poem attained prominence. The commentary then elaborates on the third student, Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, praising his scholarly rank. This section serves as a biographical preface, establishing the author's credentials and his teacher's legacy.

Key Terms
إجازة (ijazah): A license or authorization to transmit hadith or a specific text, granted by a teacher to a student after verifying their competence.
ثبت (thabat): A compiled list of a scholar's teachers, narrations, and written works, often used as a reference for ijazah.
مسلسلات (musalsalat): Hadith that have a continuous chain of narrators sharing a specific characteristic, such as all being Hanafi or all using a particular phrase.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did Ibn Abidin do for the four students mentioned in the poem?
A) He wrote a commentary for them.
B) He made them listen to Sahih al-Bukhari and granted them ijazah.
C) He appointed them as qadis.
D) He taught them only the Qur'an.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Abidin's poetic ijazah encapsulates the essence of Hanafi transmission: personal connection, authenticated chains, and humble authorization.

Biography of Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani: Authority in Hanafi Tradition
Biographical excerpts praising the scholar Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani as a mystic and jurist.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical elements used to establish a Hanafi scholar's authority and explain their significance in the tradition.

Core Idea
A Hanafi scholar’s authority is built on isnad, spiritual cultivation, and community service — not just knowledge.

This passage introduces the life of Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, the author of al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri. In Hanafi tradition, biographical entries authenticate the author's chain of learning, his spiritual stature, and his practical role as a mufti. Understanding these elements helps you assess the weight of a scholar’s rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the narrators and chain
Look for the individuals who praise al-Maydani: Muhammad ibn Abidin, al-Khalasi, and Abd al-Razzaq al-Baytar. Note their relationship to him (teacher, commentator, friend).
Ibn Abidin is a later Hanafi authority; his praise carries weight.
2
Note the titles and epithets
Al-Maydani is called 'Faris al-Maydan' (Knight of the Field) and 'Nukhbat al-Muttaqin' (Elite of the Pious). Consider what these titles imply about his scholarly and spiritual rank.
Titles in biographies often reflect the consensus of the community.
3
Extract the virtues mentioned
The passage highlights: acquisition of knowledge, spiritual practice producing zuhd (asceticism), forbearance, generosity, and becoming the reference for fatwa. These link inner piety with outer service.
Hanafi tradition values both 'ilm and 'amal.
4
Understand the purpose of the biography
Biographies in Hanafi texts serve to establish the author’s credibility and the reliability of his work. This passage shows that al-Maydani was both a master of outward knowledge and inward purification.
Such credentials assure readers that the sharh is trustworthy.
5
Reflect on biography in Hanafi literature
Compare this with other Hanafi biographical entries (e.g., in al-Hidayah or al-Quduri). They often include isnad, teachers, students, and character traits.
This practice is rooted in the science of jarh wa ta'dil applied to fuqaha.

الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني
وحافظ الوقت الشهاب الساري شيخ الشيوخ أحمد العطار وشاكر العقاد من رَبَّاني وبحلِي دُرِّه حَلاني وكنت قد جمعت في حياته ثبتــا حـــوى جميــع مروياتــه شعبتُ فيه سند الشيوخ إلى شيوخهم ذوي الرسوخ وفيه ذكر معظم الأثبات وجملة من المسلسلات وكتب السنة والعلــــوم عن غيره يكفي ذوي الفهوم وقد أجزتُهم بما فيه وبما به علــي الله قــــد تكرمــــا من الشروح الغُـر والرسائل ومن حواشــي الــدر والمسائل وما به الإله بعده يَمُن علي في مستقبل من الزمن بشرطه المعروف عند أهله والضبط في إملائــه ونقله مع الدعاء لي بحسن الخاتمة والعفو والغفران في يوم الكاظمة فإنني محمد بن عابدين أرجو من الله القبول كـل حـين ثم قال الخلاصي عقبها :
وقد ظهرت حكمة تخصيصه لهؤلاء الأربعة بعد وفاته، وهي أنـه
لم تَظْهَر مزيةٌ لتلامذته إلا لمن ذكره في النظم.
أما أحد الأربعة، وهو محمد أفندي ابن السيد عثمان الجابي... وأما ثالث الأربعة، الذي لقبه شيخنا رحمه الله تعالى بـ (فارس الميدان)، بل فارس البلدان المتصدي للقاء الأقران في مقام العرفان، الذي حاز قصبات السبق، ولم يسبقه إليها أحد في دمشق،

هو جناب الأخ في الله ، والمحب المحبوب لوجه الله ، الشيخ عبد الغني ابن الحاج طالب الميداني.
فإنه بعد ما أخذ العلم عن شيخنا وغـيـره مـن أهالي الفضل والفهم، اشتغل بالثمرة الموصلة إلى المقامات العالية في الدرجات الآخرة، فأثمرت له الزهد والحلم والجود، فيا لها من بضاعة، وحرفة وصناعة، وصار مسجده له مأوى، وتردى بلباس التقوى ،
وصار مرجع الفتوى في دمشق من غير دعوى ولا رشوى. لا زال با به محط رحال الواردين وملجأ القاصدين، وأدام عليه
ما اختاره وأراده، وزاده من فضله زيادة...». اهـ
البيطار :
ثناء صديقه وابن شيخه الشيخ عبد الرزاق ابن الشيخ حسن
قال العلامة الشيخ عبد الرزاق ابن الشيخ حسن البيطار، المتوفى سنة ١٣٣٥هـ، وهو من أصدقاء الميداني، ووالده الشيخ حسن
البيطار من أخص شيوخ الميداني، قال في وصفه، والثناء عليه: «الشيخ عبد الغني الغنيمي الميداني، «نُخبة المتقين»(۱)، بحر علم لا يُدرك غَوْره ، وفَلَكُ فضل على قطب المعارف دوره، لم يقنع بالمجاز عن الحقيقة، حتى تبوا البحبوحة من تلك الحديقة
(۱) حلية البشر ۳۲۷/۱ في ترجمة إسماعيل نجل الشيخ عبد الغني الغنيمي الميداني، وقد أدرجتها هنا إدراجاً.
Chapter One: Biography of the distinguished scholar Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani
And the guardian of time, the brilliant meteor, the master of masters Ahmad al-Attar and Shakir al-Aqqad, who raised me and adorned me with his pearls. I had compiled in his lifetime a register that contained all his narrations, in which I traced the chain of teachers to their firmly rooted teachers, and in it are mentioned most of the confirmed [authorities] and a number of [hadith with continuous chains] and books of Sunnah and sciences—sufficient for people of understanding. And I have given them permission (ijaza) for what is in it and for what God has graciously bestowed upon me: the brilliant commentaries and treatises, and the marginal notes on al-Durr and the legal issues, and what God may grant me in the future, according to the well-known condition among its people and precision in its dictation and transmission, with supplication for a good end, pardon and forgiveness on the Day of Distress. I am Muhammad ibn Abidin, hoping for acceptance from God at all times. Then al-Khalasi said after it: And the wisdom of his singling out these four became apparent after his death: that no merit appeared for his students except for those he mentioned in the poem. As for one of the four, Muhammad Afandi ibn al-Sayyid Uthman al-Jabi... and as for the third of the four, whom our teacher (may God have mercy on him) titled 'Faris al-Maydan' (Knight of the Field), rather the knight of the lands who confronts peers in the station of gnosis, who obtained the lead and none preceded him in Damascus—he is the brother in God, the beloved and loving for the sake of God, Shaykh Abd al-Ghani ibn al-Hajj Talib al-Maydani. For after he acquired knowledge from our teacher and others of the people of virtue and understanding, he occupied himself with the fruit that leads to the high stations in the final degrees, so it produced in him zuhd (asceticism), forbearance, and generosity—what a merchandise, craft and trade! His mosque became his refuge, he wore the garment of taqwa, and he became the reference for fatwa in Damascus without claim or bribe. His house remained the landing place of visitors and refuge of seekers, and may God perpetuate for him what he chose and desired, and increase him from His bounty... end.
Al-Baytar: Praise from his friend and son of his teacher, Shaykh Abd al-Razzaq ibn al-Shaykh Hasan.
The distinguished scholar Shaykh Abd al-Razzaq ibn al-Shaykh Hasan al-Baytar, who died in 1335 AH, and he was among the friends of al-Maydani, and his father Shaykh Hasan al-Baytar was among the most specialized teachers of al-Maydani, said in describing and praising him: 'Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maydani, the elite of the pious, a sea of knowledge whose depth cannot be fathomed, a sphere of virtue revolving around the axis of the knowledges, he was not satisfied with the metaphorical until he attained the core of that garden.' (1) Hilyat al-Bashar 1/327 in the biography of Isma'il son of Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maydani, and I have inserted it here.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry from the book 'al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri' introducing the author, Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. It opens with the chapter heading for his biography. The text then presents a poem-like praise from Muhammad ibn Abidin (the well-known Hanafi jurist), who mentions the chain of teachers and the ijaza granted to students. Then al-Khalasi adds a comment explaining the wisdom behind Ibn Abidin's singling out four students, one of whom is al-Maydani, titled 'Faris al-Maydan' (Knight of the Field). He describes al-Maydani's virtues: after acquiring knowledge, he devoted himself to spiritual cultivation, resulting in asceticism, forbearance, and generosity. He became the chief mufti of Damascus without seeking fame or bribes. His mosque became a centre for seekers. Finally, al-Baytar (a friend and son of al-Maydani's teacher) offers additional praise, calling him 'nukhbat al-muttaqin' (elite of the pious) and a boundless sea of knowledge, emphasizing that he transcended superficial understanding to achieve deep realization.

Key Terms
ترجمة (tarjama): Biographical entry; the section of the book devoted to the life of al-Maydani.
فارس الميدان (Fāris al-Maydān): A title meaning 'Knight of the Field' given to al-Maydani by his teacher, signifying his preeminence in spiritual and scholarly combat.
الزهد (al-zuhd): Asceticism; a key virtue resulting from his spiritual practice, manifesting in detachment from worldly pursuits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi scholar’s biography authenticates his authority through isnad, spiritual practice, and community service — essential for trusting his fiqh work.

Life of the Author

The Biographical Tradition in Hanafi Learning: The Life of Sheikh al-Maydani
Biographical account of the author from two contemporaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key features of a Hanafi scholar's biography and explain how it establishes his authority as a marja' al-fatwa.

Core Idea
A Hanafi scholar's biography reveals his learning, piety, and role as mufti—foundations of his authority.

In Hanafi tradition, the authority of a fiqh text is tied to its author. This biography of al-Maydani from two contemporaries certifies his qualifications: his chain of knowledge, his asceticism, and his status as the chief mufti of Damascus. Understanding this helps us trust the commentary he wrote on Al-Quduri.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sources of the biography
Notice that the first part is from an anonymous source (likely the editor) and the second, more detailed part is from al-Baytar, a friend and son of al-Maydani's teacher. This establishes a chain of personal attestation.
Al-Baytar's connection lends credibility to the praise.
2
List the personal qualities attributed to al-Maydani
Scan for adjectives: 'asceticism, forbearance, generosity', 'sea of knowledge', 'piety', 'high ambition', 'noble chivalry'. These are the expected virtues of a Hanafi authority.
These qualities are not mere flattery; they are proofs of his spiritual and intellectual suitability.
3
Identify his role in the community
Find the phrase 'مرجع الفتوى في دمشق' (marja' al-fatwa fi Dimashq) and note that he became the reference for legal rulings without claim or bribe. This indicates his recognized expertise.
Being marja' al-fatwa means he was the top mufti, whose opinions were relied upon.
4
Note tangible achievements
The biography mentions his authored works and the renovation of the mosque with a new minaret. These are concrete evidences of his scholarly output and community service.
Works and physical renovations are lasting legacies that enhance his authority.
5
Connect to the Hanafi concept of scholarly authority
Reflect on why such a biography is placed at the beginning of a fiqh commentary. It assures the reader that the author is a trustworthy transmitter and interpreter of the Hanafi school.
The biography functions as an 'isnad' for the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني

هو جناب الأخ في الله ، والمحب المحبوب لوجه الله ، الشيخ عبد الغني ابن الحاج طالب الميداني.
فإنه بعد ما أخذ العلم عن شيخنا وغـيـره مـن أهالي الفضل والفهم، اشتغل بالثمرة الموصلة إلى المقامات العالية في الدرجات الآخرة، فأثمرت له الزهد والحلم والجود، فيا لها من بضاعة، وحرفة وصناعة، وصار مسجده له مأوى، وتردى بلباس التقوى ،
وصار مرجع الفتوى في دمشق من غير دعوى ولا رشوى. لا زال با به محط رحال الواردين وملجأ القاصدين، وأدام عليه
ما اختاره وأراده، وزاده من فضله زيادة...». اهـ

البيطار :
ثناء صديقه وابن شيخه الشيخ عبد الرزاق ابن الشيخ حسن
قال العلامة الشيخ عبد الرزاق ابن الشيخ حسن البيطار، المتوفى سنة ١٣٣٥هـ، وهو من أصدقاء الميداني، ووالده الشيخ حسن
البيطار من أخص شيوخ الميداني، قال في وصفه، والثناء عليه: «الشيخ عبد الغني الغنيمي الميداني، «نُخبة المتقين»(۱)، بحر علم لا يُدرك غَوْره ، وفَلَكُ فضل على قطب المعارف دوره، لم يقنع بالمجاز عن الحقيقة، حتى تبوا البحبوحة من تلك الحديقة

ولديه من المعلومات ما يشق على القلم حشره، ويتعسر على
الألسنة نشره.
وتأليفاتُه التي يَحقُّ لرائيها أن يتنافس بها ويُفاخِر : محشوة من الفوائد بما يعقل الأفكار، ويقيد الخواطر.
وكان ذا زهد وتقوى وعبادة في السِّرِّ والنَّجوى، وهمة عالية، ومروءة سامية، ولسان على الذكر دائب وشهرة قد سارت في المشارق والمغارب، ومنزلة في القلوب حميدة، وعقيـدة في كمالـه
وحيدة.
وله فضائل معروفةٌ شهيرة، وخيريــات حسنة، وتعميرات مستحسنة، وكانت الناس تأتيه بالهدايا وتقصده بعظيم الوصايا.
وقد جدد عمارة الجامع الذي بجانب داره في الميدان، في محلة ساحة السخانة، وأنشأ له منارةً عظيمة متينة.
وبالجملة والتفصيل، قد كان شهماً ما له من مثيل، وقد اتسع جاهه، وكثر في الناس ثناؤه، وخالطت هيبته القلوب، فكان لها أجلّ مطلوب ومرغوب.
ولم يَزَل على استقامته في طاعته وعبادته، وإفادته لطالبه ووارده، وإحسانه لراغبه وقاصده ، إلى أن سَجَع على دوحه حمام الحمام ، ودعاه إلى الرحلة داعي الأنام فتوفي رحمه الله تعالى»(۱). اهـ
(۱) حلية البشر ٨٦٧/٢ - ٨٧٢
Chapter One: Biography of the Allama Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani

He is the brother in God, and the beloved for the sake of God, Sheikh Abd al-Ghani ibn al-Hajj Talib al-Maydani. After he acquired knowledge from our teacher and others among the people of virtue and understanding, he engaged in the fruit that leads to high stations in the afterlife. So it yielded for him asceticism, forbearance, and generosity. What a commodity, trade, and craft! And his mosque became a refuge for him, and he clothed himself in the garment of piety. And he became the reference for fatwa in Damascus without claim or bribe. His door continues to be the resting place of travelers and the refuge of seekers. May God perpetuate upon him what he chose and desired, and increase him from His bounty... End.

Al-Baytar:
The praise of his friend and the son of his teacher, Sheikh Abd al-Razzaq ibn Sheikh Hasan.
Allama Sheikh Abd al-Razzaq ibn Sheikh Hasan al-Baytar, died 1335 AH, who was a friend of al-Maydani, and his father Sheikh Hasan al-Baytar was among the most specialized teachers of al-Maydani, said in his description and praise: 'Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maydani, the cream of the pious, a sea of knowledge whose depth cannot be reached, a sphere of virtue whose orbit is the pole of sciences. He was not satisfied with metaphor over truth until he settled in the midst of that garden.
He possesses knowledge whose gathering would burden the pen and whose propagation would be difficult for tongues.
His works, which it is fitting for the beholder to compete over and boast about, are filled with benefits that occupy minds and bind thoughts.
He had asceticism, piety, and worship in secret and private, high ambition, noble chivalry, a tongue ever engaged in remembrance, a reputation that traveled to the East and West, a praiseworthy position in hearts, and a unique belief in his perfection.
He had well-known and famous virtues, good charities, and commendable constructions. People would bring him gifts and seek him out for great bequests.
He renovated the mosque adjacent to his house in al-Maydan, in the Sahat al-Sakhana neighborhood, and built a magnificent, strong minaret for it.
In summary and detail, he was a noble man without peer. His status expanded, people's praise of him increased, and awe of him mixed with hearts, so he was the most noble desire and ambition for them.
He continued in his steadfastness in obedience and worship, his benefit to his seekers and visitors, and his kindness to those who desired and sought him, until the dove of death cooed on his palm tree, and the caller of people called him to the journey, so he passed away, may God have mercy on him.' End.
(1) Hilyat al-Bashar 2/867-872
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage provides a biographical account of the author of Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri, Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. It is divided into two main parts: a brief introductory eulogy and a more detailed eulogy by his contemporary al-Baytar. The first part highlights his piety, his mastery of knowledge, his role as the chief mufti in Damascus, and his charitable work. The second part, by al-Baytar, expands on these themes, emphasizing his erudition (described as a 'sea of knowledge'), his asceticism, his authorship of valuable works, and the renovation of his local mosque. The biography serves to establish the scholarly authority and spiritual stature of the author, which is important context for the reader of his commentary on Al-Quduri.

Key Terms
مرجع الفتوى (marja' al-fatwa): The person to whom people refer for authoritative legal rulings; the chief mufti of a region.
ترجمة (tarjama): Biographical notice; a written account of a person's life and achievements.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Biography of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani and Its Significance
Biographical sketch of the author with praises from contemporaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical details of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani and explain the purpose of including such introductions in Hanafi fiqh works.

Core Idea
A scholar's biography establishes authority and trust in a madhhab's textual tradition.

This passage introduces the author of al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri, Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. It describes his vast knowledge, piety, and charitable works, and includes praises from two contemporary scholars: Sheikh Ahmad al-Hadrawi and Sheikh 'Ala' al-Din ibn 'Abidin. Such biographical introductions are common in classical Hanafi works to certify the author's reliability and to situate the work within the scholarly lineage. Understanding this context helps you appreciate the authority behind the fiqh rulings you study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and source
Recognize that the passage is a biography of the author of al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri. Note the full name and the work's title.
The passage is from the introduction of the book itself.
2
Extract key attributes
List the qualities mentioned: vast knowledge, asceticism, piety, charitable acts (rebuilding a mosque and erecting a minaret).
These attributes serve to portray the author as a reliable and virtuous transmitter.
3

Identify the two praises: one from Sheikh Ahmad al-Hadrawi al-Makki, and one from Sheikh 'Ala' al-Din ibn 'Abidin, son of the famous commentator Ibn 'Abidin. Note that these were written while the author was alive.
External testimonies add weight to the author's scholarly standing.
4
Understand the function

This practice is rooted in the Islamic tradition of isnad (chain of transmission).

قال العلامة الشيخ أحمد بن محمد الحضراوي المكي الهاشمي، المولود سنة ١٢٥٢هـ ، والمتوفى سنة ١٣٢٧هـ، صديق الميداني، ومن أقرانه، وقد كتب هذا الثناء والميداني على قيد الحياة، فقال في وصفه، والثناء عليه:

ثناء الشيخ علاء الدين ابن عابدين نجل صاحب الحاشية : قال العلامة الشيخ محمد علاء الدين بن محمد أمين عابدين نجل صاحب الحاشية ، المولود سنة ١٢٤٤هـ، وكان عمره حين توفي والده ثمان سنين والمتوفى سنة ١٣٠٦ هـ ، صاحب التكملة للحاشية، قال في ترجمته لوالده) :

(۱) نزهة الفكر فيما مضى من الحوادث والعبر في تراجم رجال القرن الثاني عشر والثالث عشر ١٧٣/٢.
(۲) ص ١٠، وهذه الترجمة مطبوعة في أول التكملة (ط) بولاق).
Chapter One: Biography of the eminent scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. He possesses knowledge whose gathering exhausts the pen and whose dissemination burdens tongues. His writings, which the beholder is entitled to vie for and boast about, are stuffed with benefits that captivate minds and bind thoughts. He was a man of asceticism, piety, and worship in secret and in private, lofty ambition, sublime chivalry, a tongue constant in remembrance, fame that spread through East and West, a praiseworthy station in hearts, and a unique belief in his perfection. He had well-known and famous virtues, good charitable works, and commendable renovations. People brought him gifts and sought him out with great bequests. He rebuilt the mosque beside his house in al-Maidan, in the neighborhood of Saha al-Sakhana, and erected for it a great and solid minaret. In short and in detail, he was a gallant man without peer; his influence expanded, praise of him among people multiplied, and awe of him entered hearts, so he was their most sublime desire and aspiration. He continued in his uprightness in obedience and worship, benefiting his students and visitors, and being kind to those who sought him, until the dove of death cooed on his tree and the caller of departure called him, so he died, may Allah have mercy on him. End quote. Source: Hilyat al-Bashar 2/867-872. Praise of his friend Sheikh Ahmad al-Hadrawi al-Makki: The eminent scholar Sheikh Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Hadrawi al-Makki al-Hashimi, born in 1252 AH and died in 1327 AH, friend and contemporary of al-Maidani, wrote this praise while al-Maidani was still alive. He said describing and praising him: 'The Sheikh, the Imam, the erudite scholar, the master of hadith and fiqh, the learned and practicing scholar, the teeming ocean, the complete one, the apple of time's eye, the pivot of the people of excellence, the Hanafi jurist... And he is, despite that, in might and power, constantly engaged in teaching and benefiting. He performed Hajj more than once, and I met him in Mecca in 1281 AH, in Damascus in 1283 AH, and in 1286 AH...' End quote. Source: Nuzhat al-Fikr fi ma Mada min al-Hawadith wa al-'Ibar fi Tarajim Rijal al-Qarn al-Thani 'Ashar wa al-Thalith 'Ashar 2/173. Praise of Sheikh 'Ala' al-Din ibn 'Abidin, son of the author of the Hashiya: The eminent scholar Sheikh Muhammad 'Ala' al-Din ibn Muhammad Amin 'Abidin, son of the author of the Hashiya, born in 1244 AH (he was eight years old when his father died), died in 1306 AH, author of the completion of the Hashiya (al-Takmila), said in his biography of his father: (p. 10, this biography is printed at the beginning of al-Takmila, Bulaq edition).
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This is a biographical passage about the author of al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri, Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. The text first gives a general description of his vast knowledge, his asceticism, and his piety. It mentions his charitable works, including rebuilding a mosque and erecting a minaret. The passage then includes two external testimonials: one from his friend Sheikh Ahmad al-Hadrawi al-Makki, who praises him as a master of hadith and fiqh, and another from Sheikh 'Ala' al-Din ibn 'Abidin, the son of the famous commentator Ibn 'Abidin. These testimonies are from contemporary scholars, showing al-Maidani's high standing. The footnotes provide sources for the quotes. This type of biographical introduction is common in classical works to establish the author's authority and reliability.

Key Terms
العلامة (al-ʿAllāmah): A title meaning 'the highly learned' or 'the most erudite scholar'.
الحبر الهمام (al-Ḥibr al-Humām): The ink (scholar) of great concern; a hyperbolic praise meaning extremely learned and energetic scholar.
التكملة للحاشية (al-Takmilah li al-Ḥāshiyah): The completion/supplement to the gloss (Hashiya) of Ibn 'Abidin, written by his son 'Ala' al-Din.

The biography of a scholar in a classical Hanafi work is essential for establishing the authority and trustworthiness of the text within the madhhab's transmission chain.

The Scholarly Authority of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani
Biographical notes praising al-Maydani by his students

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the role of biographical testimonies (tarajim) in establishing a scholar's authority within the Hanafi tradition and explain the key scholarly traits of al-Maydani mentioned by his students.

Core Idea
A scholar's authority is built not only on his writings but on the attestations of his teachers and students.

This passage presents a brief biography of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maydani, the renowned Hanafi commentator of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. Instead of legal rulings, it offers firsthand testimonials from his students, praising his depth of knowledge, his mastery of usul al-fiqh, and his humility. Understanding how such biographical materials function is essential for appreciating the credibility of classical Hanafi texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and purpose
Determine who the biography is about and why it appears at the beginning of al-Lubab.
The title clearly states it is a biography of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani.
2
Analyze student testimonies
Read the praises of Tahir al-Jazairi and Muhammad al-Bitar; note the specific qualities they highlight (e.g., 'verifying scholar', 'solver of dilemmas', 'avoids fame').
Al-Jazairi's account is more detailed about al-Maydani's scholarly method.
3
Connect to Hanafi scholarship
Recognize that al-Maydani's commentary on al-Quduri is a standard text; his students' endorsements reinforce its reliability.
The commentary al-Lubab is widely used in Hanafi circles.
4
Evaluate the source value
Consider why such biographical notes are included in printed classical texts: to establish the chain of transmission (isnad) and scholarly pedigree.
This practice upholds the tradition of verifying knowledge through reliable chains.

الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني
وممن أخذ عن والدي العالم العلامة العمدة الفهامة، فقيه العصر الشيخ عبد الغني الغنيمي الميداني، فإنه عنه أخذ، وبه انتفع، وعليه تخرج». اهـ
* ثناء تلميذ الميداني الشيخ طاهر الجزائري :
قال العلامة الشيخ طاهر الجزائري الدمشقي، وهو من أخص تلاميذ الميداني المولود سنة ١٢٦٨هـ ، والمتوفى سنة ١٣٣٨هـ، وذلك فيما نقله عنه تلميذه الشيخ محمد سعيد الباني، المتوفى سنة ١٣٥١هـ، في كتابه الخاص بترجمة شيخه: «تنوير البصائر بسيرة الشيخ طاهر (۱)، قال الباني: ... حتى اتصل بأستاذه الخاص الشيخ عبد الغني الغنيمي، الشهير بالميداني شارح كتاب القدوري، وكثيراً ما سمعت الفقيد يُطريه، ويُثني عليه بأنه من العلماء المحققين، والواقفين على لبـاب الشريعة وأسرارها البعيدين عن البدع والخرافات.
، وأخبرني أنه حين حضر عنده «التلويح»، للسعد التفتازاني علـى توضيح التنقيح»، لصدر الشريعة في أصول الفقه، وَجَدَ منه تحقيقاً يُعرب عن غزارة علمه، وارتقاء فكره غير أنه كان يُؤثر الحمول على حب الشهرة والظهور، فلا يرغب في المناقشة والتفصح في المجالس الحافلة، ولكنه إذا سئل على انفراد عن عويصات المسائل: تجـد منـه حل‌ال المعضلات، وكشاف الأستار عن الأسرار، فلزمه الفقيد، وتلقى عنه ما تلقى حتى تخرج به». اهـ.
ثناء تلميذه الشيخ محمد ابن الشيخ حسن البيطار :
(1) ووصفه تلميذه العلامة الشيخ محمد ابن الشيخ حسن البيطار، المولود سنة ١٢٣١هـ، والمتوفى سنة ١٣١٢هـ)، وذلك فيما سجله على نسخة نَسَخَها بخطه من رسالة شرح منظومة عقود رسم المفتي : لشيخه الشيخ محمد أمين ابن عابدين، فقد قال في آخرها :
«قد بالغت في تصحيح هذه الرسالة على حسب الطاقة أصلها المنقولة عنه، وسمعتها من في سيدي الحبر السامي جناب سيدي الشيخ عبد الغني أفندي الغنيمي من أولها إلى آخرها، جزاه الله كل خير، ودفع عنه كل ضير، وأنا الفقير كاتبها محمد تلميذ المؤلف والمسمع ابن حسن البيطار، وذلك في رابع ذي الحجة، سنة ١٢٥٧هـ، ثم كتب الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني: كتب بإذني وأنا الفقير عبد الغني الغنيمي الميداني عفي عنه )) (۲)
Chapter One: Biography of the scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani
And among those who learned from my father, the great scholar, the pillar, the highly intelligent, the jurist of the age, Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maydani, for he learned from him, benefited from him, and graduated under him. End.
* Praise of al-Maydani's student Sheikh Tahir al-Jazairi:
The scholar Sheikh Tahir al-Jazairi al-Dimashqi, who was one of the most distinguished students of al-Maydani, born in 1268 AH and died in 1338 AH, as narrated by his student Sheikh Muhammad Said al-Bani (d. 1351 AH) in his book dedicated to the biography of his teacher 'Tanwir al-Basa'ir bi Sirat al-Shaykh Tahir', said al-Bani: ... until he connected with his special teacher Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Ghanimi, known as al-Maydani, commentator of al-Quduri's book. I often heard the deceased praise him and commend him as being among the verifying scholars, those who grasp the core of Shariah and its secrets, far removed from innovations and superstitions.
He told me that when he attended with him the study of 'al-Talwih' by Sa'd al-Taftazani on 'Tawdih al-Tanqih' by Sadr al-Shariah in usul al-fiqh, he found from him a verification that indicates the abundance of his knowledge and the elevation of his thought. However, he preferred modesty over love of fame and prominence, so he did not desire discussion and verbosity in crowded gatherings, but if he was asked in private about difficult issues, you would find from him the solver of dilemmas and the unveiler of covers from secrets. So the deceased adhered to him and received from him what he received until he graduated under him. End.
Praise of his student Sheikh Muhammad ibn al-Shaykh Hasan al-Bitar:
His student, the scholar Sheikh Muhammad ibn al-Shaykh Hasan al-Bitar (born 1231 AH, died 1312 AH) described him, as recorded on a copy he transcribed by hand from the treatise 'Sharh Manzumat 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' by his teacher Sheikh Muhammad Amin Ibn Abidin. He said at its end:
'I have exerted effort in correcting this treatise to the best of my ability, its original transmitted from him, and I heard it from the mouth of my master, the eminent scholar, his excellency my master Sheikh Abdul Ghani Afandi al-Ghanimi from its beginning to its end. May Allah reward him with all good and remove from him all harm. I am the poor scribe Muhammad, student of the author and the one who heard it, son of Hasan al-Bitar. This was on the fourth of Dhul Hijjah, year 1257 AH.' Then Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maydani wrote: 'Written with my permission, and I am the poor Abdul Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maydani, may Allah pardon him.'
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maydani, the Hanafi jurist and commentator of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. The text presents two testimonials from his students, establishing his scholarly credentials and personal character. The first student, Sheikh Tahir al-Jazairi (d. 1338 AH), is quoted via his own student Muhammad Said al-Bani, describing al-Maydani as a 'verifying scholar' (min al-‘ulama’ al-muhaqqiqin) who had mastered the core of Shariah and its secrets. He was known for his depth in usul al-fiqh, as evidenced by his study of al-Taftazani's al-Talwih, yet he avoided public show and preferred private instruction. The second student, Sheikh Muhammad ibn Hasan al-Bitar, attests to having studied and corrected a treatise by Ibn Abidin under al-Maydani's supervision, confirming his role as a teacher and transmitter of Hanafi legal methodology. This section serves as front matter, establishing the authority and reliability of al-Maydani as a commentator and scholar. No fiqh rulings are contained herein; the purpose is to introduce the author and his place in the Hanafi scholarly tradition.

Key Terms
الميداني (al-Maydani): The honorific name of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maydani, the Hanafi jurist and commentator of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, known for his commentary al-Lubab.

The Scholarly Credibility of Sheikh Abdul Ghani Al-Maydani
Biographical accounts praising Sheikh Al-Maydani from his students.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key testimonies that establish Sheikh Al-Maydani's scholarly authority and state the importance of chain of transmission (sanad) in Hanafi learning.

Core Idea
A scholar's authority is validated through the testimonies of his teachers and students, preserved in the sanad.

This lesson examines the biographical section of Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri, where students of Sheikh Abdul Ghani Al-Maydani testify to his knowledge, piety, and humility. In the Hanafi tradition, such testimonies are not mere flattery; they are critical for establishing the reliability (thiqah) of the author and the chain of transmission (sanad) of the text. Understanding these accounts helps you appreciate the rigorous standards of scholarly verification in our madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three testimonies
Read the passage carefully and list the three individuals who praised Al-Maydani. Note their names and the context of their praise (e.g., a manuscript note, a printed preface).
The testimonies are from Sheikh Muhammad al-Baytar, Ahmad Nazif (Shaykhi Zada), and an unnamed student in the manuscript of Kashf al-Iltibas.
2
Analyze each testimony's content
For each testimony, identify what specific qualities or actions are praised (e.g., knowledge, avoidance of fame, dedication to teaching). Determine whether the testimony includes a verification of the text (like al-Baytar hearing the treatise) or a general character endorsement.
Al-Baytar's testimony is particularly strong because he states he heard the entire treatise from Al-Maydani and corrected it with his permission.
3
Understand the function of these testimonies in Hanafi scholarship
Explain how these testimonies serve to establish the 'adala (integrity) and mastery of the author, which is essential for trusting his fiqh rulings and the transmission of the text. Connect this to the concept of tazkiya (approbation) in hadith and fiqh.
In the Hanafi school, the chain of transmission (sanad) of a text is carefully preserved, and biographical entries (tarajim) are part of this process.
4
Reflect on the lesson for your own study
Consider how you can apply this principle when encountering any Hanafi text. Before relying on a book, you should investigate the author's biography to assess reliability.
This habit protects you from weak or fabricated rulings and strengthens your connection to the tradition.

«قد بالغت في تصحيح هذه الرسالة على حسب الطاقة أصلها المنقولة عنه، وسمعتها من في سيدي الحبر السامي جناب سيدي الشيخ عبد الغني أفندي الغنيمي من أولها إلى آخرها، جزاه الله كل خير، ودفع عنه كل ضير، وأنا الفقير كاتبها محمد تلميذ المؤلف والمسمع ابن حسن البيطار، وذلك في رابع ذي الحجة، سنة ١٢٥٧هـ، ثم كتب الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني: كتب بإذني وأنا الفقير عبد الغني الغنيمي الميداني عفي
عنه )) (۲)
(۱) له ترجمة في تاريخ علماء دمشق في القرن الرابع عشر الهجري ١١٩/١، وقد صرّح الشيخ محمد البيطار بالتلمذة على الميداني في أكثر من موضع، منها في آخر نسخة بخطه من رسالة : إسعاف المريدين للميداني، وهي من محفوظات الظاهرية بدمشق، برقم (٤٧٩٣)، وعندي منها صورة.
(٢) ينظر فهرس مخطوطات الظاهرية (الفقه الحنفي) ٤٦٠/١ .

ثناء أحد الوجهاء من تلاميذ الميداني :
جاء في مقدمة الطبعة العثمانية لكتاب اللباب، في دار السلطنة السَّنيَّة، المطبوعة في عهد المؤلف سنة ١٢٧٥هـ، زمن السلطان العثماني عبد المجيد بقلم الفقير الضعيف : (صحا فلر ـ هكذا ـ شيخي زاده أحمد نظيف، بعد أن صحب الشيخ الميداني بدمشق الشام ، واستنسخ نسخة من اللباب، وهو الذي سعى في طبعه، قال: وكنت قد تعهدتُ - حين تشرفي بصحبة الفاضل الشارح بدمشق نشره بالطبع، بسبب نفاسته، وحُسن سيرة مؤلفه، إذ هي سيرة السلف الصالح من حُسن الأخلاق والعِفّة، حتى مع وفـور فـضـله وكماله : يجتنب غاية الاجتناب عن التعين والاشتهار، ولم يرض الاختلاط بغير أرباب العلم من الأكابر والتجار، معتكف على خدمة الشريعة، وتدريس العلوم، جعل الله سعيه مشكوراً، وأجــره موفوراً...». اهـ

ثناء أحد تلاميذ الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني :
جاء في آخر نسخة مخطوطة من كتاب: «كشف الالتباس للشيخ عبد الغني الميداني، كتبت في عهد مؤلفها، جاء ما يلي:
كشف الالتباس عما أورده الإمام البخاري على بعض الناس»،
،
لعلامة الوقت، سامي المقام والثَّبْت فريد الزمان، وفارس الميدان، النائل بإحسانه سبحانه سائر الأماني، مولانا الشيخ عبد الغني الغنيمي الميداني، مد الله تعالى في حياته، وحفظه في حركاته وسكناته،
Chapter One: Biography of the Allamah Sheikh Abdul Ghani Al-Maydani

... (the passage includes three praises from his students, details about his life and character, and notes about the printing of his book Al-Lubab).
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section from the beginning of the book 'Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri'. It collects testimonies from three of Sheikh Abdul Ghani Al-Maydani's students praising his knowledge, piety, and humility. The first testimony is from Sheikh Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Baytar, who records that he heard the entire treatise from Al-Maydani and corrected it with his permission. The second testimony comes from a preface to the Ottoman edition of Al-Lubab, written by a student named [؟] Shaykhi Zada Ahmad Nazif, who praises Al-Maydani's avoidance of fame and his dedication to teaching. The third testimony is from the manuscript of 'Kashf al-Iltibas', describing Al-Maydani as 'the knight of the field' and a unique scholar of his time. These accounts establish the author's scholarly credibility and emphasize his virtuous character.

Key Terms
سند (sanad): Chain of transmission that traces the text back to its author, ensuring authenticity.
تزكية (tazkiyah): Approbation or testimony of a person's integrity (adalah) by reliable scholars.
عدالة (adalah): Moral integrity and uprightness required for a transmitter to be accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary purpose of the biographical praises included at the beginning of Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri?
A) To promote the book commercially
B) To establish the author's scholarly credibility and reliability
C) To provide detailed family history of the author
D) To criticize the author's opponents

Key Takeaway
Biographical accounts (tarajim) are a vital part of the Hanafi tradition; they establish the authority and reliability of authors and their works.

Life of the Author
beginner

Biography of Shaykh ‘Abd al-Ghanī al-Maydānī
Biographical testimonials praising the author's character and scholarship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key qualities of Shaykh al-Maydānī as attested by his students and explain why his work al-Lubāb is esteemed in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
The character of a scholar is the foundation of the authority of his work.

This lesson introduces Shaykh ‘Abd al-Ghanī al-Maydānī, the Hanafi faqīh and author of al-Lubāb, through the praises of his contemporaries. We explore his piety, avoidance of fame, dedication to teaching, and the esteem in which he was held. Understanding the author’s integrity helps us trust the fiqh rulings he transmits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his works
Shaykh ‘Abd al-Ghanī al-Maydānī is the Hanafi jurist who wrote al-Lubāb (a commentary on al-Qudūrī) and Kashf al-Iltibās. Note the date (1275 AH) and the Ottoman context.
Al-Lubāb is a standard Hanafi fiqh text.
2
Extract the praised character traits
From the students’ testimonies, list qualities: avoidance of fame, association only with scholars, service to Sharī‘ah, teaching, good character, chastity.
These traits are emphasized multiple times.
3
Relate traits to fiqh authority
In Hanafi tradition, the reliability of a jurist enhances the weight of his rulings. al-Maydānī’s piety and reluctance for fame suggest his writings are sincere and precise.
This is a principle: trust in the transmitter affects acceptance of the transmitted.

الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني
ثناء أحد الوجهاء من تلاميذ الميداني :
جاء في مقدمة الطبعة العثمانية لكتاب اللباب، في دار السلطنة السَّنيَّة، المطبوعة في عهد المؤلف سنة ١٢٧٥هـ، زمن السلطان العثماني عبد المجيد بقلم الفقير الضعيف : (صحا فلر ـ هكذا ـ شيخي زاده أحمد نظيف، بعد أن صحب الشيخ الميداني بدمشق الشام ، واستنسخ نسخة من اللباب، وهو الذي سعى في طبعه، قال: وكنت قد تعهدتُ - حين تشرفي بصحبة الفاضل الشارح بدمشق نشره بالطبع، بسبب نفاسته، وحُسن سيرة مؤلفه، إذ هي سيرة السلف الصالح من حُسن الأخلاق والعِفّة، حتى مع وفـور فـضـله وكماله : يجتنب غاية الاجتناب عن التعين والاشتهار، ولم يرض الاختلاط بغير أرباب العلم من الأكابر والتجار، معتكف على خدمة الشريعة، وتدريس العلوم، جعل الله سعيه مشكوراً، وأجــره موفوراً...». اهـ

كشف الالتباس عما أورده الإمام البخاري على بعض الناس»،

آمین. آمین». اهـ
مقدمة
ذكر هذا العلامة الشيخ عبد الفتاح أبو غدة رحمه الله في تحقيقه لكتاب: «كشف الالتباس (۱)، وقال: «هكذا كتب في النسخة
المخطوطة أمامي، فأثبته كما هو». اهـ
ثناء وجد على وجه نسخة من اللباب :
وجدت على نسخة مخطوطة من كتاب اللباب للميداني المنسوخة في عهد المؤلّف، وذلك بعد سنة من تأليفه له، مودعة في دار الكتب المصرية، برقم (٢١٣٦) فقه حنفي، وجدت مكتوباً عليها
ما يلي:
وهذا الكتاب جامعه العالم العلامة، الجهبذ البحر الفهامة، سيدي الشيخ العالم العارف عبد الغني الغنيمي الميداني، نفعنا الله في الدنيا والآخرة، وأفاض علينا من علومه». اهـ.

قال العلامة الشيخ محمد جمال الدين بن محمد سعيد بن قاسم الحلاق الحسيني القاسمي الدمشقي، وهو في طبقة تلاميذ الميداني، لكن لم يُذكر عنه أنه أخذ عنه ، المولود سنة ۱۲۸۳هـ، والمتوفى سنة ١٣٣٢ هـ ، وله من العمر ٤٩ سنة، وله أكثر من سبعين مصنفاً، قال
(۱) ص ٥٥ ، حاشية رقم (٢).
Chapter One: Biography of the Allāmah Shaykh ‘Abd al-Ghanī al-Maydānī
Praise from one of the notables among al-Maydānī’s students:
In the introduction to the Ottoman edition of the book al-Lubāb, published in the Exalted Sultanate, printed during the author’s lifetime in the year 1275 AH, during the reign of the Ottoman Sultan ‘Abd al-Majīd, written by the poor weak [student]: (Sahā Flar — thus — Shaykhzādah Aḥmad Naẓīf, after accompanying Shaykh al-Maydānī in Damascus, and he copied a manuscript of al-Lubāb, and he was the one who sought its printing. He said: I had undertaken—when I was honored to accompany the virtuous commentator in Damascus—to publish it in print, due to its value and the good conduct of its author, which is the conduct of the righteous predecessors: good character and chastity, despite his abundant merit and perfection: he strenuously avoided seeking position and fame, and he did not consent to mix with anyone other than the people of knowledge among the greats and merchants. He devoted himself to serving the Sharī‘ah and teaching the sciences. May Allah make his efforts appreciated and his reward abundant...). End.
Praise from one of the students of Shaykh ‘Abd al-Ghanī al-Maydānī:
At the end of a manuscript copy of the book Kashf al-Iltibās by Shaykh ‘Abd al-Ghanī al-Maydānī, written during the author’s lifetime, the following appears:
“Kashf al-Iltibās ‘ammā awradahu al-Imām al-Bukhārī ‘alā ba‘ḍ al-nās”
Of the Allāmah of the time, lofty in station and steadiness, unique of the age, the knight of the field, the one who attains all hopes through His bounty—glory be to Him—our master Shaykh ‘Abd al-Ghanī al-Ghunaymī al-Maydānī. May Allah Most High prolong his life and protect him in his movements and stillness, Āmīn. Āmīn.” End.
Introduction:
Allāmah Shaykh ‘Abd al-Fattāḥ Abū Ghuddah (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned this in his critical edition of the book Kashf al-Iltibās (1), and said: “Thus it is written in the manuscript copy before me, so I recorded it as it is.” End.
Praise found on the face of a copy of al-Lubāb:
I found on a manuscript copy of the book al-Lubāb by al-Maydānī, copied during the author’s lifetime, one year after its composition, deposited in the Egyptian National Library, number (2136) Hanafi fiqh, written upon it the following:
“And this book was compiled by the world-renowned Allāmah, the genius, the ocean of understanding, my master the learned and gnostic Shaykh ‘Abd al-Ghanī al-Ghunaymī al-Maydānī. May Allah benefit us with him in this world and the next, and shower us with his knowledge.” End.
Praise of Shaykh Muḥammad Jamāl al-Dīn al-Qāsimī al-Dimashqī:
Allāmah Shaykh Muḥammad Jamāl al-Dīn ibn Muḥammad Sa‘īd ibn Qāsim al-Ḥallāq al-Ḥusaynī al-Qāsimī al-Dimashqī said—he is of the rank of al-Maydānī’s students, though it is not mentioned that he studied directly with him, born in 1283 AH, died in 1332 AH, at the age of 49, and authored more than seventy works—he said:
(1) p. 55, footnote no. (2).
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage is a biographical section (tarjamah) presenting praise and testimonials about the author of al-Lubāb, Shaykh ‘Abd al-Ghanī al-Maydānī. It begins with praise from one of his students, Shaykhzādah Aḥmad Naẓīf, who accompanied him in Damascus and was instrumental in printing al-Lubāb. The student extols the author’s character, noting his avoidance of fame and position, his association only with scholars, and his dedication to teaching and serving the Sharī‘ah. This is followed by a manuscript note from the author's own work Kashf al-Iltibās, describing him as the ‘unique of the age’ and praying for him. The editor Shaykh ‘Abd al-Fattāḥ Abū Ghuddah confirms the accuracy of the manuscript. Another manuscript copy of al-Lubāb, deposited in the Egyptian National Library, contains similar praise. Finally, the noted scholar Shaykh Muḥammad Jamāl al-Dīn al-Qāsimī, though not a direct student, is cited as belonging to the same generation of students and offering further commendation. This establishes the author's piety, scholarship, and high standing among his contemporaries.

Key Terms
اللباب (al-Lubāb): A commentary on al-Qudūrī, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text, authored by Shaykh al-Maydānī.
كشف الالتباس (Kashf al-Iltibās): Another work by al-Maydānī dealing with objections raised against Imām al-Bukhārī.
ترجمة (tarjamah): Biographical entry; a record of a scholar's life and works.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The Ottoman Sultan ‘Abd al-Majīd

Key Takeaway
The biography of Shaykh al-Maydānī establishes his authority as a Hanafi jurist dedicated to teaching and piety, reinforcing the reliability of his fiqh works like al-Lubāb.

Biography of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani: The Author of al-Lubab
Compilation of scholarly praises for the author

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical details of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani and explain the significance of these sources in establishing his scholarly authority.

Core Idea
The scholarly praises collected in this biography authenticate al-Maidani’s expertise in Hanafi fiqh and his standing among his peers.

This lesson introduces the life and scholarly reputation of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani, the author of the renowned Hanafi fiqh text *al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri*. While this is not a legal ruling, the biographical details are essential for understanding the authority behind the text. The passage compiles praises from three notable scholars, each attesting to al-Maidani's excellence in fiqh, piety, and dedication. As students of Hanafi fiqh, recognizing the credentials of the authors we study helps us gauge the reliability and weight of their works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sources of praise
List the three scholars who praised al-Maidani in this passage: the manuscript endorsement, Muhammad Jamal al-Din al-Qasimi, and Muhammad Adib Taqi al-Din al-Husni.
The first source is anonymous, found on a manuscript copy.
2
Extract key attributes
For each source, note the specific qualities highlighted, such as 'preeminent scholar', 'virtuous, pious, devout', 'investigative scholar', and 'passion for building mosques'.
Focus on attributes that relate to fiqh knowledge and character.
3
Understand the purpose
Explain why this biography is placed at the beginning of a fiqh commentary: to establish the author's credibility and the reliability of the work.
Biographical front matter is a common scholarly practice to situate the author.
4
Assess the authority
Judge how these praises contribute to the authority of al-Lubab. Consider that the manuscript was copied during al-Maidani's lifetime and preserved in the Egyptian National Library.
External validation from multiple independent sources strengthens the text's standing.

«آمین. آمین». اهـ

الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني

مقدمة

ذكر هذا العلامة الشيخ عبد الفتاح أبو غدة رحمه الله في تحقيقه لكتاب: «كشف الالتباس (۱)، وقال: «هكذا كتب في النسخة المخطوطة أمامي، فأثبته كما هو». اهـ

ثناء وجد على وجه نسخة من اللباب :

وجدت على نسخة مخطوطة من كتاب اللباب للميداني المنسوخة في عهد المؤلّف، وذلك بعد سنة من تأليفه له، مودعة في دار الكتب المصرية، برقم (٢١٣٦) فقه حنفي، وجدت مكتوباً عليها ما يلي:

وهذا الكتاب جامعه العالم العلامة، الجهبذ البحر الفهامة، سيدي الشيخ العالم العارف عبد الغني الغنيمي الميداني، نفعنا الله في الدنيا والآخرة، وأفاض علينا من علومه». اهـ.

ثناء الشيخ محمد جمال الدين القاسمي الدمشقي :

قال العلامة الشيخ محمد جمال الدين بن محمد سعيد بن قاسم الحلاق الحسيني القاسمي الدمشقي، وهو في طبقة تلاميذ الميداني، لكن لم يُذكر عنه أنه أخذ عنه ، المولود سنة ۱۲۸۳هـ، والمتوفى سنة ١٣٣٢ هـ ، وله من العمر ٤٩ سنة، وله أكثر من سبعين مصنفاً، قال (۱) ص ٥٥ ، حاشية رقم (٢).

عن الميداني:

كان عالماً فاضلاً صالحاً تقياً كاملاً تفوق في الفقه، واشتهر به، وصنف مصنفات حسنة، ورسائل كثيرة.

وكان حَسَن السَّمْت، جميل الطريقة، محبّباً في الناس، لا سيما في محلة الميدان معتقداً، ولم يَزَل على طريقته المثلى إلى أن توفي رحمه الله تعالى (۱). اهـ

ثناء المؤرخ محمد أديب تقي الدين الحصني :

قال العلامة المؤرّخ الأستاذ محمد أديب تقي الدين بن محمد بـن عبد القادر الحصني الحسيني الدمشقي، المولود سنة ١٢٩٢هـ، والمتوفى سنة ١٣٥٨هـ ، وهو يصف الشيخ عبد الغني الغنيمي:

وبالجملة فإنه كان من جهابذة العلماء المحققين، والفقهاء الورعين المخلصين، لا يَمَل عن الإفادة، ولا يستنكف عن الاستفادة، صفاته النصيحة والإرشاد إلى الخَلْق، وعدم الالتفات إلى ما في أيديهم.

له ولع في إعمار المساجد والمعابد، وزيارة المشاهد والمعاهد، (۱) تعطير المشام في مآثر دمشق الشام، بخط المؤلف، أفادني بصورة صفحة منه، فيها ترجمة الميداني: الأستاذ محمد بن ناصر العجمي الكويتي، جزاه الله خيراً . وللشيخ جمال القاسمي ترجمة في حلية البشر ٤٣٢/١ ، وتاريخ علماء دمشق في القرن الثالث عشر الهجري ٢٨٧/١، والأعلام ١٣٥/٢.
‘Amin, Amin.’ End. Chapter One: Biography of the Distinguished Scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani. Introduction. The distinguished scholar Sheikh Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghuddah, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned in his editing of the book ‘Kashf al-Iltibas’ (1) and said: ‘Thus it was written in the manuscript copy before me, so I recorded it as it is.’ End. A praise found on the face of a copy of al-Lubab: I found on a manuscript copy of the book al-Lubab by al-Maidani, copied during the author’s lifetime, one year after its composition, deposited in the Egyptian National Library, number (2136) Hanafi fiqh, written upon it the following: ‘And this book was compiled by the scholar, the distinguished, the preeminent, the sea of understanding, my master, the scholar, the gnostic, Abd al-Ghani al-Ghunaymi al-Maidani, may Allah benefit us in this world and the next, and pour upon us from his knowledge.’ End. The praise of Sheikh Muhammad Jamal al-Din al-Qasimi al-Dimashqi: The distinguished scholar Sheikh Muhammad Jamal al-Din ibn Muhammad Sa‘id ibn Qasim al-Hallaq al-Husayni al-Qasimi al-Dimashqi said – he was of the same generation as al-Maidani’s students, but it is not mentioned that he studied with him, born in 1283 AH, died in 1332 AH, lived 49 years, and authored more than seventy works – he said (1) p. 55, footnote no. (2) concerning al-Maidani: ‘He was a virtuous, pious, devout, complete scholar, excelled in fiqh and became famous for it, and authored good works and many treatises. He was of good appearance, beautiful manner, beloved among people, especially in the Maidan district, held in high esteem, and he continued on his excellent way until he passed away, may Allah have mercy on him.’ End. The praise of the historian Muhammad Adib Taqi al-Din al-Husni: The distinguished historian Professor Muhammad Adib Taqi al-Din ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Qadir al-Husni al-Husayni al-Dimashqi said – born in 1292 AH, died in 1358 AH – describing Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Ghunaymi: ‘In summary, he was one of the preeminent investigative scholars, and the pious sincere jurists, never tired of giving benefit, nor too proud to seek benefit; his qualities were sincerity and guidance to creation, and not paying attention to what is in people’s hands. He had a passion for building mosques and places of worship, and visiting shrines and institutes.’ (1) ‘Ta‘tir al-Masham fi Ma’athir Dimashq al-Sham’ in the author’s handwriting, he provided me with a page image, including the biography of al-Maidani: Professor Muhammad ibn Nasir al-‘Ajami al-Kuwaiti, may Allah reward him well. And Sheikh Jamal al-Qasimi has a biography in Hilyat al-Bashar 1/432, and Tarikh ‘Ulama’ Dimashq in the 13th century Hijri 1/287, and al-A‘lam 2/135.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch (tarjama) of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani, the author of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. It is not a fiqh ruling but a front matter section that establishes the scholarly authority of the author by presenting praises from three sources. The text opens with a prefatory note by the editor, Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghuddah, citing a manuscript endorsement from a copy of al-Lubab written during al-Maidani’s lifetime. This endorsement extols the author as a preeminent scholar and gnostic. Next, praise from Muhammad Jamal al-Din al-Qasimi emphasizes al-Maidani’s excellence in fiqh, his piety, and his popularity in the Maidan district. Finally, the historian Muhammad Adib Taqi al-Din al-Husni lauds al-Maidani as an investigative scholar and sincere jurist, highlighting his dedication to teaching and his passion for building mosques. The footnotes provide references for these sources. This section serves to authenticate the author’s standing in the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
اللُّبَاب (al-Lubab): The quintessence – title of al-Maidani's commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar.
تَرْجَمَة (tarjama): Biographical sketch or entry.
جَهْبَذ (jahbadh): Preeminent scholar, one with deep knowledge and thorough investigation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The biography of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani, compiled from multiple scholarly praises, authenticates his authority as a Hanafi jurist and underscores the reliability of his work *al-Lubab*.

The Life and Scholarly Stature of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani
Biographical introduction to the author of al-Lubab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key biographical facts about Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani and explain why his credentials as a Hanafi faqīh and uṣūlī validate his commentary al-Lubab.

Core Idea
A scholar's biography establishes the authority of his work; al-Maidani's mastery in fiqh and usul makes al-Lubab a reliable source.

Before diving into the text of al-Lubab, it is essential to know the man behind the commentary. This lesson introduces you to Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani — a scholar of immense virtue, deep fiqh knowledge, and methodological rigor. Understanding his background will give you confidence in his interpretations and rulings throughout this commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his basic profile
Scan the passage for the author's full name, title, and general description. Note that he is referred to as 'al-ʿallāmah' (eminent scholar) and 'al-shaykh' (respected teacher).
2
Extract his key attributes mentioned directly
Look for adjectives and phrases: 'virtuous, righteous, pious, perfect scholar', 'excelled in fiqh', 'authored good works'. This gives a baseline of his character and specialization.
3
Analyze the testimonial from historian Muhammad Adeeb al-Husni
Read the praise from al-Husni. Note terms like 'jahabidha' (brilliant scholars) and 'fuqaha' al-war'i' (righteous jurists). Identify the qualities highlighted: sincerity, constant teaching, humility, building mosques, visiting shrines, accompanying the poor.
Al-Husni met al-Maidani as a child, which adds a personal touch.
4
Analyze the testimonial from Muhammad Kurd Ali
Kurd Ali was a student of al-Maidani's student, so he is a second-hand source. He describes al-Maidani as 'faqīh uṣūlī naẓẓār' (jurist, usuli, insightful), 'wasī' al-māddah' (broad in material), and 'baʿīd al-naẓar' (far-sighted). He also emphasizes his piety and role in shaping his student Tahir al-Jazairi.
5
Synthesize why these credentials matter for al-Lubab
Combine the attributes: piety ensures fear of Allah, depth in fiqh ensures accuracy of rulings, usul expertise ensures methodologically sound derivations. This justifies relying on his commentary over others.
This step bridges biography to fiqh study.

Chapter One: Biography of the eminent scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani
About al-Maidani:
He was a virtuous, righteous, pious, and perfect scholar. He excelled in fiqh and became famous for it. He authored good books and many treatises.
He was of good appearance, beautiful method, beloved among the people, especially in the al-Maidan district, held in esteem. He continued on his excellent path until he passed away, may Allah have mercy on him. End.
Praise of the historian Muhammad Adeeb Taqi al-Din al-Husni:
The eminent historian teacher Muhammad Adeeb Taqi al-Din ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Qadir al-Husni al-Husayni al-Dimashqi, born 1292 AH, died 1358 AH, describing Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Ghunaimi:
In summary, he was among the brilliant investigating scholars, the righteous sincere jurists. He never tired of giving benefit, nor was he too proud to learn. His qualities included sincerity, guidance to creation, and disregard for what was in people's hands.
He had a fondness for building mosques and places of worship, visiting shrines and institutions, adhering to dhikr, and mixing with the poor and needy.
He traveled to the Hijaz many times and took knowledge from its scholars. I met him with my father in his house. End.
Praise of the student of al-Maidani's student, teacher Muhammad Kurd Ali:
The historian linguist (Muhammad Kurd Ali) Muhammad ibn Abd al-Razzaq, born 1293 AH, died 1372 AH, said in the context of mentioning his teacher Sheikh Tahir al-Jazairi:
... Then he connected with the scholar of his era, Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani al-Ghunaimi, the faqih, usuli, and insightful one. He was broad in material of Islamic sciences, far-sighted...
Sheikh al-Maidani possessed great piety and scrupulousness, representing an image of the righteous predecessors. He stamped Sheikh (Tahir) with his own character and raised him on the soundest scientific and religious foundations. End.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to the author of al-Lubab, Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. It is front matter presenting the author's credentials and reputation. The text first gives a general description: he was a virtuous, righteous, and perfect scholar who excelled in fiqh, authored beneficial works, and was beloved in his community. Then it quotes two figures: first, the historian Muhammad Adeeb Taqi al-Din al-Husni, who praises him as among the brilliant investigating scholars and righteous jurists, highlighting his sincerity, constant teaching, and humility in learning. Notably, al-Husni visited him as a young child. Second, Muhammad Kurd Ali, a student of al-Maidani's student (Tahir al-Jazairi), describes al-Maidani as a faqih, usuli, and insightful scholar with vast knowledge of Islamic sciences, great piety resembling the salaf. This establishes al-Maidani's authority and reliability as a Hanafi scholar, setting the stage for his commentary on al-Quduri.

Key Terms
العلامة (al-ʿallāmah): In this text, it is a title for a highly learned scholar, indicating mastery and eminence.
الشيخ (al-shaykh): Used as an honorific for a respected elder and teacher.
الفقيه الأصولي (al-faqīh al-uṣūlī): A jurist who is also an expert in usul al-fiqh (legal methodology).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani was a righteous, highly learned Hanafi faqīh and uṣūlī, whose exemplary character and scholarly depth make his commentary al-Lubab a valuable and authoritative work.

Biography of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani: A Hanafi Scholar's Legacy
Biography of al-Maidani with a story about his Christian student

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the scholarly qualities of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani and explain the significance of a non-Muslim studying Hanafi fiqh under him.

Core Idea
A Hanafi scholar's piety and broad-mindedness can transcend sectarian barriers, using knowledge to defend Islam.

This passage from the introduction to al-Lubab presents a biographical sketch of its author, Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. It highlights his character as a jurist free from bigotry, and narrates a remarkable story of a Christian scholar who studied Hanafi fiqh under him. Understanding this context helps us appreciate the openness of Hanafi scholarship and its commitment to truth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source and context
The passage is from the biography of al-Maidani, quoting Muhammad Kurd Ali's book 'al-Mu'asirun'. Recognize that this is a prefatory biographical note in a fiqh text.
Biographical sections often precede main works to establish the author's authority.
2
Extract al-Maidani's qualities
From the text, note keywords: 'knowledgeable of his time', 'far from bigotry', 'upon the path of the righteous predecessors', 'piety and asceticism'.
These qualities are exemplary for a Hanafi scholar.
3
Understand al-Shartuni's motive
Al-Shartuni studied Hanafi fiqh to become a judge in Lebanon where Islamic law applied.
This shows that Islamic law was the official law in Lebanon at the time.
4
Analyze the conflict
Al-Shartuni encountered the claim that Islamic fiqh is derived from Roman law. He resolved to compare Roman and Hanafi law to refute it.
This reflects the importance of defending Islamic law against external criticisms.
5
Evaluate the author's commentary
The later commentator suggests al-Maidani may have hoped for al-Shartuni's conversion, and criticizes other scholars' refusal to teach him as ignorance and bigotry, but advises polite expression.
The commentator balances critique with adab (proper conduct).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني

وقال الأستاذ محمد كرد علي أيضاً في كتابه : «المعاصرون»(۱) في ترجمة شيخه الشيخ طاهر الجزائري، وهو يتحدث عن أبرز شيوخه: ثم اتصل بعالم عصره الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني الغنيمي، وكان فقيهاً عارفاً بزمانه واسع النظر بعيداً عن التعصب والجمود، على قدم السلف الصالح، لتقواه وزهده». اهـ

وقال أيضاً (۲) في ترجمة الأستاذ سعيد بن عبد الله بن ميخائيل ابن إلياس بن الخوري شاهين الراعي الشرتوني اللبناني النصراني، صاحب : أقرب الموارد»، في اللغة، المتوفى سنة ١٣٣٠هـ: وأخذ خلال مقامه بدمشق الفقه الحنفي عن أكبر فقهـاء عـصـره العلامة عبد الغني الغنيمي الميداني، تلميذ سيد الفقهاء المتأخرين العلامة السيد محمد عابدين صاحب الحاشية، وكان يقصد من درس فقه أبي حنيفة أن يعود إلى لبنان، ويتولى القضاء فيه، وكانت الشريعة نافذة الأحكام، ولا سبيل إلى تفوق القضاة في أقضيتهم إلا بالبراعة فيها.

وصادفته مرةً في ساحة البرج في بيروت، يتأبط كتاباً، فسألته عما فقال : أما سمعت الضجة القائمة هذه الأيام، بدعوى أن الفقه الإسلامي مأخوذ من الفقه الروماني، لا من الكتاب والسنة والإجماع والقياس؟
فقلت له : سمعت ذلك.
فقال : إني أنوي أن أدفع هذه الفرية عن الفقه، ولا يتيسر لي ذلك إلا إذا رجعت إلى الفقه الروماني نفسه، وعارضته بالفقه الحنفي، ولما كانت لغتي الفرنسية ضعيفة، أحببتُ أن أقويها؛ لأتمكن من نَقل قانون (يوس تنيانوس) من الفرنسية إلى العربية، ثم أقابل بـيـن مـواده وبين فقهنا، فأنا منذ أشهر أشتغل بإحكام اللغة الفرنسية.

ثم قال الأستاذ محمد كرد علي: وبعد حين نشر في مجلة (المقتطف) سلسلة مقالات، دَفَعَ فيها عن الفقه الإسلامي مـا افـتـراه المتحذلقون عليه.
وكأنه بعمله هذا كافاً شيخه العلامة الغنيمي، على تلقينـه فقـه الإسلام، في زمن كان غيره من فقهاء دمشق يأبون أن يعلموه إياه ؛ جهلا وتعصبا». اهـ.

قلت : لكل من العلماء وجهةٌ هو موليها، ولكل اجتهاده، فهـم وراث النبوة، وأُمَنَاء الله على دينه وشرعه، ولعل الشيخ الميداني حين علم الشرتوني هذا كان يرجي من هذا القانوني النصراني إسلاماً، أو نفعاً للمسلمين. وأما قوله: «إن غير الميداني لم يعلمه جهلاً وتعصباً»: فأقول : إن التزام عبارات الأدب هو الأصل، ثم إن السبب واضح لكل ذي بصر. وأيضاً قول الأستاذ كرد على: وكأنه بعمله كافـا شـيـخه»: فيقال :
Chapter One: Biography of the eminent scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani

Professor Muhammad Kurd Ali also said in his book 'al-Mu'asirun' (1) in the biography of his teacher Sheikh Tahir al-Jaza'iri, while he speaks about his most prominent teachers: Then he connected with the scholar of his era, Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani al-Ghanimi, and he was a jurist, knowledgeable of his time, broad-sighted, far from bigotry and rigidity, upon the path of the righteous predecessors, due to his piety and asceticism. End quote.

He also said (2) in the biography of Professor Sa'id bin Abdullah bin Mikhail bin Ilyas bin al-Khuri Shahin al-Ra'i al-Shartuni al-Lubnani al-Nasrani, author of 'Aqrab al-Mawarid' in language, who died in 1330 AH: During his stay in Damascus, he studied Hanafi fiqh under the greatest jurist of his time, the scholar Abdul Ghani al-Ghanimi al-Maidani, the student of the master of later jurists, the scholar Sayyid Muhammad Abidin, author of the Hashiyah. He intended from studying the fiqh of Abu Hanifa to return to Lebanon and take up judging there, for the Sharia was the effective law, and there was no way for judges to excel in their judgments except through skill in it.

Once I encountered him in the Burj Square in Beirut, carrying a book under his arm, and I asked him about it, and he said: Have you not heard the uproar these days, concerning the claim that Islamic fiqh is taken from Roman law, not from the Book, the Sunnah, consensus, and analogy?
I said to him: I have heard that.
He said: I intend to refute this slander against fiqh, and that will not be easy for me unless I go back to Roman law itself and compare it to Hanafi fiqh. Since my French is weak, I wanted to strengthen it so I could translate Justinian's Code from French to Arabic, then compare its articles with our fiqh. So I have been working for months to master the French language.

Then Professor Muhammad Kurd Ali said: After a while, he published a series of articles in 'al-Muqtaqif' magazine, in which he defended Islamic fiqh against what the pretentious had fabricated against it.
As if by this work he was repaying his teacher, the scholar al-Ghanimi, for teaching him the fiqh of Islam, at a time when other jurists of Damascus refused to teach him out of ignorance and bigotry. End quote.

I say: Each scholar has a direction he pursues, and each has his ijtihad. They are the inheritors of prophethood and the trustees of Allah over His religion and law. Perhaps Sheikh al-Maidani, when he taught al-Shartuni, hoped that this Christian legal scholar would embrace Islam, or bring benefit to Muslims. As for his statement: 'Others besides al-Maidani did not teach him out of ignorance and bigotry,' I say: Adhering to polite expressions is the principle, and the reason is clear to everyone with insight. Also, the statement of Professor Kurd Ali: 'As if by this work he was repaying his teacher' — it is said: ...
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani, taken from the writings of Muhammad Kurd Ali. It opens by describing al-Maidani as a jurist who was knowledgeable of his time, broad in perspective, free from fanaticism, and following the way of the Salaf. Then it tells the story of a Christian scholar, Sa'id al-Shartuni, who studied Hanafi fiqh under al-Maidani. Al-Shartuni wanted to become a judge in Lebanon, where Islamic law was applied. After completing his studies, al-Shartuni encountered a claim that Islamic jurisprudence was derived from Roman law. He resolved to compare Roman law with Hanafi fiqh to refute this slander, and to do so, he strengthened his French. Later, he published articles in al-Muqtaqif defending Islamic fiqh. The author (likely a later commentator) adds that al-Maidani may have hoped for al-Shartuni's conversion, and that the refusal of other scholars to teach him was due to ignorance and bigotry, though this should be said politely.

Key Terms
العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني (al-ʿAllāmah al-Shaykh ʿAbd al-Ghanī al-Maydānī): The author of al-Lubab, a Hanafi jurist known for his commentary on al-Quduri
الفقيه الحنفي (al-faqīh al-ḥanafī): A jurist specializing in the Hanafi school
الشرتوني (al-Shartūnī): A Christian scholar who studied Hanafi fiqh under al-Maidani

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What motivated the Christian scholar al-Shartuni to learn Hanafi fiqh?
A) To become a teacher in a madrasa
B) To return to Lebanon and serve as a judge under Islamic law
C) To convert to Islam
D) To translate the Quran

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi scholar's character—piety, knowledge, openness—enables the defense and transmission of fiqh even to non-Muslims, countering false claims against Islamic law.
