Biography of Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani
Presents biographical details and scholarly praise of al-Maydani.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to summarize the life and scholarly mission of Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani as described in the passage.

Core Idea
Al-Maydani learned French and studied Roman law to defend Hanafi fiqh from its critics.

This lesson introduces you to the eminent Hanafi scholar Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, author of 'Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri'. You will learn about his unique project of comparing Hanafi fiqh with Roman law to refute slanders against Islamic jurisprudence, and see how he was praised by later scholars for his piety and contributions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar and his project
Read al-Maydani's own words about his intention to compare Roman law (Justinian's Code) with Hanafi fiqh and his reason for learning French.
This shows his proactive defense of Islamic law.
2
Analyze the praise from Muhammad Kurd Ali
Consider Kurd Ali's account of al-Maydani teaching him fiqh when other Damascene scholars refused, and his assessment that later articles in Al-Muqtataf were a repayment.
Note the editor's critique of this 'repayment' claim.
3
Examine the editor's interjection
Reflect on the editor's defense of al-Maydani and his suggestion that al-Maydani may have hoped for the Christian lawyer's conversion or benefit to Muslims.
This highlights scholarly ethics and diverse intentions.
4
Study the praises from al-Shatti and Abu Ghuddah
Review the descriptions of al-Maydani's asceticism, piety, charity, and his renovation of a mosque, as well as Abu Ghuddah's editorial work on his treatises.
These establish his character and legacy.

الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني
فقلت له : سمعت ذلك.
فقال : إني أنوي أن أدفع هذه الفرية عن الفقه، ولا يتيسر لي ذلك إلا إذا رجعت إلى الفقه الروماني نفسه، وعارضته بالفقه الحنفي، ولما كانت لغتي الفرنسية ضعيفة، أحببتُ أن أقويها؛ لأتمكن من نَقل قانون (يوس تنيانوس) من الفرنسية إلى العربية، ثم أقابل بـيـن مـواده وبين فقهنا، فأنا منذ أشهر أشتغل بإحكام اللغة الفرنسية.
:
ثم قال الأستاذ محمد كرد علي وبعد حين نشر في مجلة (المقتطف) سلسلة مقالات، دَفَعَ فيها عن الفقه الإسلامي مـا افـتـراه المتحذلقون عليه.
وكأنه بعمله هذا كافاً شيخه العلامة الغنيمي، على تلقينـه فقـه الإسلام، في زمن كان غيره من فقهاء دمشق يأبون أن يعلموه إياه ؛ جهلا وتعصبا». اهـ.
قلت : لكل من العلماء وجهةٌ هو موليها، ولكل اجتهاده، فهـم وراث النبوة، وأُمَنَاء الله على دينه وشرعه، ولعل الشيخ الميداني حين علم الشرتوني هذا كان يرجي من هذا القانوني النصراني إسلاماً، أو نفعاً للمسلمين. وأما قوله: «إن غير الميداني لم يعلمه جهلاً وتعصباً»: فأقول : إن التزام عبارات الأدب هو الأصل، ثم إن السبب واضح لكل ذي بصر. وأيضاً قول الأستاذ كرد على وكأنه بعمله كافـا شـيـخه»: فيقال أيضاً : لا ، وأين هو من مكافأته للميداني بما علمه؟
ثناء تلميذ تلميذ الميداني الشيخ محمد جميل الشطي
قال العلامة الشيخ محمـد بـن عمـر الشطي، المولود سنة ١٣٠٠هـ، والمتوفى سنة ١٣٧٩هـ، حين وصف الميداني وهـو يلخص ترجمته من حلية البشر:
كان ذا زهد وتقوى، وعبادة في السر والنجوى، وهمة عالية، ومروءة سامية، ولسان على الذكر دائب ، وشهرة سارت في المشارق والمغارب، وكان له خيرات حسنة، ومساع مستحسنة، وقـد جـدد عمارة الجامع الذي بجانب داره في الميدان، في ساحة السخانة بالميدان، وأنشأ له منارة عظيمة، واتَّسع جاهه، وكثر في الناس ثناؤه، وخالطت هيبته القلوب، ونال أجل مطلوب ومرغوب، إلى غير ذلك»(۱). اهـ
ثناء العلامة الشيخ عبد الفتاح أبو غدة رحمه الله :
وصف العلامة الشيخ عبد الفتاح أبو غدة، المتوفى سنة ١٤١٧هـ، حين ترجم للميداني في مقدمة تحقيقه لرسالة الميداني : «كشف الالتباس» (۲) ، ورسالته : تُحفة النُّسَاك»، فقـال وهـو يـصـوغ
Chapter One: Biography of the eminent scholar Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. I said to him: I heard that. He said: I intend to refute this slander against fiqh, and that will not be possible for me except if I return to Roman law itself and compare it with Hanafi fiqh. Since my French was weak, I wanted to strengthen it in order to translate the law of Justinian from French into Arabic, then compare its articles with our fiqh. So for months I have been working on mastering the French language. Then Professor Muhammad Kurd Ali said: After a while, he published a series of articles in Al-Muqtataf magazine, defending Islamic fiqh from the fabrications of the pretentious scholars against it. As if by this work he was repaying his teacher, the eminent scholar al-Ghanimi, for teaching him the fiqh of Islam at a time when other scholars of Damascus refused to teach him due to ignorance and bigotry. End quote. I say: Every scholar has his own perspective and his own ijtihad. They are the inheritors of prophethood and the trustees of Allah over His religion and law. Perhaps Shaykh al-Maydani, when he taught al-Shartuni this, hoped that this Christian legal scholar would embrace Islam, or benefit Muslims. As for his saying: 'Others besides al-Maydani did not teach him out of ignorance and bigotry,' I say: Adhering to polite phrasing is the principle. Moreover, the reason is clear to any perceptive person. Also, the saying of Professor Kurd Ali, 'As if he was repaying his teacher,' one may say: No, and where is the repayment to al-Maydani for what he taught him? Praise from the student of al-Maydani's student, Shaykh Muhammad Jamil al-Shatti. The eminent scholar Muhammad ibn Umar al-Shatti, born 1300 AH, died 1379 AH, said when describing al-Maydani while summarizing his biography from Hilyat al-Bashar: He was a man of asceticism and piety, worship in private and in counsel, high ambition, noble character, a tongue ever engaged in remembrance, and widespread fame in the East and West. He had good charities and commendable efforts. He renovated the mosque next to his house in al-Maydan, in the Sakhanah area of al-Maydan, and built a great minaret for it. His influence grew, people praised him greatly, awe mixed with hearts, and he attained the most desired and sought after, etc. End quote. Praise from the eminent scholar Shaykh Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghuddah, may Allah have mercy on him. The eminent scholar Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghuddah, died 1417 AH, described al-Maydani when editing his treatise 'Kashf al-Iltibas' and his treatise 'Tuhfat al-Nusak', saying while composing...
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch of the eminent Hanafi scholar Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, the author of 'Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri'. It is part of the front matter of the book. The text includes: 1) Al-Maydani’s own statement about his project to compare Roman law (Justinian’s Code) with Hanafi fiqh in order to defend Islamic fiqh from slanderers. He learned French for this purpose. 2) Praise from Muhammad Kurd Ali, who wrote articles defending Islamic fiqh and credited al-Maydani for teaching him despite opposition from other Damascene scholars. 3) A commentary interjection by the editor (likely the author of this biographical section) defending al-Maydani and critiquing Kurd Ali’s remark about repayment. 4) Additional praise from Muhammad Jamil al-Shatti, highlighting al-Maydani’s piety, charity, and renovation of a mosque. 5) Mention of praise from Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghuddah in his editing of al-Maydani’s works. This passage establishes al-Maydani’s scholarly credentials and his role in defending Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
ترجمة (tarjama): Biographical account of a scholar's life and works.
الفقيه (al-faqih): A scholar of Islamic jurisprudence; here referring to al-Maydani.
يوس تنيانوس (Yus Tinyanus): Presumably a transliteration of 'Justinianus' (Justinian's Code).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To become a fluent French speaker for trade
B) To translate Justinian's Code and compare it with Hanafi fiqh to defend Islamic law
C) To teach French to Muslim students
D) To write a book on comparative religion

Key Takeaway
Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani was a dedicated Hanafi scholar who used comparative legal study to defend Islamic fiqh and was widely praised for his piety and contributions.

Understanding the Scholar Behind the Text
Biographical introduction celebrating the author's virtues

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key virtues mentioned in a Hanafi scholar's biography and explain their significance for establishing scholarly authority.

Core Idea
A scholar's piety and learning lend weight to his fiqh rulings—trust the text by knowing its author.

This lesson explores the biographical introduction to 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani's commentary on al-Quduri. While not a fiqh ruling itself, such biographical notes are crucial in the Hanafi tradition: they confirm the author's reliability and remind readers that fiqh is transmitted by upright scholars. We'll examine the specific virtues praised and understand why they matter for Hanafi jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sources of the biography
Find the two later scholars quoted. Note their full names and death dates.
Muhammad ibn 'Umar al-Shatti (d. 1379 AH) and 'Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghuddah (d. 1417 AH).
2
List the personal qualities highlighted
Extract adjectives describing al-Maydani's character: zuhd, taqwa, 'ibadah, muru'ah, etc.
These are not just flattery; they establish 'adalah (integrity) required for authoritative transmission.
3
Note the external achievements mentioned
Locate references to his charitable works, mosque renovation, and fame.
Such community service increased his credibility and acceptance (qabul) among the people.
4
Understand the purpose of such a biography
Consider why a fiqh commentary begins with the author's life. How does it affect the reader's trust?
In Hanafi tradition, the probity of the compiler is part of the proof; his piety guarantees careful transmission.
5
Connect to your study of the text
Reflect on how knowing the author's character influences your approach to his rulings.
You now read al-Lubab not just as an anonymous commentary, but as the work of a known righteous scholar.

رحم الله الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني ذاك الذي وصف بتلك الأوصاف السابقة، ونال تلك الثناءات العالية، وذلك الفضل من الله.
Chapter One: Biography of the Learned Sheikh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. Also: No, and where is his reward for what he taught al-Maydani? Praise of the student of al-Maydani's student, Sheikh Muhammad Jamil al-Shatti. The learned Sheikh Muhammad ibn 'Umar al-Shatti, born in 1300 AH and died in 1379 AH, said when describing al-Maydani while summarizing his biography from Hilyat al-Bashar: "He was a person of asceticism and piety, worship in secret and whisper, high ambition, sublime chivalry, a tongue constant in remembrance, fame that traveled East and West, he had good charities and commendable endeavors, he renewed the construction of the mosque next to his house in al-Maydan in the Sahat al-Sakhanah area, and built for it a great minaret. His influence expanded, his praise among people increased, his awe mixed with hearts, and he attained the greatest desired and sought-after station, etc." End. Praise of the learned Sheikh 'Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghuddah, may Allah have mercy on him: The learned Sheikh 'Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghuddah, died in 1417 AH, described when he wrote the biography of al-Maydani in the introduction to his editing of al-Maydani's treatise 'Kashf al-Iltibas' and his treatise 'Tuhfat al-Nussak', and he said while composing his praise succinctly based on what he had seen of biographies of al-Maydani: "He was of a high degree in knowledge and virtue, piety, asceticism, broadmindedness, sharpness of opinion, so he attained acceptance in the hearts of people, veneration in souls, great influence, and he occupied the noble and lofty station among the people of Damascus generally." End. May Allah have mercy on Sheikh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, the one described with those previous attributes, and who attained those high praises and that favor from Allah.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction from the front matter of the book 'Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri' by 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. The author's biography is presented through the praises of two later scholars: Muhammad ibn 'Umar al-Shatti (d. 1379 AH) and 'Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghuddah (d. 1417 AH). Muhammad al-Shatti quotes from his work 'Rawd al-Bashar', describing al-Maydani's asceticism, piety, charitable works including renovating a mosque and building a minaret, and his widespread fame. 'Abd al-Fattah Abu Ghuddah, in his introduction to al-Maydani's treatises, praises his high level of knowledge, virtue, and the acceptance he enjoyed among the people of Damascus. This section establishes the scholarly stature and piety of the author, which is important for readers of the fiqh commentary to trust his authority.

Key Terms
ترجمة (tarjamah): Biography; a detailed account of a person's life and accomplishments.
زهد (zuhd): Asceticism; detachment from worldly pleasures and focus on the afterlife.
تقوى (taqwa): Piety; consciousness of Allah and fear of Him, leading to obedience.
مروءة (murū'ah): Chivalry; moral excellence and generosity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The biography of a Hanafi fiqh author reinforces the trustworthiness of his legal transmission by highlighting his piety and community standing.

The Scholar and His Context: Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani and the 1860 Damascus Incident
Biographical praise and historical contextualization of a Hanafi scholar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how biographical context can clarify a scholar's role and defend against historical accusations.

Core Idea
A scholar's piety and knowledge must be understood alongside the historical trials that test his character.

This lesson examines the biography of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, the Hanafi commentator, and a controversial historical event. The passage presents a praise of his virtues and then introduces a note about his alleged involvement in the 1860 sectarian violence. We will analyze how the commentator uses biographical praise to establish credibility and then addresses a potential challenge to that credibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the biographical claims
What virtues does the passage attribute to al-Maydani? Note the specific qualities: knowledge, piety, asceticism, intellect, sound opinion.
These are found in the first paragraph.
2
Recognize the purpose of praise
Why does the editor include such praise? To establish al-Maydani's authority for the commentary.
This is a common method in academic introductions.
3
Recognize the historical note
What is the accusation? That al-Maydani assisted Christians in the 1860 incident.
The section title indicates a verification of this claim.
4
Understand the method of defense
How does the editor respond? By providing context for the incident without directly refuting, leading to a later verification.
The passage only introduces; later sections will resolve.
5
Reflect on the relationship between biography and fiqh
How does the scholar's character affect the reliability of his fiqh works?
In Hanafi tradition, a trustworthy narrator is essential.

الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني
مدحه له بإجمال ما وقف عليه من تراجم للميداني:
وكان على درجة عالية في العلم والفضل، والورع والزهد وسعة العقل، وبَصَارة الرأي، فحصل لـه قبـول في قلوب الناس، وإجلال في النفوس، وجاه عظيم، وحل المقـام الكـريـم الـرفيـع بـيـن أهل دمشق عامة». اهـ

المبحث الرابع
تنبيه فيه تحرير لما ذكره بعضهم من مساعدة الميداني للنصارى في حادثة سنة ١٨٦٠م في دمشق
حادثة دمشق سنة ١٨٦٠م ، عنوان وتاريخ لفتنة عظيمة كانت في
مدينة دمشق، جَرَتْ بين المسلمين، وبين من كان فيها من النصارى، البالغ عددهم عُشر سكان دمشق، وقد قُتِل في هذه الحادثة آلاف من النصارى، وكان سببها فتن بين الطرفين سابقة، وإحن وأحقاد متقدمة، يضيق المجال عن ذكرها، وقد فصلها من كتب عنها. وهكذا تدخلت السلطات العثمانية والسفارات الأجنبية لإيقاف تلك الفتنة، وساعدهم على ذلك وجهاء دمشق، وفريق من علمائها، وكان على رأسهم الأمير عبد القادر الجزائري، وذلك بعد استقراره في دمشق، وتم إطفاء تلك الفتنة، وكـان مـا كـان بعدها، وأعدم كثير من أهالي دمشق ممـن شـارك في تلك الفتنة، وذلك من قبل الوالي العثماني، ونُفي فريق من علماء دمشق ووجهائها إلى قبرص، ثم حكم عليهم بإقامة جبرية في اسطنبول سنوات، ثم فُرج عنهم
Chapter One: Biography of the scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani
Praise for him summarizing what he came across of biographies of al-Maydani:
He was of a high degree in knowledge and virtue, piety and asceticism, breadth of intellect, and sharpness of opinion. So he gained acceptance in the hearts of people, reverence in souls, great prestige, and occupied the noble, high station among the people of Damascus in general." End.
May Allah have mercy on Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, that one who was described with those previous attributes, and attained those high praises, and that grace from Allah.
*****

Fourth Section
A note containing a verification of what some mentioned regarding al-Maydani's assistance to the Christians in the incident of the year 1860 in Damascus.
The Damascus incident of 1860, a title and date for a great tribulation that occurred in the city of Damascus, between the Muslims and those among them of Christians, whose number was a tenth of the population of Damascus. Thousands of Christians were killed in this incident. Its cause was previous strife between the two sides, and prior enmities and hatreds, whose mention would be too lengthy. Those who wrote about it have detailed it. Thus the Ottoman authorities and foreign embassies intervened to stop that strife, and they were aided in that by the notables of Damascus and a group of its scholars, headed by Prince Abd al-Qadir al-Jaza'iri, after his settlement in Damascus. The strife was extinguished, and what happened after it happened. Many of the people of Damascus who participated in that strife were executed by the Ottoman governor, and a group of Damascus scholars and notables were exiled to Cyprus, then they were sentenced to compulsory residence in Istanbul for years, then they were released.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is biographical front matter from the editor/commentator of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. It opens with a concise praise of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, the author of the commentary. The description highlights his high level of knowledge, piety, asceticism, intellectual breadth, and sound judgment, which earned him acceptance and reverence among the people of Damascus. This sets the stage for his credibility as a Hanafi commentator.

The passage then moves to a historical note regarding an incident in 1860 in Damascus, where sectarian violence occurred between Muslims and Christians. The author clarifies that al-Maydani was accused of assisting Christians during this conflict, and thus provides a summary of the event to contextualize the accusation. The summary mentions the large number of casualties, the underlying causes of previous enmities, and the intervention of Ottoman authorities and foreign embassies, with notable figures like Prince Abd al-Qadir al-Jaza'iri playing a role in quelling the strife. The aftermath included executions and exiles of those involved. This historical context is provided to clear al-Maydani's name regarding the accusation, but the passage does not give the full resolution; it only introduces the topic.

Key Terms
الورع (al-wara'): Piety and scrupulousness; a virtue that makes a scholar trustworthy.
الزهد (al-zuhd): Asceticism; detachment from worldly pleasures.
بصارة الرأي (basārat al-ra’y): Sharpness of opinion; sound judgment in legal matters.
حادثة (ḥāditha): An incident or event; specifically the 1860 Damascus sectarian strife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To provide a full historical account of the 1860 Damascus incident
B) To introduce and verify the accusation that al-Maydani assisted Christians in 1860
C) To discuss al-Maydani's scholarly works
D) To praise Prince Abd al-Qadir al-Jaza'iri

Key Takeaway
Biographical context, including historical trials, is essential for critically engaging with a scholar's fiqh contributions.

Refuting a Biographical Claim about al-Maydani
Biographical critique refuting an unsubstantiated claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the evidence for a historical claim about a Hanafi scholar and identify the method of critical verification used in this passage.

Core Idea
A scholar's actions must be verified by multiple independent sources; a single unsupported claim is not sufficient.

This passage addresses a specific controversy about Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani's role during the 1860 fitna in Damascus. The author refutes a claim made by Muhammad Kurd Ali that al-Maydani actively protected Christians. By examining the historical context and the author's critical method, you will learn how biographical claims in the Hanafi tradition are scrutinized for authenticity.

Guided Path
1
Understand the historical context
Read the description of the 1860 fitna in Damascus: a civil strife between Muslims and Christians, resulting in thousands of deaths and intervention by Ottoman authorities. This context is essential to evaluate later claims about al-Maydani's actions.
Note the scale of the event and the involvement of figures like Abd al-Qadir al-Jaza'iri.
2
Identify the specific claim being refuted
Locate the exact claim by Muhammad Kurd Ali: that al-Maydani 'prevented the Muslim youths from attacking their Christian neighbors' and 'saved several thousand from being killed.' Highlight this in the translation.
The claim is specific: al-Maydani used guidance (irshad) to intervene in his quarter (al-Maydan).
3
Analyze the author's rebuttal
Observe the author's words: 'I say: What Professor Muhammad Kurd Ali mentioned... has not been mentioned—as far as I have seen—by anyone who wrote a biography of al-Maydani, neither his students, nor his contemporaries and admirers, nor even those who specialized in this incident.' This is the core of the refutation: lack of corroboration.
The author does not provide a counter-narrative; he simply notes the absence of supporting sources.
4
Evaluate the strength of the rebuttal
Consider whether lack of corroboration is sufficient to disprove a historical claim. The author's methodology is one of verification through multiple attestations, a standard in Islamic biographical criticism.
Think about what additional evidence might strengthen or weaken the refutation.

الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني
المبحث الرابع
تنبيه فيه تحرير لما ذكره بعضهم من مساعدة الميداني للنصارى في حادثة سنة ١٨٦٠م في دمشق
حادثة دمشق سنة ١٨٦٠م ، عنوان وتاريخ لفتنة عظيمة كانت في
مدينة دمشق، جَرَتْ بين المسلمين، وبين من كان فيها من النصارى، البالغ عددهم عُشر سكان دمشق، وقد قُتِل في هذه الحادثة آلاف من النصارى، وكان سببها فتن بين الطرفين سابقة، وإحن وأحقاد
متقدمة، يضيق المجال عن ذكرها، وقد فصلها من كتب عنها. وهكذا تدخلت السلطات العثمانية والسفارات الأجنبية
لإيقاف تلك الفتنة، وساعدهم على ذلك وجهاء دمشق، وفريق من علمائها، وكان على رأسهم الأمير عبد القادر الجزائري، وذلك بعد استقراره في دمشق، وتم إطفاء تلك الفتنة، وكـان مـا كـان بعدها، وأعدم كثير من أهالي دمشق ممـن شـارك في تلك الفتنة، وذلك من قبل الوالي العثماني، ونُفي فريق من علماء دمشق ووجهائها إلى قبرص، ثم حكم عليهم بإقامة جبرية في اسطنبول سنوات، ثم فُرج عنهم
(1)
(1) ينظر تحفة الزائر في مآثر الأمير عبد القادر، لابنه محمد ٩٢/٢، حادثة

وهكذا، فقد ذكر بعض المترجمين للشيخ عبد الغني الميداني أن الميداني شارك في مساعدة النصارى في تلك الفتنة، وأنه آواهـم، ودَفَع ودافع عنهم، ونحو هذا ، وبسبب توسعي في ترجمة الميداني، أردت هنا التنبية إلى هذا الأمر، وتجلية حقيقة ما نُسب إليه، وبيان عدم صحة ما ذكر عن الميداني في ذلك.
وممن ذَكَرَ هذا عن الميداني: مدير المجمع اللغوي في دمشق الأستاذ محمد كرد علي المولود سنة ١٢٩٣هـ، والمتوفى سنة ١٣٧٢ هـ ، وذلك في ترجمة أستاذه العلامة الشيخ طاهر الجزائري الدمشقي، وهو يذكر مشايخ الشيخ طاهر ، وعد منهم العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني، وبعد ثنائه عليه قال:
«وهو الذي حال بإرشاده في حادثة سنة ١٨٦٠م بدمشق دون تعدي فتيان المسلمين على جيرانهم المسيحيين في محلَّته ـ أي الميدان ، فأنقذ بجميل وعظه، وحُسنِ تأثيره بضعة ألوف من القتل في تلك المذابح المشؤومة»(۱). اهـ
قلت: ما ذكره الأستاذ محمد كرد علي عن الشيخ الميداني لم يذكره ـ فيما اطلعت عليه ـ أحد ممن ترجم للميداني، لا من تلاميذه، ولا من معاصريه ومحبيه، بل ولا ممَّن خص هذه الحادثة
دمشق سنة ١٨٦٠م، للحَسيبي الحسيني (مخطوط)، حسر اللثام عن نكبات الشام،
لمكاريوس، ص ٢٢٢.
(۱) كنوز الأجداد .
Chapter One: Biography of the scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani
Fourth Section
A Note: A clarification of what some have mentioned about al-Maydani's assistance to the Christians in the incident of the year 1860 in Damascus
The Damascus incident of 1860 is a title and a date for a great tribulation that occurred in the city of Damascus, which took place between the Muslims and the Christians who were there, whose number reached a tenth of Damascus's population. Thousands of Christians were killed in this incident, and its cause was previous conflicts between the two parties and ancient grudges and hatreds, which the space is too narrow to mention, and those who wrote about it have detailed it. Thus, the Ottoman authorities and foreign embassies intervened to stop that tribulation, and the notables of Damascus and a group of its scholars helped them, led by Prince Abd al-Qadir al-Jaza'iri, after his settlement in Damascus. That tribulation was extinguished, and what happened after it happened. Many of the people of Damascus who participated in that tribulation were executed by the Ottoman governor, and a group of Damascus scholars and notables were exiled to Cyprus, then they were sentenced to forced residence in Istanbul for years, then they were released.
(1) See: Tuhfat al-Za'ir fi Ma'athir al-Amir Abd al-Qadir, by his son Muhammad, 2/92, the incident...

Thus, some biographers of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani mentioned that al-Maydani participated in helping the Christians in that tribulation, that he gave them refuge, defended, and protected them, and similar things. Due to my expansion in the biography of al-Maydani, I wanted here to draw attention to this matter, to clarify the truth of what was attributed to him, and to demonstrate the incorrectness of what was mentioned about al-Maydani in that regard.
Among those who mentioned this about al-Maydani: the director of the Linguistic Academy in Damascus, Professor Muhammad Kurd Ali, born in 1293 AH, died in 1372 AH, in his biography of his teacher, the scholar Sheikh Tahir al-Jaza'iri al-Dimashqi. He mentions the teachers of Sheikh Tahir, and among them he counted the scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. After praising him, he said: 'It was he who, with his guidance during the incident of 1860 in Damascus, prevented the Muslim youths from attacking their Christian neighbors in his quarter—i.e., al-Maydan—thus saving, through his beautiful exhortation and good influence, several thousand from being killed in those ill-omened massacres.' (1) End quote.
I say: What Professor Muhammad Kurd Ali mentioned about Sheikh al-Maydani has not been mentioned—as far as I have seen—by anyone who wrote a biography of al-Maydani, neither his students, nor his contemporaries and admirers, nor even those who specialized in this incident.
Damascus year 1860, by al-Hasibi al-Husayni (manuscript), Hashr al-Litham 'an Nakabat al-Sham, by Makarius, p. 222.
(1) Kunuz al-Ajdad.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This is a biographical passage from the editor's introduction to al-Maydani's work. The author (the editor) provides a clarification regarding an allegation made by Muhammad Kurd Ali in his biography of Tahir al-Jaza'iri. The allegation is that Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani actively helped Christians during the 1860 Damascus massacre by preventing Muslim youths from attacking their Christian neighbors. The author refutes this, stating that he has not found any other biographer, student, or contemporary who confirms this claim. The author's aim is to defend al-Maydani's reputation by questioning the authenticity of this narrative. The passage first describes the historical context of the 1860 fitna (civil strife) in Damascus, including the involvement of Ottoman authorities and local notables like Abd al-Qadir al-Jaza'iri. Then it presents Muhammad Kurd Ali's specific claim, and finally the author's rebuttal, emphasizing that this claim is not corroborated by other sources. This is a critical refinement of al-Maydani's biography, typical of scholarly works that seek to verify historical accounts.

Key Terms
فتنة (fitna): A great trial or civil strife, specifically the 1860 violence in Damascus between Muslims and Christians.
ترجمة (tarjama): Biographical entry; this section is a biography (tarjama) of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the author's main argument against the claim that al-Maydani helped Christians in 1860?
A) Al-Maydani was too busy teaching to intervene.
B) The claim is not supported by any other biographer or contemporary source.
C) The Ottoman authorities forbade him from helping.
D) Al-Maydani was in exile at the time.

Key Takeaway
Historical claims about scholars require corroboration from multiple independent sources; a single report without support is not accepted.

Evaluating Historical Narratives: The Case of al-Maydani and the 1860 Events
Biographical defense with source criticism

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the reliability of a historical claim about a Hanafi scholar using source criticism (jarh wa ta'dil).

Core Idea
Trace a claim to its source; if the source is weak, reject the claim.

Historians sometimes repeat claims about scholars without verifying their origin. This passage from a biography of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani demonstrates how a careful scholar investigates the chain of transmission (isnad) of a historical report. You will learn to apply similar critical thinking to protect the integrity of biographical narratives.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
Read the passage and determine what exactly is being attributed to al-Maydani: that he helped Christians during the 1860 Damascus incident.
The claim is that he used his influence to prevent attacks.
2
Identify the source of the claim
Find who originally made the claim. The passage names Muhammad Kurd Ali, then traces it further back to Shahin Makaryus's book 'Hasr al-Litham'.
The author argues that this is the only source.
3
Check earlier biographers
See if earlier, more reliable sources mention this. The author states that none of al-Maydani's students, contemporaries, or later detailed historians mention it.
Silence of reliable sources is evidence against the claim.
4
Evaluate the credibility of the source
Assess the trustworthiness of Shahin Makaryus. The author notes he was a Lebanese Christian who served Jewish and Masonic interests, implying bias.
The author uses external criticism (jarh) to weaken the source.
5
Conclude on reliability
Based on the weak chain and unreliable source, the author concludes the claim is incorrect. You should do the same in similar cases.
This is a necessary skill for preserving accurate scholarly legacy.

Chapter One: Biography of the scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani
And thus, some biographers of Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani have mentioned that al-Maydani participated in helping the Christians in that sedition, and that he sheltered them, defended them, and so on. Due to my extensive treatment of al-Maydani's biography, I wanted here to draw attention to this matter, to clarify the truth of what has been attributed to him, and to demonstrate the incorrectness of what has been mentioned about al-Maydani in this regard.
Among those who mentioned this about al-Maydani is the director of the Arabic Language Academy in Damascus, Professor Muhammad Kurd Ali, born in 1293 AH and died in 1372 AH, in his biography of his teacher, the scholar Sheikh Tahir al-Jaza'iri al-Dimashqi, where he lists the teachers of Sheikh Tahir, among them the scholar Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. After praising him, he said:
'It was he who, by his guidance in the incident of 1860 CE in Damascus, prevented the Muslim youth from attacking their Christian neighbors in his quarter—i.e., al-Midan—and thus saved, through his good counsel and fine influence, several thousand from being killed in those sinister massacres.'(1)
I say: What Professor Muhammad Kurd Ali mentioned about Sheikh al-Maydani has not been mentioned—as far as I have seen—by anyone who wrote a biography of al-Maydani, neither by his students, nor by his contemporaries and admirers, nor even by those who specifically authored on this incident of Damascus in 1860 CE, or wrote about it in detail, except for those who followed Professor Muhammad Kurd Ali among the contemporaries, such as the author of Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin, and also the author of the book 'Ulama' Dimashq wa A'yaniha fi al-Qarn al-Thalith 'Ashar al-Hijri' in his biography of al-Maydani, and likewise in his biography of him in the introduction to his edition of al-Maydani's book Sharh al-'Aqidah al-Tahawiyyah.
He even said in this introduction (3): 'The greatest of his merits was his assistance in the incident of the sixties... and if al-Maydani had no other merit than this, it would suffice him.' End quote?! I say: The origin of the statement of Professor Muhammad Kurd Ali and those who followed him is taken—and Allah knows best—from the book 'Hasr al-Litham 'an Nakabat al-Sham', authored by one of the great Lebanese Christians, Shahin ibn Makaryus (5) (1269–1328 AH), who served the Jews and Freemasonry in his writings and elsewhere, as mentioned by al-Zirkili and others, and his father was among those killed in...
(1) Kunuz al-Ajdad, p. 222.
(5) See his biography in Fayd al-Malik al-Wahhab al-Muta'ali 1/691, al-A'lam 3/153, Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin 4/292.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a biographical critique. The author, likely a later editor or commentator, defends Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani (a Hanafi scholar known for his commentary on al-Quduri) against a specific historical accusation: that he helped Christians during the 1860 sectarian violence in Damascus. The author identifies the source of the claim as Muhammad Kurd Ali, a respected modern scholar, but argues that no earlier biographer or contemporary of al-Maydani ever mentioned this. He further traces the story back to a book by Shahin Makaryus, a Lebanese Christian writer accused of serving Zionist and Masonic interests. The author questions the reliability of this source and implies that the narrative may be fabricated or exaggerated. The passage follows a logical order: (1) states the accusation, (2) identifies the accuser, (3) argues that earlier sources are silent, (4) points to the likely dubious origin of the claim. This is a classic scholarly refutation based on source criticism and chain of transmission.

Key Terms
الميداني (al-Maydani): Sheikh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, a 19th-century Hanafi faqih, author of al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri.
محمد كرد علي (Muhammad Kurd Ali): A 20th-century Syrian historian and director of the Arabic Language Academy in Damascus, born 1293/1876, died 1372/1953.
حسر اللثام عن نكبات الشام (Hasr al-Litham 'an Nakabat al-Sham): A book by Shahin Makaryus detailing the 1860 Damascus events; the author suggests it is biased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main purpose of this passage?
A) To prove that al-Maydani did indeed help the Christians in 1860
B) To defend al-Maydani's reputation by questioning the reliability of a historical claim
C) To praise Muhammad Kurd Ali's biography of al-Maydani
D) To discuss the fiqh rulings on helping non-Muslims in times of fitna

Key Takeaway
Historical claims about Hanafi scholars should be verified through early sources and critical evaluation of the transmitters.

Biography of Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani and the 1860 Damascus Fitna
Biographical narrative with critical historiography

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the main claims about Shaykh al-Maydani's role in the 1860 Damascus events and evaluate the reliability of the source testimony.

Core Idea
Historical claims about a scholar must be verified against multiple contemporary sources to avoid overstatement.

This passage introduces the biography of Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, a Hanafi scholar, but focuses on a controversy: his alleged role in calming the 1860 sectarian conflict in Damascus. The author contrasts a single source that credits al-Maydani with the absence of his name in detailed daily accounts by other Muslim historians. Understanding this critical approach is essential for properly evaluating a scholar's legacy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the historical event and actors
Locate the 1860 fitna between Christians and Druze in Damascus, and note the key figures mentioned: al-Maydani, Amir Abd al-Qadir, etc.
2
Locate the claim about al-Maydani
Find the specific claim in Makarius's book 'Hashr al-Litham' that lists al-Maydani among those who helped calm the turmoil.
3
Identify the counter-evidence
Recognize that other contemporary historians (Muhammad Pasha, al-Hasibi) recorded daily events but did not mention al-Maydani.
4
Evaluate the weight of evidence
Compare the sources: which is more likely to be reliable? Note the author's conclusion that Makarius is unique.

Source Text

الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني لبنان في الفتن والحروب التي جرت بين النصارى والدروز، وانظر في ترجمته في أعلام الزركلي أسماء كتبه، لترى شيئاً مما ذكروه عنه. وقد عقد مكاريوس في كتابه هذا: «حسر اللثام» فصلاً خاصاً عــن تلك الحادثة، وذَكَر (۱) أن ألوفاً من النصارى قتلوا في هذه الفتنة، وأن ممن ساعد على تهدئة الفتنة الأمير عبد القادر الجزائري عبد الغني الميداني، وعد أسماء آخرين. (۲) والشيخ ... ومما يؤكد تفرد مكاريوس بذكر الميداني في هذه الحادثة، أن من كتب من علماء المسلمين عن هذه الحادثة، ودون أحداثها يومياً بالتفصيل الدقيق لم يذكروا الميداني في أحداثها. 6 فهذا محمد باشا ابن الأمير عبد القادر الجزائري حين كتب عن (١) ص ٢٣٤. (۲) وذكر هذا. عن الأمير عبد القادر أيضاً ابنه محمد في كتابه عن والده: «تحفــة الزائر في مآثر الأمير عبد القادر وأخبار الجزائر ۲ /۹۲ ، وذكر أنه نال بذلك وبغيره أوسمة نادرة كبيرة، ونياشين ضخمة، وثناءات فخمة مفخمة من عدد كبير مـن مـلـوك الدول غير الإسلامية ورؤسائها. كما ذكر محمد ابن الأمير عبد القادر في تحفة الزائر ٩٤/٢ أن صاحب الدولة فؤاد باشا وزير الخارجية للدولة العثمانية، قدم دمشق بعد الحادثة، وأجرى حكومة عرفية خارجة عن القوانين وقبض على الألوف من أهالي دمشق الذين شاركوا في الحادثة، حتى امتلأت بهم السجون، وقتل من قتل منهم، ونفى مـن نفـى، وهكذا، وينظر ما كتبه خليل مردم في أعيان القرن الثالث عشر، في ترجمـة فـؤاد باشا ص ٩٤، وما فَعَل من أفاعيل بأهالي دمشق عقب تلك الحادثة. هذه الحادثة بالتفصيل في كتابه: «تحفــة الزائــر فـي مـآثر الأمـير عبد القادر وأخبار الجزائر ) ، لم يذكر الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني في هذه الحادثة أبداً. وأيضاً ممن أفرد هذه الحادثة بكتاب خاص، ولم يذكر الميداني في أحداثها أبداً، أحد كبار أعيان دمشق وأشرافها ووجهائها، وهو السيد محمد أبو السعود الحسيبي الحسيني، ممن عاصر الحادثة، وكان مع أبيه في خصمها ومعمعتها، المتوفى سنة ١٣٣٢هـ (۲) ووالد أبي السعود الحسيبي هذا، هو أحمـد بـن علـي الحسيبي الحسيني، أحد كبار أشراف دمشق وأعيانها ووجهائها، ممن نفي مع مَن نُفي من علماء دمشق وأعيانها إلى قبرص» لما وقعت فتنة تلـك الحادثة، المتوفى سنة ١٢٩٣هـ (۳). (۱) ۲/ ٩١ - ١١٦ ، هكذا اسم الكتاب كما هو مثبت على غلافه المطبوع، في حين أن البيطار في حلية البشر ۸۹۷/۲ سماه : «الكوكب الزاهر»، والكتاب مطبوع سنة ١٩٠٣م، في المطبعة التجارية بالإسكندرية، في مجلدين، ومنه نسخة في مكتبة الشيخ عبد القادر شلبي في المكتبات الخاصة المودعة في مكتبة الملك عبد العزيز بالمدينة المنورة. (۲) له ترجمة في معجم المؤلفين ،۲۳۱/۹ ، وتاريخ علماء دمشق في القرن الرابع عشر الهجري ۲۹۱/۱ ، ومنتخبات التواريخ لدمشق للحصني ٨٢٨/٢. (۳) له ترجمة في حلية البشر ٢٤١/١ ، وينظر تاريخ علماء دمشق في القرن الرابع عشر الهجري ٢٩/١.
First Chapter: Biography of the illustrious scholar Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. Lebanon in the turmoil and wars that occurred between Christians and Druze. Refer to his biography in al-Zirikli's 'Alam' for the titles of his books to see some of what they mentioned about him. Makarius in this book 'Hashr al-Litham' composed a special chapter about that incident and mentioned (1) that thousands of Christians were killed in this turmoil, and that among those who helped to calm the turmoil were Amir Abd al-Qadir al-Jaza'iri and Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, and he listed other names. (2) And the Shaykh... And what confirms the uniqueness of Makarius in mentioning al-Maydani in this incident is that those Muslim scholars who wrote about this incident and recorded its events daily in precise detail did not mention al-Maydani in its events. 6 Thus Muhammad Pasha, son of Amir Abd al-Qadir al-Jaza'iri, when he wrote about (1) p. 234. (2) This was mentioned... about Amir Abd al-Qadir also by his son Muhammad in his book about his father: 'Tuhfat al-Zair fi Ma'athir al-Amir Abd al-Qadir wa Akhbar al-Jaza'ir' 2/92, and he mentioned that he thereby and otherwise obtained rare large medals, huge decorations, and great lofty praises from many kings of non-Islamic states and their presidents. Similarly, Muhammad, son of Amir Abd al-Qadir, mentioned in Tuhfat al-Zair 2/94 that his excellency Fuad Pasha, Minister of Foreign Affairs of the Ottoman state, came to Damascus after the incident and imposed martial law outside the laws, arrested thousands of the people of Damascus who participated in the incident, until prisons were filled with them, killed some of them, exiled some, and so on. See also what Khalil Mardam wrote in 'Ayan al-Qarn al-Thalith 'Ashar', in his biography of Fuad Pasha p. 94, and what he did to the people of Damascus after that incident. This incident in detail in his book: 'Tuhfat al-Zair fi Ma'athir al-Amir Abd al-Qadir wa Akhbar al-Jaza'ir', he never mentioned Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani in this incident at all. Also among those who devoted a special book to this incident and never mentioned al-Maydani in its events at all is one of the great notables of Damascus, its nobles, and its leaders, namely Sayyid Muhammad Abu al-Sa'ud al-Hasibi al-Husayni, who lived through the incident and was with his father in its thick and its tumult, died in 1332 AH (2). And the father of Abu al-Sa'ud al-Hasibi is Ahmad ibn Ali al-Hasibi al-Husayni, one of the great nobles of Damascus, its notables, and its leaders, among those exiled with those exiled from the scholars of Damascus and its notables to Cyprus when the turmoil of that incident occurred, died in 1293 AH (3). (1) 2/91-116, the name of the book as it appears on its printed cover, while al-Bitar in Hilyat al-Bashar 2/897 called it 'al-Kawkab al-Zahir', and the book was printed in 1903 CE in the commercial press in Alexandria in two volumes, and a copy of it is in the library of Shaykh Abd al-Qadir Shalabi among the private libraries deposited in the King Abdulaziz Library in Medina. (2) His biography is in Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin 9/231, and Tarikh 'Ulama' Dimashq fi al-Qarn al-Rabi' 'Ashar al-Hijri 1/291, and Muntakhabat al-Tawarikh li Dimashq by al-Hisni 2/828. (3) His biography is in Hilyat al-Bashar 1/241, and see Tarikh 'Ulama' Dimashq fi al-Qarn al-Rabi' 'Ashar al-Hijri 1/29.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical excerpt from the introduction of the book, specifically the first chapter titled 'Biography of the Illustrious Scholar Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani.' It does not contain any fiqh rulings but rather historical details about the author's life and his alleged role in the 1860 sectarian conflict in Damascus between Christians and Druze. The author argues that only one source, a book by Makarius, claims al-Maydani helped calm the turmoil, while other contemporary Muslim historians who documented the events daily do not mention him at all. The passage cites the works of Muhammad Pasha (son of Amir Abd al-Qadir) and others to support this claim, implying that al-Maydani's involvement may have been overstated. It also provides additional details about the aftermath of the incident, including the harsh measures taken by Fuad Pasha, the Ottoman minister. As a teacher, I emphasize that this is a purely biographical/historical section, not a legal discussion. The style is typical of a tarjama (biographical entry) that establishes the author's context and addresses controversies about his life. Note the use of footnotes to provide references for the statements.

Key Terms
ترجمة (tarjama): A biographical entry or chapter that narrates the life and works of a person, in this case the author of the book.
فتنة (fitna): A state of turmoil or civil strife, specifically referring to the 1860 sectarian conflict in Damascus between Christians and Druze.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Makarius's 'Hashr al-Litham'
B) Muhammad Pasha's 'Tuhfat al-Zair'
C) al-Zirikli's 'Alam'
D) al-Hasibi's book

Key Takeaway
The involvement of Shaykh al-Maydani in the 1860 fitna is based on a single source, while contemporary daily accounts omit him, highlighting the importance of source criticism in biographical studies.

Al-Maidani's Avoidance of the 1860 Fitna
Historical defense of al-Maidani's non-involvement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the evidence that al-Maidani did not participate in the 1860 fitna and explain its significance for his scholarly reputation.

Core Idea
Al-Maidani's name is absent from detailed accounts of the 1860 fitna, confirming his deliberate avoidance.

This passage is from the biographical preface of the book you are studying. It defends the character of its author, Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani, against claims that he participated in the sectarian violence of 1860 in Damascus. Understanding this historical background reinforces his reliability as a Hanafi scholar. The editor uses two key sources to prove al-Maidani's non-involvement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being refuted
The passage responds to an allegation that al-Maidani was involved in the 1860 fitna. Your first task is to understand what is being denied.
Not all scholars of that era kept aloof; some were deeply embroiled.
2
Examine the first piece of evidence: 'Tuhfat al-Za'ir'
A book detailing the fitna exists, but it never mentions al-Maidani. This absence is significant because the book covers many individuals.
The author of Tuhfat al-Za'ir is not named in this passage, but it is a major work on the subject.
3
Examine the second piece: the book by Muhammad Abu al-Sa'ud
Another notable contemporary wrote a dedicated book on the events, including names of participants and victims. Al-Maidani is absent from this book as well.
Muhammad Abu al-Sa'ud witnessed the fitna personally, making his account highly credible.
4
Recognize the pattern of absence
Two independent, detailed sources fail to mention al-Maidani. This consistent omission strongly suggests he was not part of the events.
The passage contrasts this with the sole claim of Makarios, whose reliability is questioned.
5
Conclude the deliberate avoidance
The editor concludes that al-Maidani chose to remain aloof, seeking safety. This fits his known biography and protects his academic integrity.
We are not meant to doubt Makarios' report entirely, but to see it as outweighed by the evidence.

الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني
هذه الحادثة بالتفصيل في كتابه: «تحفة الزائر في مآثر الأمير عبد القادر وأخبار الجزائر» ، لم يذكر الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني في هذه الحادثة أبداً.
وأيضاً ممن أفرد هذه الحادثة بكتاب خاص، ولم يذكر الميداني في أحداثها أبداً، أحد كبار أعيان دمشق وأشرافها ووجهائها، وهو السيد محمد أبو السعود الحسيبي الحسيني، ممن عاصر الحادثة، وكان مع أبيه في خصمها ومعمعتها، المتوفى سنة ١٣٣٢هـ
ووالد أبي السعود الحسيبي هذا، هو أحمد بن علي الحسيبي الحسيني، أحد كبار أشراف دمشق وأعيانها ووجهائها، ممن نفي مع مَن نُفي من علماء دمشق وأعيانها إلى قبرص» لما وقعت فتنة تلك الحادثة، المتوفى سنة ١٢٩٣هـ.
فهذا محمد أبو السعود بن أحمد ألف كتاباً في هذه الحادثة. وذكر أحداثها بالساعة واليوم والتاريخ ، مع ذكر أسماء من حضر، ومَن قُتل، ومَن...، هذا كله لم يذكر الميداني في ذلك كله. ومع وبهذا يظهر ويتأكد أن الميداني كان معتزلاً هذه الفتنة، مؤثراً عدم الخوض فيها، طالباً السلامة، على ما عُرِف من سيرته، وأنه لم يذكر عن خوضه فيها أحد ممن ترجم له إلا مكاريوس ـ وهـو مـن هـو ـ، و من تابعه والله تعالى أعلم.
Chapter One: Biography of the scholar Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani
This incident is detailed in his book 'Tuhfat al-Za'ir fi Ma'athir al-Amir Abd al-Qadir wa Akhbar al-Jaza'ir'; Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani is never mentioned in this incident.
Also, among those who wrote a specific book about this incident, and never mentioned al-Maidani in its events, is one of the great notables, nobles, and leaders of Damascus: Sayyid Muhammad Abu al-Sa'ud al-Hasibi al-Husayni, who witnessed the incident and was with his father in its midst and turmoil, died in 1332 AH.
And the father of Abu al-Sa'ud al-Hasibi, namely Ahmad ibn Ali al-Hasibi al-Husayni, one of the great nobles, notables, and leaders of Damascus, was among those exiled with the exiled scholars and notables of Damascus to Cyprus when the fitna of that incident occurred, died in 1293 AH.
So this Muhammad Abu al-Sa'ud ibn Ahmad wrote a book about this incident, mentioning its events by hour, day, and date, along with the names of those who attended, those killed, etc. — none of this does al-Maidani mention at all. And with this, it becomes clear and confirmed that al-Maidani kept aloof from this fitna, preferring not to enter into it, seeking safety, as is known from his biography, and that no one who wrote about him mentioned his involvement in it except Makarios — and he is who he is — and those who follow him. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is from the biographical preface of the book, where the editor discusses the life of the author, Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maidani. The focus is on a historical event, likely the Damascus sectarian violence of 1860 (known as 'Fitnat al-Sittin'), and the claim that al-Maidani was involved. The editor provides evidence to refute this claim. He points out that in a book detailing the incident, Tuhfat al-Za'ir by another author, al-Maidani is not mentioned. Furthermore, another notable, Muhammad Abu al-Sa'ud, wrote a specific book on the events with precise details, yet al-Maidani is absent from that account too. The editor emphasizes that those who claim al-Maidani's involvement rely on a single source (Makarios) whose credibility is questionable. The conclusion is that al-Maidani deliberately avoided the fitna, seeking safety, consistent with his known character. This passage serves to defend the scholarly reputation of al-Maidani from false associations.

Key Terms
فتنة (fitna): Refers to the sectarian conflict in Damascus in 1860, specifically called 'Fitnat al-Sittin' (the Fitna of the Sixties).

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) He was exiled to Cyprus.
D) He was killed during the fitna.

Key Takeaway
Al-Maidani's deliberate avoidance of the 1860 fitna is confirmed by his absence from detailed contemporary chronicles, reinforcing his scholarly integrity.

The Adab of a Scholar: al-Maydani's Example
Biographical narrative emphasizing scholarly virtues and avoidance of fitna.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key characteristics of a Hanafi scholar's adab and evaluate the importance of avoiding fitna based on al-Maydani's example.

Core Idea
A true scholar avoids fitna and embodies adab with teachers and all people.

This passage from the introduction to al-Lubab presents Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani as a model of scholarly virtue. It highlights his deliberate withdrawal from a historical fitna (civil strife) and his exceptional adab (good manners) towards his teachers. Understanding these traits is essential for anyone aspiring to the Hanafi scholarly tradition, as they reflect the character expected of a mufti and teacher.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fitna and al-Maydani's stance
Read the opening lines to understand what the Incident of al-Sittin was and how al-Maydani responded. Note that he remained aloof and did not write about it, which was a deliberate choice for safety and integrity.
The author contrasts al-Maydani's silence with another scholar who wrote a detailed account.
2
Recognize the unanimous praise
Move to the fifth section where the author states unanimous praise for al-Maydani. Identify the key virtues mentioned: completeness of adab, beautiful character, piety, asceticism, and turning away from the world.
Notice that the praise comes from his senior teachers and later scholars, establishing his credibility.
3
Focus on adab with teachers as a case study
The passage begins detailing al-Maydani's manners, starting with his treatment of his teachers. Observe that his own teacher, Shaykh Hasan al-Baytar, specifically praised him. This underscores that adab is not just general good behavior but especially directed toward those from whom one learns.
In the Hanafi tradition, adab with teachers is a prerequisite for the transmission of knowledge.

۱ ـ أدبه الجم مع مشايخه :
إن مما امتاز به الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني أنه كانـت لـه أخلـاق عالية، وآداب سامية ومروءة نادرة، وبخاصة مع أساتذته وشيوخه، فقد بلغ في ذلك ذروةً عليا، وقدراً كبيراً، حتى أثنى عليه في ذلك أخص مشايخه، وهو العلامة الشيخ حسن البيطار،
Chapter One: Biography of the Scholar Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani. So this Muhammad Abu al-Sa'ud ibn Ahmad wrote a book about this incident (1). He mentioned its events by hour, day, and date, along with the names of those present, who was killed, and who... All of this al-Maydani did not mention at all. And with this it becomes clear and certain that al-Maydani was aloof from this fitna, preferring not to enter into it, seeking safety, as is known from his biography, and that none of those who wrote about him mentioned his involvement in it except Makarius—and he is who he is—and those who followed him. And Allah knows best. (1) He named it: 'The Incident of al-Sittin'; there is a manuscript copy from the author's draft in the Zahiriyya of Damascus, number (4668), in 31 folios, and Allah facilitated for me to obtain a copy of it. It is printed in the Journal of the American University in Beirut, but I was not able to find that print, despite my earnest effort. The Fifth Section: Virtues of al-Maydani and His Character and Manners. Indeed, there was unanimous praise for Shaykh al-Maydani from his senior teachers and those after them, that he was a collection of virtues and perfections, and that Allah Almighty had bestowed upon him complete good manners, perfect good character, along with piety and god-fearing, righteousness and success, asceticism and turning away from the world and its seekers. The author of Hilyat al-Bashar (2/872) concluded his biography saying: 'His virtues are well-known and famous, his good deeds are beautiful, his beneficial constructions are commendable. People would bring him gifts and seek him for great bequests. In short and in detail: he was a generous man without equal, his influence expanded, his praise among people increased, and his awe permeated hearts, so he was for them a great sought-after goal and desire.' End quote. I will mention below what I have come across of his lofty reports in this regard: 1. His excellent manners with his teachers: Indeed, what distinguished Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani is that he had lofty character, sublime manners, and rare chivalry, especially with his professors and teachers. He reached in that a high pinnacle and great status, even his most senior teacher, the scholar Shaykh Hasan al-Baytar, praised him for that.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account from al-Lubab's introduction, written by the editor, presenting Shaykh 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani's life and character. It begins with a discussion of al-Maydani's avoidance of a historical fitna (civil strife), specifically the 'Incident of al-Sittin' which involved Muhammad Abu al-Sa'ud ibn Ahmad writing a detailed book. Al-Maydani distanced himself entirely, as confirmed by his biographers except for one questionable source (Makarius). The text then transitions to a new section on al-Maydani's virtues, highlighting unanimous praise from his teachers and later scholars. He is described as the epitome of virtues, possessing complete adab (good manners), beautiful character, piety, righteousness, asceticism, and renunciation of worldly pursuits. The author quotes from Hilyat al-Bashar, emphasizing al-Maydani's fame for virtues, charitable works, and his awe-inspiring yet beloved presence. Finally, the passage begins to detail specific examples, starting with his excellent treatment of his teachers, exemplified by Shaykh Hasan al-Baytar's praise. This shows that al-Maydani's excellence was recognized by the highest authorities of his time, forming a strong chain of scholarly transmission.

Key Terms
الأدب (al-adab): Good manners and respectful conduct, especially towards teachers, a defining characteristic of al-Maydani.
المروءة (al-murūʼa): Chivalry, manliness, and noble character, referring to al-Maydani's rare and excellent behavioral traits.
الفتنة (al-fitna): A specific historical event of civil strife, likely the 'Incident of al-Sittin', from which al-Maydani distanced himself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A scholar's character—especially adab and avoidance of fitna—is integral to his authority and the proper transmission of Islamic knowledge.

Life of the Author
beginner

The Virtue of Adab in the Hanafi Tradition: Al-Maidani's Example
Biography highlighting al-Maidani's virtues and respect for teachers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how biographical accounts in Hanafi fiqh texts establish the author's spiritual and scholarly authority, using al-Maidani's adab as a model.

Core Idea
A scholar's adab (refinement) is essential to his authority; al-Maidani's purchase of Ibn Abidin's library exemplifies this.

This passage from the biography of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani is not merely historical filler. In the Hanafi madrasa, the character of a scholar is integral to the transmission of knowledge. Here we see how his conduct towards his teachers, especially his purchase of Ibn Abidin's library, demonstrates the high value placed on adab in our tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of the biographical section
Recognize that this section is meant to establish the author's credibility by highlighting his virtues.
In Hanafi texts, such biographies are not decorative; they underpin the reliability of the fiqh.
2
List the virtues attributed to al-Maidani
Scan the text for specific qualities: adab, good character, piety, asceticism, etc.
Note how the passage emphasizes consensus among his teachers.
3
Focus on the act of birr towards Ibn Abidin
Analyze the story: after Ibn Abidin's death, al-Maidani bought his library to prevent dispersal.
This illustrates practical application of adab and loyalty to teachers.
4
Reflect on how this builds trust in the author
Consider how such a story would reassure readers that al-Maidani is a reliable transmitter of fiqh.
Adab is linked to the integrity of the scholarly chain.

الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني
المبحث الخامس
فضائل الميداني وأخلاقه وآدابه
لقد أجمعت الكلمة على الثناء على الشيخ الميداني، مـن كبـار مشايخه ومن بعدهم ، وأنه كان مَجمَعَ الفضائل والكمالات، وأن الله تعالى قد من عليه بكمال الأدب، وتمام حُسن الخلق، مع ورع وتقوى، وصلاح وفلاح ، وزهد وإعراض عن الدنيا وطلابها . وقد ختم صاحب حلية البشر ٨٧٢/٢ ترجمته بقوله : وفضائله معروفة مشهورة، وخيريات حسنةٌ، وتعميرات مستحسنة، وكانت الناس تأتيه بالهدايا، وتقصده بعظيم الوصايا، وبالجملة والتفصيل: قد كان شهماً ما له من مثيل، وقد اتسع جاهه، وكثر في الناس ثناؤه، وخالطت هيبته القلوب، فكان لها أجل مطلوب ومرغوب». اهـ
وأذكر فيما يلي ما وقفت عليه من أخباره العالية في ذلك :
١ ـ أدبه الجم مع مشايخه :
إن مما امتاز به الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني أنه كانـت لـه أخـلاق عالية، وآداب سامية ومروءة نادرة، وبخاصة مع أساتذته وشيوخه، فقد بلغ في ذلك ذروةً عليا، وقدراً كبيراً، حتى أثنى عليه في ذلك أخص مشايخه، وهو العلامة الشيخ حسن البيطار،
فقال عنه وهو يصفه :
الفصل الأول : ترجمة العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني
... القائم بحقوق أشياخه بالأدب التام، والحائز بنـور رضـاهـم أعلى درجة ومقام»(١). اهـ
وقال عنه شيخه الشيخ عبد الرحمن الكزبري: «ولقد من الله على الميداني فيما عَلِمنا بكمال أدب ، وحُسن خُلُقٍ، وتورع وتقوى، بهـا إن شاء الله تعالى إلى المنازل العليَّة يرقى ، وإنا لنرجو لـه فـوق ذلك مظهراً ... » (٢) . اهـ * ومن الصور العظيمة لأدبه ، وحُسن خُلُقه : ما حفظ عنه من بره بشيخه العلامة ابن عابدين، وذلك أنه بعد وفاة ابن عابدين أراد ورثته بيع مكتبته، ولم يكن لابن عابدين من الورثة الذكور إلا ابنه محمد علاء الدين، وكان صغيراً في الثامنة مـن عمـره، فلـم يـرض الميداني أن تُباع مكتبة شيخه ابن عابدين العظيمة، وأن تُضيع شـذر مذر هنا وهناك، فقام بشرائها، وكان غالبها عنده، والقسم الآخر منها عند تلميذ ابن عابدين الآخر الشيخ محمد ابن الشيخ حسن البيطار. وبذلك البر العظيم حفـظ الميداني مكتبة شيخه من الضياع، وكانت عنده في المحل الأسمى

Chapter One: Biography of the eminent scholar Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani. Fifth Section: The virtues of al-Maidani, his manners and etiquettes. The consensus of opinion has agreed upon praise of Sheikh al-Maidani, from his senior teachers and those after them, that he was a gathering of virtues and perfections, and that Allah Almighty had bestowed upon him complete refinement, perfect good character, with piety and God-consciousness, righteousness and success, asceticism and turning away from the world and its seekers. The author of Hilyat al-Bashar (2/872) concluded his biography saying: 'His virtues are well-known and famous, his good deeds are excellent, his improvements are commendable, people would bring him gifts and seek him for great bequests; in sum and in detail: he was a distinguished man without equal, his status expanded, his praise among people increased, and his awe mixed with hearts, so he was for them the most sought-after and desired.' End quote. I will mention below what I have come across of his lofty reports in that regard: 1. His excellent manners with his teachers: Indeed, what distinguished Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani is that he had high morals, sublime manners, and rare chivalry, especially with his teachers and masters; he reached in that a high pinnacle and great degree, such that his most specific teacher, the eminent scholar Sheikh Hasan al-Bitar, praised him for it, saying describing him: '... the one who fulfills the rights of his teachers with complete refinement, and the one who attains through the light of their pleasure the highest rank and station.' End quote. His teacher Sheikh Abd al-Rahman al-Kuzbari said about him: 'Allah has indeed bestowed upon al-Maidani, as far as we know, with perfect refinement, good character, piety, and God-consciousness; by which, Allah willing, he will ascend to high stations, and we indeed hope for him beyond that a manifestation...' End quote. And among the great examples of his refinement and good character is what is preserved of his kindness towards his teacher the eminent scholar Ibn Abidin, namely that after the death of Ibn Abidin, his heirs wanted to sell his library; Ibn Abidin had no male heirs except his son Muhammad Ala al-Din, who was a young child of eight years. Al-Maidani did not agree that the great library of his teacher Ibn Abidin be sold and scattered here and there, so he proceeded to purchase it, and the majority of it was with him, and the other portion was with the other student of Ibn Abidin, Sheikh Muhammad ibn Sheikh Hasan al-Bitar. By this great kindness, al-Maidani preserved the library of his teacher from loss, and it remained with him in the highest place.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch of Sheikh Abdul Ghani al-Maidani, focusing on his virtues and especially his exemplary conduct towards his teachers. The text opens by stating the universal praise he received from his teachers and contemporaries, emphasizing his perfection in adab (refinement), good character, piety, righteousness, and asceticism. It quotes a summary from Hilyat al-Bashar, highlighting his renown and the people's esteem for him. The author then presents specific testimonies: first, from his teacher Hasan al-Bitar, who praises al-Maidani for fulfilling the rights of his teachers with complete adab and thereby attaining high ranks. Second, from another teacher, Abd al-Rahman al-Kuzbari, who confirms his adab and character, hoping for his elevation. Finally, the passage narrates a concrete act of kindness: after the death of Ibn Abidin, his library was at risk of being sold and dispersed. Al-Maidani, out of respect for his teacher, purchased the library himself, preserving it as a whole. This story illustrates the practical application of his adab and loyalty. The footnote references indicate sources for the quotes and the story. This biographical material serves as introductory front matter, establishing the author's credentials and character for the reader of the fiqh text.

Key Terms
أدب (adab): Refined conduct, manners, and proper behavior, especially towards teachers and elders.
بر (birr): Kindness, piety, and dutifulness, particularly towards one's teacher, as shown by al-Maidani's purchase of Ibn Abidin's library.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What specific action did Sheikh al-Maidani take to show kindness (birr) to his teacher Ibn Abidin?
A) He wrote a commentary on Ibn Abidin's works.
B) He bought Ibn Abidin's library to prevent its dispersal.
C) He taught Ibn Abidin's son for free.
D) He built a mosque in Ibn Abidin's name.

Key Takeaway
Biographical accounts in Hanafi texts ground the authority of fiqh in the character of its transmitter; al-Maidani's adab exemplifies this tradition.
